BENJAMIN BUCKINGHAM AND THE END OF DREAMS

By GREGORY GERSHWIN

New York City, NY

All Rights Reserved

2013

Chapter 1: In Which There Is A Beginning

        A heroic wave crashed into Benjamin Buckingham, throwing him into the large mast on the other end of the ship. He couldn’t hear his shipmates but he could see them moving about as they ventured forward. The stegosaurus steered to the right as fast as he could steer and the tyrannosaurus rex held onto the sail as tightly as he could and the triceratops bailed buckets of water back into the ocean and the brontosaurus stood at the front and yelled how far they were from land. Benjamin’s heart raced as he held tightly to his binoculars. This was definitely turning into his best dream of the year.

        The brontosaurus let out a booming roar.

        “Iceberg!” Benjamin yelled. “Go around it, stegosaurus! Go around!”

        The stegosaurus turned quickly and violently. The tyrannosaurus rex fell into the mountainous waves of the ocean followed by the triceratops, stegosaurus, brontosaurus, and, finally, Benjamin who crashed to the floor.

        Mrs. Buckingham stood at the entrance to Benjamin’s door with her hands on her hips. She looked as if she had seen her nine year-old boy do this hundreds of mornings, because this happened almost every morning.

        “OK, time to wake up,” Mrs. Buckingham said to Benjamin who had fallen to the ground, his pillows and blankets strewn across him.

        “Mom, it was amazing!” Benjamin began as he leaped to his feet. “The dinosaurs and I were only a mile away from destroying Professor Undutois’ lair and then a big storm came in and we had to survive. We steered the ship straight and we were going to make it but then the stegosaurus moved us too quickly. We were so close!”

        Benjamin waved his arms back and forth as he moved throughout his room, almost knocking over the dinosaur posters that lined his walls and the dinosaur figurines that sat upon his dresser.

        “The stegosaurus always seems to ruin it for you.”

        “Yes!” Benjamin said as he stopped in front of his stegosaurus alarm clock. “I don’t know why he can’t just steer like the brontosaurus can steer.”

        “Maybe you should tell the stegosaurus not to overdo it next time he has to steer through the storm.”

        “Or, maybe I could go back to sleep and I’ll give him the instructions now,” Benjamin suggested before he jumped back into bed.

        Mrs. Buckingham gave Benjamin a disapproving look and cleared her throat once, which alerted Benjamin to her serious tone.

        “You have a doctor’s appointment this morning,” she reminded Benjamin. “Get dressed because we’re going to be late.”

        On any other day, Benjamin would not have been excited about going to the doctor’s office. But on that day, Benjamin’s life could change. And, not only could it change. It could change for the better.

        Benjamin paced back and forth in Dr. Ogar Connolley’s examination room while his mother read an old nature magazine that had been read by many other mothers. The pacing was disturbing Mrs. Buckingham, mostly because Benjamin’s nervousness and restlessness was starting to make his mother nervous and restless. He could not help it, though. He needed Dr. Connolley to tell him what he had been hoping to hear all year long. He wanted to know that he is average for his age. Average in height, average in weight, average in seeing, average in not cleaning after himself, average in supernatural powers was all that he wanted. During each of the previous eight doctor’s appointments, Benjamin had been told that he was, sadly, below average.

        The doorknob started to turn and Benjamin released all of his anticipation at once. Mrs. Buckingham also jumped and the nature magazine flew across the room into a picture of an ankle. The door opened slowly for Benjamin, his eyes as wide as his ears were open.

        Benjamin’s mind raced with thoughts as to what it would be like to be average. He did not bother to imagine what it would be like to be above average. That would be a dream even his creative mind could not fathom. Being average would mean that he could finally blend in with everyone else at school. Being average would mean that he could finally act like everyone else his age. Being average would mean he would no longer stick out of the crowd. Being average would make him happy.

        Dr. Connolley's tall, skinny figure entered the room, his grey, wiry hair pointing every direction and his thick glasses almost hiding his tiny eyes. Dr. Connolley took Benjamin’s chart and uttered some “ahh,” “ooo,” “I see,” “interesting,” and other noises that Benjamin could not interpret as either positive or negative. He placed the papers back on the table and crossed his hands in front of Benjamin.

        “You are perfectly healthy, Benjamin,” Dr. Connolley said with a smile more round than his balding head.

        “Well, that’s great to hear, Dr. Connolley,” Mrs. Buckingham said as she stood from her chair to leave.

        “We’ll see you again next year,” Dr. Connolley offered as he patted Benjamin on the head.

        This was not the information Benjamin wanted to hear. He did not want to know if he was healthy. Healthy was not nearly as important to him as knowing how he compared to all of the other children in his class.

        “Am I average?” Benjamin asked earnestly.

        “Oh, Benjamin,” Mrs. Buckingham began. “You’re perfectly healthy so we can get you off to school. We don’t want you to be late for school.

        “Oh, but it should be in the chart,” Benjamin pointed to the papers on the table. “Am I average?”

        And then, Dr. Connolley offered an expression that gave Benjamin the complete answer. Dr. Connolley tightened his lips. This was not a positive expression. Benjamin’s stomach felt weak and he threw his hands into the air before falling onto his back on the ground.

        “He is very healthy,” Dr. Connolley said to Mrs. Buckingham.

        “But, I’m below-average,” Benjamin sulked while on the ground.

        “You’re below-average right now, “Dr. Connolley added. “Next year, you could be above-average. You could grow a lot in a year.”

        Benjamin groaned. He could not wait a year.

        Benjamin continued groaning the entire ride to school. He had planned to tell everyone that he was average. Now, he had to make sure no one knew that he was still below average.

        The news reporter on the radio was going on and on about the story of the day.

        “People everywhere appear to be dreaming less, according to a recent story,” said the news reporter. “Dreams are in decline and are showing no signs of improvement. This is a reflection of our point in history where--”

        “I think you are over exaggerating things a little bit,” Mrs. Buckingham said as she stopped her baby blue car in front of the school’s entrance. “Some people take a little longer than other people to grow. There’s nothing wrong with that. You just have to be a little patient.”

        Benjamin groaned loudly as he swung his dinosaur backpack onto his shoulder.

        “Have a great day at school!” Mrs. Buckingham yelled to Benjamin as he sulked towards the entrance. Every step felt like an eternity, like an unbelievable amount of exertion needed. Benjamin groaned loudly as he strained to open the door that only yesterday could have been opened with ease. One year, he thought to himself. How many more years of being below average would he have to endure.

Mr. Arnold Marchetta stood at the front of the class with a globe in one hand and a blue marker in the other. He was not the best teacher that Benjamin had and he was arguably the worst. Mr. Marchetta was very good at keeping his desk clean and his space organized. He was not, however, very good at keeping his classroom clean or his students organized. While Mr. Marchetta brushed the dust from his tie and shoes, Benjamin’s classmates would throw things back and forth.

“Benjamin!” Mr. Marchetta yelled at the classroom with his shrill, nasal voice. “Did you throw something?”

“No, I didn’t,” Benjamin replied quickly because it was the truth.

“That’s what he always says,” Howard Horne snickered from the back of the room.

“But, I didn’t. I never do.”

“Then who did, Benjamin?” Mr. Marchetta asked.

Benjamin thought about how he could answer this question. If he said that Howard did it, Howard would seek revenge at a later time. And if Mr. Marchetta did not believe Benjamin, he would be in even more trouble. Benjamin did not know how to escape this situation. He gazed into the black dots in the ceiling and wondered if Mr. Marchetta would be picking on him if he was not so small.

“I don’t know,” Benjamin said quietly.

“Well, if you don’t know and no one else seems to know, I’d say that you’re hiding something,” Mr. Marchetta continued. “Is there something like you’d like to share with the class?”

Benjamin thought that Mr. Marchetta was going to tell everyone the results of his doctor’s appointment. No one must know, Benjamin thought.

“Nothing,” Benjamin said. “I don’t have anything.”

“Well in that case, you’re going to sit next to me for the remainder of the day,” Mr. Marchetta continued as Benjamin’s classmates laughed.

This was not the first time that Benjamin had been punished by having to sit next to Mr. Marchetta. Benjamin knew that his teacher was only picking on him because Howard Horne was bigger than everyone else in class, including the teacher. No one wanted to be bullied by Howard, even the teachers.

“Does everyone have their weekly assignment?” Mr. Marchetta asked his classroom of students who looked back at him blankly.

“You didn’t give us an assignment yet,” Benjamin said with his hands supporting his head.

“Oh,” Mr. Marchetta said while looking at the dust on the back of his pants. “You have to journal your dreams for the next week. No one appears to be able to dream anymore, especially here in New York. When you have a dream and you remember it in the morning, write it down in a journal. I’ll ask a few of you to share your dreams with the rest of the class.”

Benjamin was a little excited about this task because he loved dreaming. Or, to be more precise, he loved dreaming about adventures that he and dinosaurs would undertake. This would be the easiest assignment to complete, he thought to himself as he left the classroom at the end of the day. He could fill up his journal in one night.

The school buses were parked next to each other to take the children home. Since Benjamin lived on the other side of the city than the other students, this was a welcome time of the day. Benjamin hurried to bus number forty-two but as he moved forward, he felt a sudden tug at his shoes. Before he could realize what had happened, he felt as it he was flying. He wished he was flying because if he was flying, he would not be falling. Benjamin fell to the sidewalk and scraped his hand. He could hear Howard Horne laughing at him from behind. Howard had tripped Benjamin by attaching a string to two poles.

Benjamin gathered the books that had fallen from his backpack and hurried again to the school bus. The sooner he was in the bus, the sooner he would be away from Howard. But as he stood at the entrance to board, the bus driver took one look at Benjamin’s scraped hand and shook her head.

“You should get a bandage for that,” she said while she chewed gum loudly.

“No, I’m fine,” Benjamin said quickly, careful not to make eye contact with the bus driver. He knew that if he made eye contact, she would continue to ask questions.

“No, I think you should see the school nurse before you get on board,” the driver continued as she closed the door in front of Benjamin.

Howard Horned laughed loudly from another bus. He groaned for what he hoped to be the last time as he marched back into school to see the school nurse. He was fine. He knew that. Dr. Connolley told him he was healthy. A little scrape wouldn’t cause him any harm, he thought.

But, that was not exactly true. Benjamin was becoming more and more upset with how he was being treated at school. As the nurse bandaged his hand, he imagined what it would be like to be twelve inches taller than everyone else at the school. No one would push him. No one would tease him. He would be so intimidating.

“And, you’re all set,” the school nurse said gently.

As Benjamin stood up to leave, he watched the bus drive off without him. He let out one big sigh and then started walking home. It started to rain, of course, a few blocks from home so Benjamin ran the rest of the way. He entered the house and his mother looked shocked.

“Why weren’t you on the bus?”

“Long story,” Benjamin muttered as he walked upstairs.

“We’re eating dinner in a few minutes, Benjamin,” Mrs. Buckingham called after him.

Benjamin went into his room and lay on his back on the bed, staring into the white ceiling above him. Tomorrow, he decided, would be better than today. It had to be.

“Benjamin!” he heard from downstairs.

He ran downstairs to find his father and mother already sitting at the dinner table, in the middle of which sat Benjamin’s favorite food, spaghetti and meatballs. If each day was a game of positives and negatives, spaghetti and meatballs was a big positive.

“We have an announcement to make, Ben,” Mr. Buckingham said. Benjamin always imagined that he was a smaller version of his father and that at any moment, he would find himself to be about the exact same size with the exact same laugh.

“An announcement?” Benjamin asked while plunging his fork into one of the meatballs.

“That’s right, Ben,” his dad continued. “Your mother and I wanted to let you know that you are going to be a big brother!”

His mother and father wore smiles larger than the room. Benjamin, however, dropped his fork with a meatball on it onto his plate. The family dog Jupiter, a golden retriever, barked at attention.

“Ben? What’s wrong?” his dad asked.

“I’m going to be a brother?” Benjamin asked with concern.

“Yes! Isn’t that great?”

“No,” he said. “I mean, can you wait a little bit.”

“Well, it’s not going to be tomorrow. It’ll be a few months.”

“How about years?”

“Oh, no it won’t be years.”

“Don’t you want to be a big brother? You’re going to have someone who is going to look up to you.”

        “You don’t understand,” Benjamin said while staring at the meatballs.

        “What don’t we understand?” Mrs. Buckingham asked.

        “If you have another boy, that means that there are going to be two Buckinghams being picked on at the school.”

        “Benjamin,” his dad started. “We’re going to make sure neither you nor your brother are being picked on at school.”

        “When do I get a brother?”

        “Around six months,” his mom answered with a smile.

        Benjamin took a big bite of a meatball.

        “This isn’t good,” he said. “If I have such a hard time, how will my brother survive?”

Chapter 2: In Which There Is A Nightmare

        Benjamin tossed and turned in bed, unable to get himself into a deep sleep. He went through all of the typical things the he did to prepare himself for a night of dreaming about dinosaurs. He counted the number of figurines in his room. One hundred and forty-seven. He studied the skeletons of his favorite dinosaur, the tyrannosaurus rex. And, he even walked through his dreams from the previous five nights. But, nothing was happening.

        He stood up from the bed and looked at it accusingly. There must be something wrong with it because it would not let him sleep. Benjamin gave the mattress a kick to the side as he would give his computer when it started to make a noise.

        From his backpack, he retrieved that empty dream journal that Mr. Marchetta had given the class to record their dreams for the week. It was the same type of journal that he was given to record the foods he ate during a week, the birds he saw during a week, and the number of times Jupiter jumped into the ground floor family swimming pool from the second floor balcony. Six times. Benjamin was convinced that Mr. Marchetta had billions of these journals in his classroom.

        Benjamin paced back and forth in his bedroom. Still feeling alert, he turned on his computer and set the volume to a low level that he assumed would not wake his parents. He navigated the internet until he found Jurassic Superheroes episodes, a popular television series in which a group of good dinosaurs destroy fat, tall Professor Undutois’ plans to destroy the world. His favorite episode also happened to be the episode that his mother felt was too violent and would not let Benjamin watch again. But since she was asleep and Benjamin wanted to go to sleep, he thought there would be no harm in watching the episode again.

        The dinosaurs were flying in an airplane together when they saw a newsflash that Professor Undutois was going to destroy a large metropolis by blasting it with a gigantic blue laser. One of the dinosaurs knew that it would take at least fifteen minutes until Professor Undutois could start his evil plan. They needed to land the plane immediately and find his location before it was too late.

        Benjamin watched the dinosaurs ride their motorcycles between cars and trucks along a crowded highway, their eyes focused on an evil trailer in the distance. Suddenly, the backdoor of the trailer opened and Professor Undutois threw bowling balls at the dinosaurs. They dodged left and right and Benjamin’s heart, which normally began racing during this scene, stayed very, very steady. He had watched the dinosaurs destroy Professor Undutois’ plans thousands of times and he knew their lines, strategies, and characters as well as he knew himself. As the dinosaurs steered closer to Professor Undutois, Benjamin’s eyelids began to close and his brain took over the story in Benjamin’s dream.

        The dinosaurs rode immediately next to Professor Undutois’ trailer causing the evil villain to brake suddenly and turn sharply off the highway and into the European streets below. Benjamin and the dinosaurs chased after him, Benjamin leading the way on a light green bicycle. He passed old coffee shops with women drinking espresso and dodged pedestrians carrying baguettes and swerved around taxis transporting people on these Parisian streets while keeping his eye on Professor Undutois in the distance. Benjamin knew exactly where his nemesis had stationed his laser; it was positioned at the top of the Eiffel Tower.

        Benjamin stopped chasing after Professor Undutois and instead started racing towards the large metal structure in the middle of Paris. The Eiffel Tower was only a quarter mile away as darkness suddenly overcame the city, sending Benjamin’s heart into a fast pace. Professor Undutois was nearly at the destination and Benjamin thought, for a moment, that he would not be able to stop him from doing harm. As soon as he started to doubt himself, he realized that if he did not stop Professor Undutois, no one would. He took a deep breath and tried to find courage. As thunder and lightning overwhelmed Paris, Benjamin ran to the Eiffel Tower and began to ascend it to the top.

        But then, Professor Undutois came down from Eiffel Tower and ran away as fast as he could, his arms flailing as he screamed loudly. Benjamin stood confused because his dreams never ended this way. Professor Undutois must have another scheme to destroy earth.

        When Benjamin looked to the top of the Eiffel Tower, he realized that was not the case. A gigantic figure stood at the top and bellowed so loudly that Benjamin could feel the growl pulse through his tiny body.

        “Benjamin, it’s time to wake up,” Mrs. Buckingham said as she opened Benjamin’s door on her way downstairs to the kitchen.

        Benjamin woke up and stared at his computer. He felt that something was wrong with how he woke up. He pinched himself and rubbed his eyes over and over to make sure that he was indeed awake.

        In all of his dreams he ever had, there was never an evil villain other than Professor Undutois. Benjamin didn’t know what that other monster was it was not good.

        “Benjamin!” Mrs. Buckingham yelled from the kitchen.

        Benjamin ran downstairs and pondered what had just happened over french toast. Mr. Buckingham was holding the newspaper with a headline DREAMS HAVE DISAPPEARED. He continued to think about the monster at school and wondered if there was something in one of the Jurassic Superheroes episodes that he was misremembering. He knew them completely, though, so it was quite unlikely.

        “On Tuesday, I dreamed that I was at dinner with my parents when my brother spilled lasagna. It was going to fall on our dog but I saved her just in time,” one of Benjamin’s classmates said in front of the class. Each of his classmates was reading from their dream journals and Benjamin was beginning to think that he might be teased if he read about his dreams fighting crimes with dinosaurs.

        “Howard,” Mr. Marchetta read from a list on his desk. “You’re next. Please read your dreams to the class.”

        Howard walked to the front of the class with his journal, smirking at Benjamin along the way. He cleared his throat arrogantly and Benjamin rolled his eyes, wishing Howard would embarrass himself in front of everyone. Instead, Howard started to detail dreams that everyone in the class thought were exciting and thrilling.

        “I was a gladiator Wednesday night and there was a dragon that had invaded our school,” Howard said as he clenched the journal with one hand and pointed to his classmates with the other. “The dragon was here to destroy us. It was going to destroy all of us. It blew fire everywhere and the school started to burn. This wasn’t so bad but I was not going to let the dragon destroy our houses. And, the baseball field. I ran after it and then I destroyed the dragon using my gladiator shield and gladiator sword.”

        The class applauded and Benjamin participated, weakly, so that he did not draw attention to himself.

        “Benjamin, you’re next,” Mr. Marchetta said.

        Benjamin gulped. His dreams were not nearly as courageous and none of the characters in his dreams were people who he knew in real life.

        “Benjamin, come on,” Mr. Marchetta said because Benjamin had not yet moved.

        He walked to the front of the class with his journal in his left hand and a worried state in his mind. And just like he did in his dreams when he was losing confidence, he took one big breath to try to get as much of it back as he could.

        “The other day I dreamed that I was with a group of dinosaurs in Honolulu. The evil villain Professor Undutois was going to start a volcano that would destroy the entire island. I led the dinosaurs up the volcano and found Professor Undutois and his evil machine. I went up to him and said--”

        “That’s an episode!” Howard Horne yelled from the back of the class.

        “Howard, quiet,” Mr. Marchetta interjected.

        “That’s not a dream!” Howard said with a laugh. “That’s the tenth episode of Jurassic Superheroes.”

        The entire class started to laugh as Benjamin’s face turned red. It was an episode of that popular television series but it also happened to be his dream. He didn’t know what to do next so he continued to stare into his journal in hope that time would move much faster than it was. He had lost any confidence that the deep breath had given him.

        “Benjamin, you can continue,” Mr. Marchetta said.

        “I don’t think I should,” Benjamin said nervously.

        “OK,” Mr. Marchetta said. “But, that will mean you still have to complete your assignment. You can’t disguise television episodes as your dreams. If you don’t have a dream, just say that you didn’t have a dream. Don’t lie about it.”

        “I didn’t lie,” Benjamin said quietly.

        “I bet I’ve already seen all of your dreams on television,” Howard said over the laughter of all the other kids in the classroom.

        For dinner, Mr. Buckingham made waffles topped with fruit because it was his favorite meal and because he had decided that the family did not consume enough waffles. Benjamin did not have any complaints but he was distracted by the events of the day.

        “We had to read through our dream journal at school today,” Benjamin began, slowly.

        “That’s great,” Mrs. Buckingham responded as she set the table. “How did it go?”

        “Not good.”

        “Why not?” Mr. Buckingham said as he continued to make waffles.

        “None of my dreams are creative.”

        “Sure they are. You told me all about those dinosaur dreams,” his dad continued. “And, frankly, I don’t know how anyone would think that they weren’t creative.”

        “Well, it’s just that they are from Jurassic Superheroes.”

        “You’re not watching that episode I told you not to watch, are you?” his mother asked as she handed him a napkin.

        “No, but all my dreams star me and I go around with the dinosaurs stopping Professor Undutois.”

        “Those are great dreams!” his dad continued while making more waffles.

        “I think we have enough waffles,” Mrs. Buckingham whispered.

        “Ten more?” he asked quickly. “Did you know that I haven’t had a dream in months. I couldn’t tell you the last dream I’ve had. I’d love to have a dream where I am parading around with dinosaurs solving crimes.”

        “But, all the other kids in school have dreams that different. I want my dreams to be like their dreams.”

        “Different is good. You should be glad you’re different. One day, you might regret that.”

        “I’m thinking about getting rid of my dinosaur posters in my room,” Benjamin said to his parents shock.

        Mr. Buckingham put down the waffle maker and Mrs. Buckingham stopped setting the table. They were surprised with Benjamin. He had not thought about it for very long but he had decided that by getting rid of the dinosaurs in his room, he would have different dreams.

        “How about this,” Mr. Buckingham continued slowly. “You keep all the dinosaur stuff in your room for a month. If you don’t have a creative dream in a month, we’ll redesign your room to something else. Maybe sports? Cars?” Mr. Buckingham paused and looked at Mrs. Buckingham briefly. “Girls?”

        Mrs. Buckingham rolled her eyes at Benjamin’s dad.

        “I think you’ve had a bad day,” she said. “But the great thing about having a bad day is that the next day is always better. Tomorrow will be better than today.”

        “Who wants some waffles?” Mr. Buckingham asked with four enormous plates of waffles and very little fruit.

        The television was playing in the family room and an emergency alert appeared at the bottom of a news television show: WE CAN NO LONGER DREAM....

Chapter 3: In Which There Is A Dinosaur

        That night, Benjamin dreamt that he was meeting the dinosaurs at Prague Castle to discuss Professor Undutois’ plan to destroy the Czech Republic capital by flooding the city. Benjamin had to figure out where his evil nemesis was going to access enough water to execute the plan. Benjamin and the dinosaurs looked down from Prague Castle to the river below.

        There just isn’t enough water there to flood the entire city, Benjamin thought to himself. There was no ocean or lake nearby. If Professor Undutois was going to bring in a vast amount of water, Benjamin would be able to see it from the castle. He rubbed his brow as the stegosaurus, tyrannosaurus rex, and brontosaurus waited to hear the plan. Benjamin was confused because he could not figure out where water could come from.

        And then, he had his answer.

        “Professor Undutois is going to make it rain upon Prague until the city is underwater,” he proclaimed to the seated dinosaurs. “We have to find the machine he built to create rain and stop him before it’s too late.”

        “What does the machine look like?” the tyrannosaurus rex asked.

        “I’m not exactly sure,” Benjamin said. “But, it has to be large enough to produce big clouds.”

        Benjamin noticed that the previously clear blue sky had one small cloud floating in it. He pointed at the cloud and then followed its direction so that he could imagine where it came from.

        “There!” he yelled as he traced the cloud’s origins to the ground. “The machine has to be over there.”

        All of the dinosaurs looked in the direction Benjamin was pointing and agreed that his conclusion made perfect sense. Before their eyes, they watched another cloud appear from the ground. Then, another. And, another. There was no doubt in Benjamin’s mind that Professor Undutois was making rain clouds and that the evil nemesis would continue to do so until Prague was underwater.

        “Let’s get him!” Benjamin shouted to his friends.

        The raced down Prague Castle and through the old city, navigating the roads on bicycles so that they could dodge the trolleys quickly and safely. Benjamin’s heart beat faster as he realized that this beautiful city could be lost if he didn’t stop Professor Undutois. It was a lot of pressure, he thought, but he would do it with the assistance of his friends.

        “I think we should go--” Benjamin started.

        “I’m hungry,” the brontosaurus yelled back.

        “You’re what?”

        “I’m hungry.”

        “How can you be hungry now? Can’t you wait until after we arrest Professor Undutois?”

        “No, I’m pretty hungry,” the brontosaurus named Gary added. “I think I need to eat or I’m not going to be help at all.”

        “Is anyone else hungry like Gary?” Benjamin asked his friends while standing in the middle of Wenceles Square.

        “I could use a nap,” the tyrannosaurus rex named Snark said.

        “A nap!”

        “Well, we’ve been going pretty fast for quite some time. I’m kind of tired.”

        “But we don’t have time!”

        “It won’t be a long nap.”

        “How long will it be?”

        “Twenty minutes?”

        “Twenty minutes!”

        “If I start now, I think it could be fifteen.”

        Gary came back with a gigantic salad and began eating it on a park bench.

        “OK, Snark. Get some sleep,” Benjamin said. “Gerald and I will find a way to get to Professor Undutois faster so that we don’t lose much time.”

        “Actually, I kind of have to...,” Gerald the stegosaurus paused.

        “You have to what?”

        “Use the restroom,” Gerald whispered into Benjamin’s ear.

        “Fine!” Benjamin said as he flung his hands to his side. “Go use the bathroom.”

        Gerald stumbled away from the group, Snark slept on the ground, and Gary ate on the parkbench. Benjamin was sure that he was losing valuable time that should have been spent stopping his evil nemesis. He turned his head to the sky and noticed that there were more than ten clouds in the sky. It was only a matter of time before the sky was covered with them.

        “I don’t think I can wait much longer,” Benjamin said to Gary. “I need to go stop Professor Undutois.”

        “I’ll only be a few more minutes,” Gary said as he chewed on some carrots. “But, I kind of have to use the bathroom as well.”

        “I’m going to go,” Benjamin decided. “When Snark wakes up and Gerald returns, find me where Professor Undutois is creating the clouds.”

        “Sounds good, Ben,” Gary replied while eating broccoli.

        Benjamin did not like the idea of abandoning his friends but he also did not like the idea of Professor Undutois flooding Prague. He thought that he would find the villain and when the dinosaurs were ready, they would not have to waste any time searching. They could simply come to him.

        The sky started to hold more clouds and then, Benjamin felt a raindrop. It was the first raindrop he had felt and so, he was not very nervous. Then, he felt another and then another. Professor Undutois was well underway with his plan and Benjamin needed to stop him quickly. If the rain continued at this pace, there could be a flood very soon.

        Benjamin found an abandoned bicycle and rode it to the cloud machine. He saw the object on the top of a small apartment building. But, he could not see Professor Undutois.

        It was very likely that Professor Undutois had gone to stop them from interfering with his cloud machine. Since Benjamin had left his friends behind, Professor Undutois would not realize that there was nothing to stop Benjamin from turning off the machine. Benjamin inhaled deeply and then began to climb the exterior staircase of the apartment building to the roof.

        Clouds scattered themselves across the sky and the rain began to pour more violently. Benjamin climbed faster and faster, careful not to slip on the metal steps. When he reached the rooftop, he saw the machine and also saw that the buttons to control it were missing. Professor Undutois had them, he thought to himself.

“You’ll never stop me this time, Benjamin,” Professor Undutois yelled from the rooftop across the street.

Benjamin thought quickly about what to do next because he did not believe he could turn off the machine without obtaining the controls that Professor Undutois held. As the rain started to pour more violently, he climbed back down the apartment building and raced across the street. He was about to ascend the staircase when he saw Professor Undutois descending the staircase, heading right for Benjamin. Benjamin took a step back and prepared himself to tackle the evil villain as soon as he was within reach. This would be Benjamin’s most successful win yet.

Oddly, though, Professor Undutois was screaming. He was screaming so loudly that Benjamin realized the villain was not running toward Benjamin but away from something. Professor Undutois landed on the ground, threw the controls for the cloud machine at Benjamin, and then ran down the street with his arms above his head, panicking more and more.

Benjamin looked in the direction from which Professor Undutois came and saw the top of the staircase was beginning to shake. There was no time to lose, though, because Benjamin needed to stop the production of clouds. He looked at the controls that Professor Undutois had thrown at him and decided that it would be simple enough to stop the rain. Benjamin lowered his index finger onto the OFF button when bricks started to fall from the side of the apartment building. Benjamin looked to the roof and saw the most gigantic face of a monster he had ever seen.

It was the same monster.

It screamed at Benjamin more loudly than any noise Benjamin had ever heard previously.

It displayed teeth that were like enormous swords.

It emanated fire from its body as if it was a moving volcano.

And, it moved slowly towards Benjamin.

Benjamin did not know what to do in this situation because he had never encountered such a thing before. If he turned off the rain, he thought, the episode would be over and he will have won. His finger clicked the OFF button on the controls and the clouds stopped appearing and the rain stopped falling and Prague stopped being flooded. But, the monster kept moving toward Benjamin.

It jumped to the street level, destroying the cars and trucks that it landed upon. Benjamin realized that this monster was after him. And, Benjamin could not hide his fear. His legs shaked. His arms felt numb. His muscles felt immobile. His face felt weak.

And then, he felt a painful thud in the side of his body. He looked to the ground and realized that he was moving, but his legs were still and his body was still. Snark had grabbed him and ran faster than Benjamin had ever seen him run before. The monster began to chase and Snark sprinted more quickly away, sprinting down deserted streets and heading for a section of the city that Benjamin had not seen before.

Benjamin panicked and did not enjoy the dream anymore. He felt in danger and he felt that his friends, the dinosaurs, recognized that there was indeed a danger. Benjamin wanted to leave, so he did.

He woke up.

He rubbed his eyes and stretched his arms and remarked how his heart was racing a little bit more than he was comfortable with.

“It’s over,” he thought to himself, disappointed that he did have a successful dream and curious as to why that monster appeared again.

Benjamin threw his legs over the side of the bed and although he was still waking up, he realized that something was wrong. Whenever he looked to his wall, his eyes were inline with the poster of a stegosaurus. But now, his eyes were well above the poster. In fact, his head was only a foot away from the ceiling. Benjamin looked down and realized that he was almost six feet above the ground. And if he was six feet above the ground, there was something underneath his bed.

He jumped to the ground, looked under his bed and screamed. There was a dinosaur who did not look too unlike the dinosaur in Benjamin’s dreams named Snark. The dinosaur looked at Benjamin and screamed in return.

Benjamin screamed.

Snark screamed.

Benjamin panicked.

Snark panicked.

Benjamin tried to run away.

Snark tried to run away.

Benjamin wanted to exit the room but Snark was standing in the path to the door. As Benjamin moved to one side, Snark moved to that same side in an awkward dance of two very scared creatures. And then, Snark grabbed Benjamin by his shoulders.

The only thought that passed through Benjamin mind was that he was going to be eaten at that moment. It was inevitable. Snark was probably hungry and Benjamin was food. But if I’m going to be eaten, Benjamin thought, I’m going to run away and hide. And since he couldn’t move, he fought the only way he knew how to fight; he spat into Snark’s eye.

“Oh, gross!” Snark replied as he dropped Benjamin and rubbed the left side of his face. “Gross!”

The voice sounded a lot less menacing than Benjamin had expected. It sounded like it belonged to a man older than Benjamin but not as old as his dad. It sounded as if it was from someone who was not a kid but not yet an adult. Benjamin stepped backward slowly to the door so that he could escape.

“I’m going to get in so much trouble for this!” Snark said as he sat heavily upon Benjamin’s chest of dinosaur toys, denting the middle quite significantly. Snark waved one of his claws against his face to brush away some dust in his eye. “Come on, Rodney. Pull yourself together. You can do this.” Snark took a deep, long breath. “You can do this!”

“Rodney?” Benjamin asked with curiosity.

Snark turned quickly to Benjamin.

“Listen, Benjamin,” Snark said. “You need to go about your day and when you come back to your room tonight, I’ll be gone. Actually, it would be really, really great if you didn’t tell anyone that I’m here. Can you do that for me? I mean, I’m really, really trying hard to keep this job and I’m really, really close to losing it. I need you to do a big favor for me and not tell anyone that I was here. Otherwise, I’ll lose my job. Is that OK?”

“What’s your job?”

“Oh, I keep talking and I get myself into more trouble,” Snark continued as he shook his head. “I can’t tell you that, Benjamin. I’ve said too much. You just have to promise me that you’re not going to tell anyone that I’m here.”

“That’s kind of hard,” Benjamin responded. “You’ve destroyed my room and you’re making so much noise.”

Snark and Benjamin looked at the room which appeared to have been torn apart by a tornado, the posters and toys strewn everywhere. The bed was almost unusable and there was clothing everywhere. The lamps were knocked over and there were gigantic tyrannosaurus rex footprints everywhere, including the ceiling.

“Benjamin!” Mrs. Buckingham yelled up the stairs. “Stop jumping around up there and come down for breakfast!”

“You need to clean this up,” Benjamin said to Snark.

“I can’t clean it up,” the dinosaur responded to Benjamin.

“You made this mess! You clean it up.”

“But, I can’t.”

“Why not?”

“I’ve got these tiny arms. It’ll take me weeks to clean up and I need to get back to work.”

“Work? What do you do?”

“I told you I can’t tell you.”

“So, you’re an accountant too?”

“Benjamin, I’m sorry I destroyed your room but I have to go and I need you not to tell anyone that I was here.”

“Fine,” Benjamin said with a little anger at the state of his space. “But, you’re going to have to go out through the window.”

“The window!” Snark yelled with surprise.

“If my mom sees a dinosaur was in my room, I’m going to be in even bigger trouble.”

“I’m not going out the window!”

“Why not? Is it the arms again?”

“No, that’s not how I can leave.”

“How are you going to leave?”

“I can’t tell you.”

“You’ve destroyed my room and now you’re going to run around my home. Do you know what the kids at school are going to say about me when they find out a dinosaur came from my room?”

“I know, I know. I’m going to leave quickly but I can’t let you know how I’m going to leave. You just need to step into the hallway for one minute.”

“If you steal any of my toys,” Benjamin began.

“I’m not going to steal any of your toys!”

“Or the posters!”

“I’m not going to steal any of your posters!”

“Just, please, Benjamin, I’m going to get into so much trouble. I’m really late. I need to go!”

“Fine,” Benjamin said as he gave one last frustrated look to Snark for the inconvenience of the morning. He stepped into the hallway and closed the door, but only until there was a tiny sliver through which he could see what Snark was going to do next.

Benjamin watched Snark walk back and forth with his claws on his head, obviously worried about the state of things. He kept looking at his wrist, upon which Benjamin realized was a watch. He had not noticed it earlier. Maybe Snark really was late for something, Benjamin thought. Curiosity was overwhelming him and he wanted to know where he was going next. Dinosaurs did not just walk around the neighborhood trying not to be seen.

Snark took one more glance at his watch and rubbed his claws together. He grabbed the side of the bed and stood it up on its side. Benjamin couldn’t believe what he was watching. Snark was making more of a mess of his room even after promising that he wouldn’t. It would take him months to restore the room, Benjamin thought.

And then, a bright light appeared on the floor that had been previously hidden by the bed. It became larger and larger and brighter and brighter. Snark shielded his eyes and Benjamin did the same. And without saying anything to Benjamin, Snark jumped into the light in the ground as if it was a swimming pool and disappeared.

Benjamin’s mind was overwhelmed with thoughts. Where was Snark going? How long had there been this light under his bed? Where did it go? Who was going to clean up this mess? How mad will his mother be?

He opened the door to his room and stepped to the light, peering as closely to it as he could without falling into it. He couldn’t see anything beyond brightness. And then, the circular light started to get smaller and smaller.

More thoughts entered Benjamin’s mind as he realized that a door to something else was closing. He did not know what was on the other side of the door but he did know that there was a dinosaur who was late for something. And, that dinosaur knew Benjamin’s name. He struggled with what he should do next.

“Benjamin, time for school!” Mrs. Buckingham yelled to him.

“School!” Benjamin echoed to himself.

I don’t want to go to school today, he thought to himself.

And so, he jumped.

Chapter 4: In Which There Is A Lost Child

        Benjamin kept opening and closing his eyelids because he could not believe a space could be a dark as this was. He had never been in a place where he felt so alone and so isolated. It made him very uncomfortable and paralyzed. He didn’t know what was ahead of him, what was behind him, what was beside him, or what was above him. The only thing he knew was that he was somewhere he did not want to be.

        When he followed Snark, he didn’t know what he was doing. But at a minimum, he assumed there would be light and that he would be able to navigate his way around some new space. Instead, Benjamin didn’t want to move, in case one step to his left led him to a five thousand foot fall off a mountain with rocks and trees and other sharp things ready to knock into his little body along the way. He thought that if he took one step forward, he might step onto some old wooden platform that could give way to him falling six thousand feet into an ancient gold mining shaft. He thought that if he took one step backwards, he might step get his foot tangled into a rope that had been placed to catch large animals like dinosaurs and suddenly he would be pulled seven thousand feet into the air, dangling from some magnificent tree. He leaned a little bit the left and then decided that taking a step to the left would be just as bad. If he took a step to the left, as opposed to the right, he might step into the opening of a gigantic volcano eight thousand feet tall, his tiny body flailing and falling into the erupting lava below.

        And he worried that if he jumped, the land on which he currently stood might suddenly disappear, leaving him with nothing but his thoughts. And although he didn’t know it well at the time, his thoughts were what he had at that time. What he didn’t have was control of his thoughts.

        So Benjamin did the safest thing he thought he could do given the circumstances before him: he sat down. He would wait, he decided, until this perpetual darkness disappeared and then he would go about his way. There was no sense in perishing into the abyss without first understanding where he was, he decided.

        As he sat on the ground, he wished that his mind would wander into the many glorious things that might await him when the darkness faded. But instead, he could only image negative things like falling, failing, and perishing. He closed his eyes and took a deep breath, trying to calm himself.

        Something hit him. He felt something brush by his back so quickly that it didn’t hurt or even phase him. Nonetheless, he knew that something was close to him so he twisted his body in place so that he was facing a different direction.

        Something hit him again. This time, he felt it across his left shoulder as if someone had waved her hand across him quickly. Benjamin cowered down lower to the ground.

        Something hit him twice, this time on both the left and right shoulder. Benjamin was still not going to move, because the dangerous elements had not changed, but now he became worried that although he could not see anything, something could see him. Perhaps, he thought, dinosaurs could see in the dark.

More and more, Benjamin felt things hitting him but he did not know what to do.

But then at a distance of about thirty feet away from where he was sitting, a tiny candle light was lit to reveal that there was no volcano, mountain, mine shaft, or dinosaur traps around him. There was flat ground and a light not too far away. As he was hit again, this time on the top of the head, Benjamin jumped to his feet and ran to the candle, hoping that he could use it to illuminate more of what was around him.

He examined the light and saw that it was on top of a wooden pole. Without thinking about who turned the light on, he grabbed the torch and slowly walked forward into the abyss.

He was glad that he had light because he could convince himself that he was just imagining things. But, he was not happy that he had light because he could see shadows everywhere. Shadows of various sizes were moving at high speeds all around him. As soon as he thought he found some empty ground, he saw more shadows.

He needed to move faster, he thought, because whatever was around him could see him, if they could not before. He jogged further and further, not knowing where he was going and not knowing what was happening.

Another light appeared to his left. As if someone was directing him to follow, Benjamin ran to that second light and noticed that it, too, was on a wooden stake. And again, he did not see anyone or anything around that could have turned it on. He saw only shadows.

Benjamin started to look for a candle when the environment around him changed so much that he no longer needed them. Light came from above and illuminated everything, allowing Benjamin to see clearly where he was.

He was standing at the entrance to a large stadium with tens of thousands of people cheering and screaming in the crowds. The audience was looking upon a circular ground covered with sandy dirt that felt hot under the blue sky and unforgiving sun. In the middle of this arena stood a gladiator, with a shield the size of his body and a sword twice as long. He pounded the sword into his shield and screamed back at the crowd. The crowd screams back at the gladiator.

“Today!” the gladiator beckons. “We will no longer be afraid!”

The audience of thousands jumped up and down as the gladiator gestures every direction, including a momentary glance directly at Benjamin. Benjamin did not know where he was but he did not want to be mistaken as something that gladiator was going to battle. So, Benjamin did what he thought he knew how to do best: he hid behind a doorway at the exit that would obscure his presence from anyone in the stadium.

The gladiator ran around the arena holding a gigantic flag three stories high of blue, yellow, and orange colors. The audience loved every moment of it and many people threw flowers upon the ground.

As the gladiator returned to the center of the arena, thunder broke out in the distance. The gladiator looked in the direction of the thunder and raised both his shield and sword into the air. The crowd erupted in excitement.

Thunder clapped again, closer to the arena. The gladiator yelled back and the audience erupted again.

Thunder clapped once more and Benjamin realized it was not thunder at all. It was a monstrous red dragon who breathed fire into the sky.

The gladiator ran through the crowd and grabbed the dragon by its tail, swinging it around and around and around until he threw it to the ground. He ran to its head and wrapped the dragon’s jaw with thick rope, preventing it from doing any harm to the audience who loved every moment of it. Then, the gladiator sat on the dragon’s back and grabbed its wings.

“This is our land!” the gladiator yelled as he directed the dragon to fly where he wanted.

Benjamin’s eyes were wide and his jaw was low. He did not know where he was but if there were dinosaurs, gladiators, and dragons, he decided that he made the correct decision to skip school that day.

As he leaned forward to try to get a better view of the gladiator flying the dragon around the arena, something brushed his shoulders again. But this time, they did not let go and Benjamin realized he was being pulled backwards by something he couldn’t see.

Chapter 5: In Which There Is A Castle

        Last year, Mr. Buckingham asked if Benjamin wanted to come to his office for Take Your Child To Work Day. Having to decide between going to school and not going to school was a rather easy decision for Benjamin who had never been to Mr. Buckingham’s work. He was thrilled to go somewhere else and imagined it to be something of an exciting, thrilling field trip. Benjamin always wanted to know what it was like to be one of the adults.

        But as the day wore on at the accountancy office, Benjamin was more bored than he had ever been in his entire life. This was not the exciting and thrilling day that he had imagined. Instead, it was a lot of accountants sitting in offices behind computers, talking to each other rarely. He could hear the air conditioner buzzing, the fax machine resetting, the printer spinning, and the workers typing. For most of the day, Benjamin sat on a chair thinking that school may have been more exciting.

        Benjamin reflected upon this memory as he sat on a boring office chair in a stale, white hallway, waiting to enter one of the offices. There was no one else in the hallway except for a man older than Benjamin’s dad who sat on the opposite end, hundreds of feet away from Benjamin. The man was tapping his foot and it sounded like time passing slowly in an office building. At least it wasn’t a noisy printer, Benjamin thought to himself.

        “You’re in so much trouble,” the man said without looking at Benjamin.

        Benjamin didn’t respond.

“Excuse me! I’m talking to you,” the man repeated.

        “I just wanted to see where he was going. That’s all,” Benjamin replied back.

        “What’s your name?”

        “Benjamin.”

        “Well, Benjamin, you should know that Pritchett doesn’t like when people are late. You’re probably going to be punished pretty heavily for what you did. But, you already know all of this.”

        “No, I don’t know any of this,” Benjamin staggered. “What’s your name?”

        “Fox,” he said. “Russell Fox. And if I were you, I wouldn’t pretend you don’t know anything. You know that only makes it worse for Pritchett.”

“I don’t understand. What did I just see?”

“Where?”

        “In the arena, I saw a gladiator fighting a dragon.”

        Russell Fox let out a shrill laugh that made Benjamin uncomfortable.

        “Right,” Russell Fox said. “You should ask Pritchett that. You’re the reason we’ve got delays and problems, you know. It doesn’t take much discipline to arrive and be on time.”

        Benjamin watched Russell Fox play with his wristwatch, a watch strikingly similar to the watch that Snark had been wearing. In an instinctual reaction, Benjamin rubbed his wrist where a watch would be.

        “Why aren’t you wearing your watch?” Russell Fox asked with a sinister look.

        “I don’t wear watches,” Benjamin said honestly.

        “Oh, you’re one of those,” Russell Fox responded calmly as he opened up his jacket to reveal nearly a hundred watches lining the interior of his jacket. He inspected all of the moving faces and parts of all of the watches. Slowly, he removed one and tossed it down the hallway to Benjamin, who was not prepared to catch it. “There, now you don’t have an excuse any more.”

        Russell Fox left and Benjamin looked at the watch that he was given. It was a golden watch that was well too large for his wrist. At about the center, it said Ehtahl Time.

        “Benjamin, come in,” a female voice said from behind a wooden door.

        Benjamin stood, put the watch in his pocket, and looked down the long, expansive hallway. There were no pictures and no windows but lots of fluorescent lights. He felt like he had gone to whatever was the opposite of dinosaurs and gladiators.

        “How do you know my name?” Benjamin asked an older woman with grey hair and red glasses perched on the end of her nose.

        “I heard you tell it to Russell outside,” she said.

        Benjamin looked at her desk and noticed that there was a tissue box placed on top of a red painted square on the desk. There was a computer placed on top of a blue painted square, a telephone on top of an orange painted circle, a keyboard on top of a yellow painted rectangle, and so forth. Throughout the entire office, everything was placed on top of a painted shape that indicated where it would be. Nothing was misaligned and everything was organized to an unbelievably exact degree. When Benjamin looked to the floor, he noticed that the chairs also had markers on the wooden floor.

        “Now, have a seat,” she said.

        Benjamin sat down on the chair and felt that he was seated too far away from the desk to be comfortable. So, he nudged the chair forward a tiny bit.

        Pritchett Pollock sighed, stood from her chair, pulled at her dress, and then walked behind Benjamin and pulled the chair back that same tiny bit.

        “What division were you supposed to be reporting to?” Pritchett asked as she stared into her computer.

        “Division?” Benjamin asked. He leaned forward and nudged the chair a little bit.

        Pritchett sighed, stood, walked behind Benjamin, and fixed the chair.

        “Yes, division,” Pritchett said as she looked back into the computer. “Stop wasting my time.”

        “I’m sorry. I don’t know what you mean.”

        “Division. D-I-V-I-S-I-O-N. Fine, what’s your kpi code?”

        “My what?”

        “Benjamin, you’re going to make this much worse for yourself if you don’t start cooperating.”

        Benjamin shuffled in his chair and Pritchett stood up but before she could reset the chair, Benjamin looked to the ground and moved it for her. Pritchett nodded quickly.

        “Fine,” she said. “I’ll do this myself. What is your last name?”

        “Buckingham.”

        Pritchett Pollock’s eyelids covered half of her eyes as she stared deeply in her computer screen. Benjamin imagined that the computer was probably as organized as her desk was. Even the way Pritchett dressed was exact and precise. A vertical line in her top ended at the precise moment when a line in her dress began.

        “I need your real name,” she said with deep frustration.

        “My name is Benjamin Buckingham.”

        “Benjamin, stop playing around with me. Give me your identification card.”

        Finally, Benjamin thought he would be able to identify himself because he happened to have his school identification card in his pocket. He pulled out the orange and blue card with a tiger mascot in the upper left hand corner. He stretched his arm forward and meant to place it on the desk, but he paused for a moment because there was no painted area where he should put it.

        “Just give me it,” Pritchett Pollock said, annoyed for reasons that Benjamin did not understand.

        He also did not understand her reaction. Benjamin noticed that she was breathing much more deeply and that her nostrils had flared. She turned the card away from her face and looked at Benjamin, trying her best to maintain her composure.

        “I need you to wait here for one minute,” Pritchett Pollock said as she hurries for the exit.

        Benjamin heard the sound of her heels hitting the hallway floor and realized that she was running. He thought for a moment about switching the tape dispenser with the cup holder on the desk, to see what her reaction would be. He thought that his mother would be thrilled if he kept his room as organized as Pritchett Pollock kept hers.

A wind moved the white blinds that stretched from the ceiling to the floor and that hid the windows behind them. Benjamin stood from his chair and opened the door to the hallway as slowly as he could. After stretching his head to see that Pritchett Pollock was not within view, he moved quickly to the window and brushed the blinds away.

Before him, he saw a large village of stone buildings, scattered organically against a green mountain. Each building had a chimney and red clay roofing and stone paths to all of the other buildings. People were walking throughout the town, talking to each other, and reading newspapers. The entire scene felt like his neighborhood but the buildings being closer together meant that more people were interacting with each other. It felt warm and welcoming and natural in ways that Benjamin had not seen before. He did not know that such a place could exist.

There were two other pieces of the village that Benjamin noticed were unusual. The first was a large tower in the center that stood hundreds of feet tall and seemed to have thousands of tiny moving parts. The second was that the entire village was surrounded by large granite walls. It was a castle, he realized. He was in a castle.

“Benjamin!” Pritchett Pollock yelled from behind Benjamin. The blinds swung back and forth as Benjamin released them quickly. Pritchett Pollock exhaled quickly as she watched her orderly environment become disordered. “Please, follow me.”

Pritchett Pollock turned around quickly, clutching a clipboard tightly with her arms held close to her body. Benjamin did not hesitate and followed immediately behind her. Her walking pace was much faster than his and she made a much louder noise when her heels hit the ground than his sneakers did.

“Where are we going?” Benjamin asked quickly.

“Not now, Benjamin,” Pritchett Pollock said in a more cordial tone than she had been using earlier.

“I looked outside and I saw huge walls all around. Is this a castle?”

“Yes, something like that.”

“That’s awesome!”

Pritchett Pollock stopped abruptly. Benjamin almost walked right into her leg.

“Benjamin, you need to be quiet while I escort you. You shouldn’t be here. You know that and now, so do I. You’re a real threat to our castle and to your own life,” Pritchett Pollock said quickly while gathering herself. “Now, I’m going to make sure you get back home. Shouldn’t you be in school?”

“Yes,” Benjamin said slowly.

They turned down one hallway to another hallway and then made a turn into another hallway. Each of these long, white tunnels felt stale, empty, and boring. It was exactly like his dad’s accountancy office.

Pritchett Pollock stopped in front of one of the hundred identical doors that they had passed and spun around to face Benjamin.

“Enter this room,” she said. “You’ll find a telephone. When it rings, answer it. Sweet dreams.”

Benjamin walked into the room and Pritchett Pollock closed the door behind him. In the plain, boring office was a wooden desk, a chair, and a black telephone. There wasn’t even a window for him to further explore his neighboring environment. This room was, he decided, the worst room he had ever been in so far. He looked at the telephone and realized that his time of exploration was coming to an end. Surely, he thought, his mother would call at any moment and yell at him for not cleaning up his room. He would never know where the dinosaur went or what castle he was currently visiting. Instead, it would be right back to school and enduring more teasing from Howard Horne.

The telephone rang much more loudly than Benjamin expected, causing him to bounce from the seat.

“Hi, mom,” Benjamin said into the telephone.

“Uh, I’m not your mom,” said a deep masculine voice. Benjamin was glad the person on the other end could not see his face because it was as red as a tomato from the garden. “Benjamin?”

“Yes, this is Benjamin.”

“I need you to sit in the chair. Please tell once you are seated.”

Benjamin sat down again.

“OK, I’m seated.”

“Benjamin, it’s very important that during the next thirty seconds, you do not move. You will notice that things are going to move around you but you cannot move. This is for your own safety. Do you understand?”

“Yes, I understand.”

“OK, Benjamin. As soon as you hang up this phone, wait thirty seconds and then walk through the door.”

“OK.”

“Bye.”

“Bye.”

        There was a long pause.

        “Benjamin?”
        “Yes,” Benjamin said into the phone.

        “Benjamin, I need you to hang up the phone.”

        “Oh, right. Bye,” Benjamin said as he place the receiver back on the telephone.

        As soon as he did, the ceiling moved up two feet and the walls began to separate in all directions. The floor shifted from side to side and Benjamin was moved to the other side of the room. The desk and telephone disappeared and a new floor appeared below him, much more colorful than before. The door that was the exit into the hallway slid into the floor and was replaced with a solid wall. The wall to Benjamin’s right had been replaced completely and a golden door now occupied the center of that space. All of these pieces were finally aligned and Benjamin heard what sounded like air exiting pipes. The room had been completely rearranged and redesigned around him.

        Benjamin stood from the chair and admired the room for being much more interesting than the boring, white office environment he had previously occupied. Walking through the golden door should be easy enough, he decided. And surely, he thought, his mother would be waiting for him with a laundry bag and the vacuum cleaner. He was fearful at how upset she would be after having seen the destruction that a dinosaur can cause in a bedroom.

        Benjamin took one step forward and the door got a little bit smaller but not so noticeable. He took another step forward and the door got much smaller. He kept walking directly to the door and as he approached it, the door was no larger than his foot. There was no way that he could exit through this door, he thought. It was impossible. He would have to be eight inches tall to exit.

        The telephone had disappeared and he did not have any way of communicating that although he was below-average, he was large enough to fit through a normal door. Benjamin walked to the opposite wall where the exit to the hallway was and could not find any seams in the wall. He turned around, and upon doing so, saw that the golden door was full-size again.

        He walked toward the door and it continued to shrink in size.

        He then took a step backward and recognized what was happening. As he walked backwards, the door got larger. As he walked forward, the door got smaller.

        So, Benjamin did what he thought any normal child would do. He turned around and walked backwards through the door.

Chapter 6: In Which There Is A King

        Benjamin stood in a grand hall that had portraits of men and women lining the walls with candles hanging from the ceiling on chandeliers and with tiny statues scattered across the floor. A deep blue carpet with bits or orange and yellow spanned the length of the space, below arches in the air. The grand hall made Benjamin feel like he was among something great, something much older than him, something that had earned respect and a place in history. It was much different than his classroom and neighborhood, Benjamin felt like he was among unearthly people.

        At the far end of the room, standing upon a yellow star was a large man who looked like both a wizard and a professor.

        “Welcome!” King Bernard Zwirn yelled to Benjamin. “No one in the castle is capable of walking. Where are you from? You’re definitely not from this castle because you were able to walk backwards through our golden door. I’m glad it worked, actually, because we’ve had some major problems with that room in the past. The number of people we lost! Oh, the humanity! It’s something, though, right?”

        “You mean you can’t walk backwards?” Benjamin asked the heavy, old man with a curving chin. He wore a flowing blue velvet robe.

        “That’s correct. You’ve got a flaw in your design.”

        “I have a flaw?”

        “Why sure! Do you have eyes in the back of your head?”

        “No.”

        “Then, you shouldn’t be able to walk backwards.”

        “No one here can walk backwards?”

        “Everyone here walks forward, like people who do not have flaws do.”

        “And, where am I?” Benjamin asked.

        “You, Benjamin, are in Ehtahl Castle and I am King Bernard Zwirn.”

        Benjamin felt no more aware of his surroundings than he did when he arrived. The king stretched his arms wide and Benjamin realized that although this moment meant nothing to him, it meant a lot to the king.

        “You are the first visitor we’ve ever had from the outside,” Bernard Zwirn continued.

        “Outside?”

        “Yes! No one from your hometown has ever been here. We take great pride in our secrecy and our secret location. It’s a wonder you found us at all. But now that you’re here, I’d like to offer you a key to the castle.”

        Bernard Zwirn turned from Benjamin and ran down the hall like a rhinoceros running through a beautiful, pristine setting. The pictures shook, the candles bounced, and Benjamin thought for a moment that the king was not as graceful as he was portraying himself to be. Bernard Zwirn rummaged through dozens of suitcases at the end of the hall, throwing clothes and boxes and other ancient artifacts behind him as he desperately searched for the key.

        “It’s in here somewhere!” he yelled to Benjamin as he turned a large trunk upside down and sorted through its contents.

        Benjamin knew his mother would not be happy with the manner in which Bernard Zwirn was searching. The previously beautiful grand hall was becoming a messy large room. Bernard Zwirn walked to Benjamin like a defeated creature who returned empty handed following a long search.

        “Here,” Bernard Zwirn said as he passed a small box to Benjamin. “You have a key to my castle.”

        The tiny silver box with a gold ribbon looked as extraordinary as anything else around him. Benjamin unwrapped it quickly, tossing the paper to the ground, and opened the lid.

        “It’s a grasshopper!

        “A what?”

        “It’s a grasshopper. Look,” Benjamin said as he offered the box back to Bernard Zwirn.

        Bernard Zwirn looked inside and there was indeed a grasshopper living in the box.

        “The grasshopper ate the key!” Bernard Zwirn yelled accusingly.

        “I don’t think a grasshopper can eat at key,” Benjamin responded.

        “There was a key in here and now there is a grasshopper. That can only mean that the grasshopper ate the key,” Bernard Zwirn said as he scolded the grasshopper. “There can be no other explanation!”

        “Was the key smaller than the grasshopper?” Benjamin asked.

        “It was a huge key. It was much larger than this grasshopper.”

        “Then, there’s no way the grasshopper can eat the key.”

        “How do you know so much about grasshoppers?”

        “We have a lot of them in my backyard.”

        “You have grasshoppers in Ehtsetra?”

        “Ehtsetra?” Benjamin asked with a puzzled face.

        Bernard Zwirn looked at the grasshopper and then leaned in to Benjamin, his face contorted in confusion. He looked around the room quickly, as if he was unsure if anyone was watching him.

        “Benjamin, Pritchett told me you were a visitor.”

        “I am a visitor.”

        “From Ehtsetra?”

        “No.”

        “No?”

        “No.”

        “And if you are not from Ehtsetra, where may I ask are you from?”

        “New York.”

        “I see,” Bernard Zwirn said as he stepped away very slowly with incredibly long strides. Benjamin could sense that the grasshopper was nervous because it had stopped gnawing on the side of the box. Bernard Zwirn looked at Benjamin from the corner of his eye, continuing to move further and further away. “If you’ll excuse me, I have to--.”

        And with that, Bernard Zwirn sprinted away with his arms waving over his head, his feet slipping on the blue carpet. Benjamin never heard an adult scream as loudly as Bernard Zwirn did as he ran away. The faces in the paintings appeared to squirm with discomfort over the dreadful noise.

        Benjamin sighed. This wasn’t the first time someone ran away after learning where he was from. No one seemed excited to see him but it wasn’t for lack of acting politely. If he was not being nice, he would expect people to run away from him screaming. But given the circumstances, Benjamin did not understand what he was doing wrong.

        If they don’t want to be friends with me, he thought to himself, I’ll just explore on my own.

        There were more paintings of people on the walls than Benjamin could count. There was Sir Laborious Maximus who looked like an Italian painter with an absurdly long mustache. There was Queen Jebra Coolihan whose head was four times larger than the rest of her body. There was a dog named Woolfred Woofery who looked more brave than all of the other people in the paintings. And then there was a tiny plaque for Aloysius Trenhaile but there was no painting. Instead, the words We don’t talk about it were inscribed in the wall above his name. Benjamin found this intriguing but did not have further time to contemplate the difference in paintings because Bernard Zwirn reappeared.

        With Bernard Zwirn came a security guard who was as short as he was wide. He looked like a cube with tiny little feet and short red hair.

        “Noel, get the monster!” Bernard Zwirn yelled. Benjamin realized that Bernard was referring to him, that he was the monster.

        Noel charged at Benjamin as if he was designed for this specific task. Benjamin did not move because he was not a monster and he also did not see Noel as a threat. The square man stood only three feet tall. But that did not deter Bernard Zwirn’s chants of encouragement. The king was convinced that Benjamin was a monster.

        “I am not a monster,” Benjamin yelled back.

        “That’s something a monster would say!” Noel said as he leaped into the air and dove headfirst at Benjamin. Benjamin took one step to his left and Noel hit the carpet like a dice being tossed across the ground.

        “We do not welcome your kind here,” Bernard Zwirn said.

        “My kind?” Benjamin asked with confusion.

        “Yes, dream makers do not interact with nightmares!” Noel screamed as he dove at Benjamin again, and again hit the ground like a square bowling ball would.

        “I’m not a monster or a nightmare!” Benjamin responded. He was becoming more agitated that no one was believing him.

        “That’s exactly what a nightmare would say,” Bernard Zwirn said in response. “Come on, Noel. Get him this time. Really concentrate hard.”

        “He keeps moving,” Noel said as he gasped for air.

        “Then wait until he stops moving,” Bernard Zwirn said to Noel.

        “But what if he moves again?”

        “Then, wait some more.”

        “I can hear you,” Benjamin said from the opposite side of the room with his hands on his hips.

        “Don’t listen to us, monster,” Bernard Zwirn replied.

        Benjamin thought hard about how he could escape this situation. If he ran away, he did not know where he would run and Bernard Zwirn would further believe that he was a monster. He could not confess to being a monster because Noel would inevitably try to hurt him. He decided that the only way to remedy this predicament would be to convince these two men that he was not a monster.

        “What do monsters do?” Benjamin asked.

        “Monsters cause nightmares. They terrorize people. You should know,” Noel said. “You are a monster!”

        “But, you’re terrorizing me,” Benjamin replied. “So, you two must be the monsters.”

        Bernard Zwirn stood tall and shifted his head slightly as he looked upon the young child.

        “We aren’t the monsters,” Bernard Zwirn said. “We aren’t terrorizing you.”

        “You are most definitely terrorizing me.”

        “You are terrorizing us.”

        “I was not! I was admiring these paintings and then that block monster tried to tackle me.”

        “That block’s name is Noel Jaffin,” Noel responded.

        “If monsters are creatures that terrorize other creatures, you are the monsters. I am not,” Benjamin said.

        Benjamin watched Bernard Zwirn’s expression change from cold and angry to warm and gentle. He began to breath more easily as he realized that he may have somehow convinced them.

        “Tell me, Benjamin,” Bernard Zwirn said with his hands on his hips. “Where is this New York you speak of?”

Chapter 7: In Which There Are Automatons

        Benjamin followed Bernard Zwirn and Noel Jaffin to the end of the room to another golden door similar in design to the door that led him to this room in the first place. Instinctively, Benjamin turned his back to the door and started to walk towards it. As he made his way backwards, he paused as he saw Bernard Zwirn waving his hands in a flabbergasted state. Noel Jaffin touched his brow and shook his head.

        “Oh,” Benjamin said. “I forgot you can’t walk backwards. So, how do you walk through doors?”

        “We walk through doors like normal human beings,” Bernard Zwirn answered as he turned the knob and stepped through.

        “But, I can walk through doors backwards--” Benjamin began before he was interrupted.

        “Yes, I initially thought you were from Ehtsetra but, alas, you are not. You are from New York.”

        “Right,” Benjamin said as he admired the green floor and yellow walls of a new hallway lined with windows on his left and plants on his right. He smelled flowers that reminded him of chocolates his parents would buy him in April. “So, where is Ehtsetra?”

        “People in Ehtsetra can walk backwards but we don’t know exactly where they are located. And, we want it that way.”

        “Don’t you like them?”

        “Oh, no. We really like people from Ehtsetra but it’s for our mutual protection that we don’t know where the other is.”

        “Protection?”

        “Benjamin,” Bernard Zwirn said as they walked through another door to a hallway with white ceilings and blue walls with fish tanks on his left and stained glass windows on his right. The tropical fish swimming throughout the enormous fish tank looked as if they were attempting to mirror the colorful glass display on their opposite side. “I need you to answer some questions from my advisors so that we can figure out how we can get you home.”

        Benjamin slowed his walking a little bit because he did not want to go home and the thought of doing so was almost paralyzing. He had just arrived and did not want to leave without knowing where the dinosaur went. There was more to see here than there was at school, he thought.

        “Benjamin?” Bernard Zwirn said when he realized that Benjamin was not moving forward.

        The three continued walking at a relaxed pace as Benjamin began to dread the possibility of returning so quickly back home.

        “Why did it say we don’t talk about it above Aloysius Trenhaile’s name?” Benjamin asked.

        “Oh, that’s an easy question,” Bernard Zwirn answered. “Because we do not talk about it.”

        “But who is Aloysius?”

        “We don’t talk about it.”

        “At all?”

        “At all.”

        “Does he live here?”

        “We don’t talk about it.”

        “And people don’t like him?”

        “We don’t talk about it.”

        “Or he did something really bad?”

        “We don’t talk about it.”

        “I have to find someone who can talk about it so that I know why we don’t talk about it.”

        Bernard Zwirn stopped walking and closed his eyes in a manner that Benjamin had seen his mother do when Benjamin had misbehaved. Noel Jaffin did not make eye contact with Bernard Zwirn and Benjamin sensed that the stocky man was uncomfortable.

        “Benjamin, we do not talk about it!” Bernard Zwirn snapped. “You cannot talk about something we do not talk about!”

        They proceeded to walk forward and Benjamin did not ask any more questions. And although he was even more curious about Aloysius Trenhaile, he did not want to be accused of being a monster again. Living with curiosity was better than not being liked, Benjamin decided.

        As yet another door opened to yet another colorful room, Benjamin was blinded by a bright light that escaped so quickly. The circular room looked like the inside of a round monument, the walls made of marble and the ceiling holding a mural with clouds that appeared to move. It was not a large room and Benjamin felt that Noel Jaffin was occupying an unfair amount of it because of his size. And that may have been his only thoughts about the room had there not been one more unusual and unique feature; he was surrounded by twelve automatons, machines that looked like people seated at desks as if they were in a meeting.
