        “Nothing is orange?” Benjamin asked as he thought about that situation for a moment.

        “Nothing is orange,” Pritchett Pollock said as she placed her hand on another door knob.

        Benjamin walked inside the next production studio and saw a ski slope higher than any building he had ever seen before. At the very top stood a skier whose smile stretched wider than her face. All around her, people in orange suits carried lighting instruments and speakers as the woman bounced back and forth. Before she leaped down the slope, Benjamin thought that she saw him, that they had exchanged glances for one moment. But before he could think any further, she moved down that hill as fast as that speed boat had moved through that river. Snow splattered and sprayed in all directions as she raced between trees, jumped over large rocks, and did flips in the air over bored brown bears. Benjamin could hear the calmness of the wind as well as the sound of her skis carving into the snow.

        Pritchett Pollock grabbed Benjamin by the shoulder and took him into another production studio.

        Here, Benjamin awed at the propeller airplane dodging cloud after cloud that people in orange vests had sent into the air from their machines on the ground. The old grandmother inside the plane laughed as she maneuvered it from side to side and then into a full loop. Benjamin noticed his smile was widening as wide as the people who were experiencing these dreams. He was watching adventure. In each of these production studios, adventures were being created in the form of a dream. Everything before him was created by machines and people. The clouds, the blue sky, the trees on the ground, the birds flying past the airplane, and the sun in the corner of the room. He could not believe people could possibly make something like this. It was, in his mind, unbelievable.

        Pritchett Pollocked grabbed him by the shoulder again and they returned into the hallway.

        “Which one is next?” Benjamin asked with excitement as he jumped from side to side.

        Pritchett Pollock pulled at her clothing until it looked perfect and then addressed Benjamin directly.

        “I have ten minutes to get to the control center so we need to get moving,” she said. “I have to work and you will be sitting next to me while I work.”

        Obviously, Benjamin was not excited about having to work, especially with someone who worked like Pritchett Pollock worked. It was more unbearable than when he had to spend time in his mother’s law firm’s office. He wondered if there was any other place he could be and still be safe.

        “Could I hang out in one of the production studios?” he asked with eager anticipation.

        “Absolutely not,” Pritchett Pollock said as she continued to march forward.

        “Could I hang out with the people who make the clouds?” he asked again while also thinking about his next proposal in anticipation that Pritchett Pollock would not approve.

        “Absolutely not,” Pritchett Pollock responded quickly as she marched faster and faster.

        “Can I see more dreams?”

        “Yes,” Pritchett Pollock said. “You will be seated next to me.”

        At that moment, Benjamin realized he did not quite know what Pritchett Pollock did. He assumed that by her office she typed on her computer to other people who typed on their computers. And, that was presumably what they did all day long. He did not think that she did something outside of that office.

        “What do you do here?” Benjamin asked with a pause between each word.

        “I am the director,” Pritchett Pollock responded as she moved her legs even faster. “I direct dreams.”

        “You’re a director?”

        “Yes,” she said. “And, the people who dream are my audience. We’re taking a shortcut.”

        Pritchett Pollock pulled Benjamin through another white doorway and into a room with a large orange screen and people standing in front of it. They passed through the orange room and into a make-up room that looked like it had enough paint to cover all the houses in his neighborhood. They then ran through a prop room that had baseball bats and soccer balls and race cars and guitars and cooking gear and televisions and lots of deer and costumes and elephants and tigers and bunnies and anything else Benjamin could think existed. He marvelled over everything as they ran through another door and up a spiral staircase until they had reached a point where Benjamin could see everything in Castle Ehtahl below him.

        “This is the control tower,” Pritchett Pollock said as she opened a door into a room with more television and computer screens than Benjamin had ever seen in his life. “It’s almost nine o’clock in New York.”

        Benjamin looked at his watched and confirmed that she was correct. It was, also, his bedtime at home.

        “Ready everyone?” Pritchett Pollock said to a room full of men and women seated before computers. “We’re going live in five, four, three, two.”

        Benjamin realized he should be at home and that one of these screens should have contained his dream. Instead, he was on the other side. He was beginning to see where dreams come from.

        “One,” Pritchett Pollock said and all of the computer screens blinked at once.

Chapter 14: In Which There Is An Attack

        Benjamin’s eyes scanned across the thousands of television screens before him. There were as many production studios as Pritchett Pollock had said there were. She wasn’t lying. And from the control tower, he could see into every one of them.

        Seeing all these dreams made him realize some things about himself. Whenever he went to sleep, he did not think that there would be hundreds of thousands of other people dreaming at the same time. But here, it was impossible to ignore because he was seeing all of the dreams simultaneously. It made him wonder if he was only thinking about himself sometimes, because he forgot that he lived in a world with so many other people.

        He also realized that some people just do not have as complicated or adventurous a dream as other people do. There was a screen in front of him with a man standing on a bridge looking down upon waterlilies. There were no explosions or high speed chases or dangerous situations. It was just waterlilies and a bridge. And to the right of this screen, there was a woman looking at an owl, watermelon, pineapple, and coconut on a yellow table. Further along, there was a young child looking at a man on all fours carrying a gigantic basket of flowers on his back, that was strapped to him with a yellow cloth and supported by a larger woman. Benjamin realized that he expected dreams to be adventurous. He did not realize that dreams don’t necessarily have to be what he called adventurous. He also did not quite know what to make of it because he found that he loved the more adventurous dreams.

        There were car chases.

        And base jumping.

        And throwing fire.

        And chasing animals.

        And flying.

        And dinosaurs.

        Snark! Benjamin saw his friend in screen eighteen thousand, one hundred and four. It was him, he saw as he walked closer and closer. That was definitely Snark.

        “That’s him!” Benjamin yelled to Pritchett Pollock.

        Pritchett Pollock was standing in the middle of all of the people who worked for her. She was shouting orders for them to change certain screens or to adjust lighting in different ways or to increase the volume on certain sounds or to encourage more creativity in some dreams while telling actors in other dreams to cool it down. She pointed every which direction and simultaneously seemed to be talking to more people than Benjamin had ever known in his entire life. She yelled commands with such confidence and poise that she did not seem to sweat at all. Benjamin knew that if he was in charge, his heart would race and his mind would be overwhelmed with thoughts. For Pritchett Pollock, however, she behaved exactly as she behaved in her office. It was as if she had done this thousands of times, which she had.

        “Not now, Benjamin,” Pritchett Pollock said as she quickly turned to Benjamin.

        “But that’s him!” Benjamin said without concern for what Pritchett Pollock was doing. “That’s Snark! That’s the dinosaur from my dream, the one who took me here, the one I saw in the plaza.”

        Pritchett Pollock covered her microphone with her hand and leaned her head towards Benjamin ever so slightly. With a pause, everyone in the room turned silent.

        “Who?” Pritchett Pollock said, her lips pursed as if to imitate an owl.

        “The dinosaur from my dreams. Right there!” Benjamin shouted as he pointed to Snark in one of the television screens.

        “Expand one eight one zero four, please,” Pritchett Pollock said calmly.

The small screen where Benjamin had seen Snark expanding to fill nearly a quarter of the entire room. It was definitely him, Benjamin thought. He looked at Pritchett Pollock and she did not share the same enthusiasm.

“Why is Rodney Cohen working?” Pritchett Pollock said into a microphone.

Benjamin did not know who she was speaking to but he could hear the brief sounds of someone responding back to her.

“I told him that he was banned from working until he passes the safety and health test again,” Pritchett Pollock said sternly into the microphone.

Rodney Cohen continued to be a name that Benjamin heard. He must be, Benjamin thought, the name Snark was referred to in Castle Ehtahl.

“I don’t care,” Pritchett Pollock said. “Do I have to come down there and handle this on my own?”

Benjamin could see that Pritchett Pollock was aggravated. Snark had obviously done something wrong but if it meant that Benjamin could finally meet him, it would be worth being stuck in Castle Ehtahl after all. Pritchett Pollock turned off her microphone with disgust and waved her hand in front of her eyes. Everyone who had previously been silent started issuing commands and orders to each other. Dreams continued to display over thousands of screens everywhere. Pritchett Pollock walked slowly to Benjamin and bent over to whisper in his ear.

“I need to go talk to that dinosaur,” she said slowly and tensely. Benjamin knew that Snark was in trouble but he did not know why. “You have to stay here and I’ll be back in ten minutes. You can watch me on that screen and everyone here knows to keep an eye on you. So, will you be fine alone here for ten minutes?”

“Sure,” Benjamin said, a little bit too eagerly.

“Great,” Pritchett Pollock said without enthusiasm. “I’ll be right back after I speak with the dinosaur.”

        “Can I come along?” Benjamin asked with earnest.

        “Absolutely not,” Pritchett Pollock said as she brushed the dust from her clothing and put on her jacket. “I’ll be right back.”

        It was more exciting being in this room than being in her office, Benjamin decided. Although he did not know exactly what was happening, the dreams alone were so interesting that they appeared to make his imagination grow more vivid. He walked around in front of the screens and the people working at computers sometimes made noises that he was in their way. He would walk to the right and look at the screens but then someone would complain that he was blocking their view. So, he would walk to the left and look at the screens but then someone else would complain that he was blocking their view.

        “Where can I stand where I won’t be in the way?” Benjamin shouted to the hundred or so people working frantically on their computers and telephones.

        “Over there!” someone shouted from the back.

        “Over where?” Benjamin answered with his hands at his side.

        “Near the broom closet on the right,” the same voice shouted back among all the other shouts.

        So, Benjamin decided to walk to the broom closet which was just next to the last column of screens. If this meant he would not be in the way, he would gladly stand next to some brooms. Pritchett Pollock would be back soon enough, Benjamin thought, and he could not wait to ask her many questions about Snark. He wanted to know everything.

        A hand gently rested on Benjamin’s left shoulder and he was thrilled to realize that Pritchett Pollock was back. His first question, he decided, was to ask where the dinosaurs lived. But when Benjamin turned around, he saw quickly that the hand did not belong to Pritchett Pollock. It belonged to Russell Fox. And standing behind Russell Fox was Thalia Nachamie, wearing all black and nearly invisible when standing in front of the dark broom closet.

        “Hi, Benjamin,” Thalia Nachamie said in a menacing voice.

        Benjamin turned to run toward all of the workers but Russell Fox grabbed his shoulder and made a sign with his finger that Benjamin had better be quiet.

        “Don’t run, Benjamin,” Thalia said in a long drawn out voice. “I’m here to watch the dreams. Do any of them interest you?”

        Benjamin did not want to speak with this man. He wanted Pritchett Pollock to return as soon as possible. He strained his neck to look at screen one eight one zero four but he was too far away now to see where she was.

        “Benjamin, I only have a question or two for you,” Thalia said. “What kind of child leaves their home to go to someplace unknown? Did you not know what you were getting yourself into? Did you not know what would be on the other side? Tell me, Benjamin, why are you here?”

        Benjamin paused and looked back and forth throughout the workers for someone who could help him. No one seemed to be looking in his direction. They were all preoccupied with the dreams on the screens.

        “Silent, aren’t we?” Russell Fox said. And at that moment, Benjamin realized that it was the same voice that had told him to go to the broom closet.

        “I’d like you to leave me alone,” Benjamin said sternly. He was scared because he was defenseless against two people who made him feel very uncomfortable.

        “I’ll leave you alone, Benjamin,” Thalia Nachamie said. “But if you don’t have a good reason for why you came here, I’m left to assume that you came here for something. And, you’re not willing to tell me what that something is.”

        “I came here for adventure,” Benjamin said quickly as he tried to wrestle his arm away from Russell Fox.

        “Adventure?” Thalia Nachamie echoed with a laugh. “Why of course. You’ll find adventure here. But you’re after something more, aren’t you?”

        Benjamin got one hand loose and started to move away but Thalia grabbed his neck with a strength that Benjamin had never felt before.

        “Now, now,” Thalia Nachamie said. “I’m just going to warn you once, Benjamin. There is no room for someone like you here. We don’t take kindly to people who want to change the way we do things around here.”

        “I’m not trying to change anything!” Benjamin yelled. “I just want to go home!”

        “You’ll go home soon enough,” Thalia Nachamie said as he released Benjamin to the ground. “But do realize, I have my eye on you and I don’t take kindly to people who aren’t honest with me. You had better stay out of my business, Benjamin.”

        Thalia Nachamie and Russell Fox stared angrily at Benjamin as they walked into the broom closet and disappeared. Benjamin could still feel the tight grip from Thalia Nachamie and more than ever before, he wanted to go home. He was now aware of the danger that Miss Lindenmeyer said might come upon him. And, he needed to either run away or hide.

        “Benjamin,” Pritchett Pollock said as she reentered the room. “Please don’t put your fingers on the television screens. Fingerprints are just about impossible to remove and it takes us hours to clean each screen.”

        She did not even realize that he had been through an ordeal, Benjamin thought. He ran up to her as she continued to shout orders and commands to everyone before her and on the screens.

        “Pritchett,” Benjamin said as he tugged at her pant leg.

        “Benjamin, not now,” she responded.

        “But, I’m danger,” he whispered. “I need to talk to you right now.”

        Pritchett Pollock put her hand over her microphone and leaned over to listen to Benjamin.

        “Russell Fox was here and he--” Benjamin started to say. But as he began to speak, a loud noise erupted from one of the screens and several employees stood and pointed in the direction. Pritchett Pollock jumped up and began issuing new commands.

        “Isolate it!” she yelled. “Isolate eight five zero!”

        “It’s spreading,” a worker yelled.

        “Shut it down,” Pritchett Pollock responded.

        “Are you sure?” someone yelled back.

        “Yes, shut it down,” Pritchett Pollock said calmly.

        Benjamin looked at screen eight five zero. There was chaos. A man was hitting everyone in the scene and causing violence everywhere. He was acting ruthless and without concern for anyone’s safety.

        “Something is wrong,” Pritchett Pollock whispered to herself but in a voice loud enough for Benjamin to hear. “We never get a nightmare like that.”

        “Nightmare?” Benjamin asked.

        “That was a nightmare,” Pritchett Pollock responded. “That’s why we have walls around our castle. Now, what were you going to tell me about Russell Fox?”

Chapter 15: In Which There Is Anger

        Ryan Eden and Steven Wazen waited for Benjamin to wake up in the dormitory before they began firing questions at him. They had been waiting for about thirty minutes, watching Benjamin sleep as all of the other children left. Little did they know, however, that Benjamin was doing his best to sleep as long as he could. He realized that being awake was only causing him trouble and that sleeping would allow him to pass time more quickly. There were too many people he did not trust and sleeping was his escape. The two children waiting for Benjamin to wake did not know his plan. And having the personalities that they did, they grew tired of waiting any further. They grabbed Benjamin’s bed and began rocking it from side to side.

        Obviously, Benjamin could not sleep through what was essentially a simulation of an awful boat ride. His eyes flew open and his body shifted forward as he put his arms in front to signal that he had had enough. But Ryan Eden and Steven Wazen had not noticed because they then became more occupied with shaking the bed than waking up Benjamin.

        “What are you guys doing?” Benjamin asked as he rubbed his eyes.

        “You have to wake up,” Ryan Eden said.

        “I don’t have to wake up,” Benjamin replied. “There’s no school today.”

        “Well, you were going to have to wake up at some point,” Steven Wazen added with a snicker. “And besides, we’ve got some questions we want answers to.”

        “Everyone has questions for me,” Benjamin said as he found clothing to change into. “I don’t want to answer any more questions.”

        Steven Wazen and Ryan Eden followed Benjamin as he walked across the dormitory like two snakes stalking a prey. Benjamin felt unease about their presence because they obviously had questions that he did not want to answer. And even though he could not stand up to Russell Fox or Thalia Nachamie, he also knew he could not stand up to Steven Wazen or Ryan Eden. There seemed, in Benjamin’s mind, to be no weaker person in Castle Ehtahl than himself.

        “Just one question, then,” Steven Wazen continued, unphased by Benjamin’s request for silence. “Why is it that you want to be friends with dinosaurs.”

        Benjamin paused his walking because that question was more unexpected than all of the questions that raced through his mind. But he wondered what Steven Wazen was getting at because Ryan Eden laughed uncontrollably behind him. He could answer this question, he decided, because he was not scared of what he would say.

        “We go on adventures together,” Benjamin said. “They are my friends.”

        “But, they’re in your dreams,” Steven Wazen said. “They aren’t real.”

        “I know they’re in my dreams,” Benjamin replied. “And, I thought they weren’t real. But then, I saw one of them in my bedroom.”

        “Right,” Steven Wazen said quickly. “We all know the story of how you got here. But you don’t realize that you didn’t see a dinosaur. You saw Rodney Cohen.”

        “Everyone keeps saying Rodney Cohen. Who is Rodney Cohen?”

        “Oh, Benjamin. You really don’t know? You can’t be that dumb?”

        Benjamin paused for a moment because he knew from his experience dealing with Howard Horne that there was no good answer to that question. If he responded that he was not dumb, that would be the expected response. But if he responded that he knew who Rodney Cohen was, he would be lying. Although he heard the name many times before, he still did not know. And so, Benjamin turned around in hopes that the question and the two boys would disappear.

        “Gentleman,” Noel Jaffin said as he entered the dormitory wearing less armor than on previous days. Noel cleared his throat several times as if there was something lodged between his pumpkin body and his bowling ball head. “Benjamin, follow me.”

        “Where are you taking him?” Ryan Eden asked as he walked towards Noel Jaffin.

        “That’s none of your business, Ryan,” Noel said despite being nearly a foot shorter than the boy. “Benjamin, you are to follow me at once. Let’s go.”

        Benjamin smiled inwardly as he passed the two boys and although he was not thrilled to see Noel Jaffin, he was thrilled to leave the dormitory. Whenever Noel Jaffin appeared, Benjamin knew that something had happened that was not very good. It was as if Noel Jaffin’s arrival was a message alone that trouble was near.

        “Where are we going?” Benjamin asked Noel Jaffin.

        “We,” Noel Jaffin stated as he tried to lengthen his walking distance to match that of Benjamin’s, “are not going anywhere. I am going home to watch the football game. You are going to meet Miss Lindenmeyer and Pritchett Pollock.”

        “But, there’s no school today,” Benjamin protested.

        “You are a smart one,” Noel Jaffin said sarcastically. “But danger doesn’t rest on the weekends and you’ve got a date with two lovely women. I mean, I wouldn’t--”

        “Fine, fine,” Benjamin said because he did not want to hear any more.

        Noel Jaffin escorted Benjamin through a series of buildings and hallways that Benjamin had become more accustomed to seeing. He did not know which one but he knew that the guard was taking him to a production studio.

        “Noel, how do nightmares get in here?” Benjamin asked.

        “Oh I don’t know,” Noel Jaffin grumbled through his mustache. “I suppose they come in here a lot like you came in here.”

        Benjamin thought about that answer for a second because only at that moment did he realize that he may have been confused as a nightmare. If nightmares entered the way he entered, of course everyone would assume that he was one. It made logical sense.

        The guard reached his arm above his head and grabbed a doorknob to open. It was studio two thousand and two.

        “In you go,” Noel Jaffin said as he began to shuffle Benjamin forward.

        “Wait, Noel,” Benjamin said. “Who is Rodney Cohen?”

        “Rodney? Is he here? He’s not supposed to be here! He’s been suspended! Where is he?”

        “No, no. Who is he?”

        “Rodney? He’s probably one of the most incompetent actors we’ve got in this castle,” Noel Jaffin said as he began to leverage his back to push Benjamin into the studio. “Now, in you go!”

        Rodney is an actor? Benjamin thought to himself. So, Snark wasn’t real?

        “Who are my friends?” Benjamin whispered to himself as he stared into the ground in disbelief.

        “Over here!” Miss Lindenmeyer yelled from the far side of the production studio. “Oh, Benjamin! Come over here.”

        Benjamin continued to stare into the ground as he walked forward as if walking slowly would dig up answers. He knew his friends weren’t real. They were in his dreams. But, they became real and that was why he chased after them. Well, he chased after Snark. But now, he knew his friends weren’t real. What was this place? Benjamin asked himself. Was nothing here real?

        “And, away we go,” Pritchett Pollock shouted as she turned on a flying machine and soared into the air. “I haven’t done this in a long time!”

        She moved every which direction as Miss Lindenmeyer used another machine to create clouds on the ground. She then turned on a fan which blew the clouds in the air so that Pritchett Pollock could fly between them. Miss Lindenmeyer and Pritchett Pollock were both laughing and Benjamin thought that it did look like fun.

        “Is this all fake?” Benjamin asked them.

        “What?” Miss Lindenmeyer asked. “What do you mean?”

        “Is this all fake? Are my friends fake? Are these dreams fake? Is this castle fake?”

        “Well, Benjamin, I think you’re in a state where you can answer that question as best as I can. What do you think?”

        “I don’t know anymore,” Benjamin said very grumpily. “Well, that’s not true. I’m pretty sure this is all fake.”

        “So, if it’s all fake, why don’t you just go home?”

        “I don’t know how!”

        “It can’t be all fake if you can’t get rid of it, right?”

        Benjamin did not know but he thought that perhaps Miss Lindenmeyer had a point. If it was all fake, he should be able to leave. But, he couldn’t. At least, he did not know how.

        Pritchett Pollock landed the flying machine next to Benjamin and then promptly brushed off the dust from her jacket and began straightening her hair. It was the most unorganized Benjamin had seen her so far. And, it was also the happiest he had seen her.

        “It’s been decades since I’ve used any of these machines,” Pritchett Pollock said. “I’ve been directing all this time but I haven’t had any reason to come down here and use any of these things. It’s quite enjoyable.”

        “Benjamin,” Miss Lindenmeyer began. “We asked Noel to bring you here because we want to show you how to use these machines. I told Pritchett that you could fly and, well, we want to see if you can do that again.”

        “You want me to fly?” Benjamin asked with concern. “I promise you that I don’t know how to fly.”

        “Sure,” Pritchett Pollock said. “And, I can’t either. Fly, that is. But, perhaps under the right circumstances, you might be able to do something else.”

        “With one of these machines?”

        “Yes, with one of these machines.”

        “This one,” Miss Lindenmeyer said, “is made for surfing a gigantic wave. You won’t get wet at all but you’ll be able to surf with ease.”

        The machine looked like a metal basket sewn together with copper, steel, and iron. Orange lights lined the outside and blinked like a fluid dance. It looked mechanical yet organic and heavy yet light. Like all the other machines that sat next to it, it looked like someone had spent years piecing each individual component together. If it didn’t cost a billion dollars, it looked like it was worth that much.

        “Hop on!” Pritchett Pollock said with enthusiasm.

        Benjamin had not seen her so excited and thought that perhaps this was the way adults acted when they weren’t working. Miss Lindenmeyer, too, was more excited than Benjamin had ever seen her. It was a welcome change from when the two women were so scared for Benjamin’s life.

        “I don’t know,” Benjamin said. “I’m not sure I’m ready to use these machines.”

        “Oh, nonsense,” Miss Lindenmeyer said. “Once you start it up, you don’t have to do anything. You just enjoy the ride.”

        Benjamin looked at the machine and wondered if it would bite him or guide him. Pritchett Pollock nudged Benjamin from behind but Benjamin did not move. Miss Lindenmeyer budged him and he still held his ground. He did not want to get involved with these machines. He wanted calm and anything that was less exciting at that point.

        But when both Pritchett Pollock and Miss Lindenmeyer pushed Benjamin together, he fell forward into the arms of metal and lights. The machine enveloped him like a mechanical kangaroo would hold its baby. Without asking or telling him, Pritchett Pollock pushed hard on the ignition switch and Benjamin moved to an area of the production studio where the floor was beginning to separate down the middle. As the divide grew larger, water began to rush through in powerful waves that would have been perfect for an experienced surfer. It was not, however, ideal for a boy who was pretty much scared of everything.

        The machine touched down on the water and Benjamin could not believe what was happening. He was surfing, albeit with a lot of help. But, he was actually surfing. This was something he did not imagine was possible. And more than that, he was awake and having fun.

        He surfed for what felt like hours and then Miss Lindenmeyer told him to turn the machine off. It guided him back to the women who had their hands crossed and their smiles strewn from ear to ear. They looked as happy as Benjamin looked.

        “Can I try another?” Benjamin asked with curiosity.

        “Sure!” Pritchett Pollock said. “That one will let you float in the air.”

        Benjamin ran to the machine that looked like a large mechanical crow with thousands of pieces. He turned it on and then started to float throughout the room. Miss Lindenmeyer sent clouds into the air and Benjamin felt like he was experiencing something much more enjoyable than dreams. He felt like he was experiencing something magical.

        “What is he doing up there!” Selma Applebaum yelled from the entrance of the production studio.

        She stamped her feet as she walked to Miss Lindenmeyer. Behind her, Ryan Eden and Steven Wazen marched with their arms folded and their eyes squinted. Benjamin fell from the sky upon seeing them and landed in Pritchett Pollock’s arms.

        “What are you three doing here?” Pritchett Pollock asked.

        “I want to know why he is allowed to use these machines and I am not,” Selma protested.

        “Selma, this is none of your business,” Miss Lindenmeyer said. “You need to leave immediately.”

        “We told you Miss Lindenmeyer wouldn’t let you use the machines,” Ryan Eden said from behind Selma. “Benjamin is being trained to be the top student in the class.”

        “They don’t want you to be the best anymore,” Steven Wazen said to Selma Applebaum.

        Benjamin did not know what to say because he did not know if that was Miss Lindenmeyer’s intentions. He thought that he was going to learn more machines. He did not realize that he was using machines that the other students were not allowed to touch. But, Selma Applebaum knew this and tears welled in her eyes. She turned around quickly and ran from the production studio. Ryan Eden and Steven Wazen did not waste any time and chased after her. Pritchett Pollock and Miss Lindenmeyer simply sighed and gave expressions of disappointment.

        “Is that true?” Benjamin asked. “Am I being trained to be the best in the class?”

        “No,” Miss Lindenmeyer said. “You’re not being trained.”

        “But anyone can use these machines,” Benjamin said as he looked at the thousands of machines spread across the floor.

        “That’s correct,” Pritchett Pollock said. “But, you are the only person we know who is able to use these machines while they are off.”

        “But, I turned them on before I used them.”

        “Those were buttons from my office. They did nothing. You flew and you carried a machine along with you as you flew. No one else is able to do that and that’s why you’re in a lot of danger. You are a threat to Thalia Nachamie because you don’t need to buy a machine to create a dream. You may be the most imaginative person in this castle.”

Chapter 16: In Which There Is An Escape

        Benjamin had enough. If Miss Lindenmeyer and Pritchett Pollock wanted them to be their hero, he was not going to be a part of it. He had no problem being someone’s hero, in principle. The problem he had was that to be a hero, he would have to do something remarkable and courageous. No one became a hero by being bland and predictable. And, that was what Benjamin wanted. This adventure was over and he was going home.

        In the dormitory, he wrote a note to Miss Lindemeyer and Pritchett Pollock in which he thanked them for their hospitality and for protecting him from what he did not know. And after he signed his name, he wrote that he wished he could also say bye to Bernard Zwirn as well.

        That was it, Benjamin thought. He left the note on his bed and exited the dormitory. He did not know where he was going but he decided that he could not longer stay here. Staying here was making him uncomfortable. He would go anywhere but where he was.

        As he looked at the sun rising above the green mountain, he felt free. Granted, he was still in the castle and therefore not truly free. But in his mind, he was independent and this was good. This was what he wanted. He didn’t know where he was going to go or how he was going to get there. And for the first time in his life, he was fine with that. For the first time, he was taking control.

        “Where are you walking?” Benjamin heard the familiar voice of Selma shouting down the hallway. He did not have time to say goodbye to everyone he met and so, he continued to march forward. “I said, where are you going?” she shouted again.

        When Benjamin picked up his walking pace, he heard Selma walking faster. He started to run forward and as he did so, he heard her sprinting after him. This was not, he thought, how he planned to leave. Selma could not get in his way.

        But, she was faster than he was. Benjamin tried his hardest to move every muscle faster than they had ever moved before. It was the fastest he had ever run but it was not fast enough. Selma stood in front of him and would not let him pass.

        “Are you deaf?” she shouted into his face. “I asked you where you were going.”

        “I am going home,” Benjamin declared and walked past her.

        Selma followed and laughed lightly as she did so.

        “And how exactly are you going to do that?” she asked.

        “I haven’t figured it out,” Benjamin said honestly. “I’m going to find Rodney Cohen and he’s going to tell me how to get back home. He’s the only person here who knows where I live. He’ll show me the way.”

        Selma laughed again, more lightly this time.

        “Benjamin, all Rodney Cohen will do for you is get you lost somewhere else. You’re better off waiting for Bernard Zwirn to return.”

        Benjamin stopped and turned to the taller, stronger child standing before him.

        “Why do you care?” he asked.

        “I don’t!” she answered quickly. “But, I’m telling you that you’re stupid to think you can get back home with Rodney Cohen guiding you. He doesn’t know his left from his right. I’m not kidding.”

        “I’m not going to stay where I’m not welcome so I’m going to leave.”

        “Do you do that often?” Selma asked as Benjamin marched away into the crowds walking in the town.

        “Do I do what often?” he yelled back.

        “Do you walk away from your problems often?” she yelled back.

        Benjamin turned around sharply to address her but when he looked in her direction, she disappeared. He did walk away from his problems and he did not know why this was any of her business. If he wanted to walk away from problems, he would walk away from problems. That was, he believed, the only thing he could do. What else could he do? Nothing, he thought.

People brushed by him from every direction as they walked to their destinations for the day. Some walked to the production studios, some walked to the market, and some walked to the cafes and bakeries that had opened only an hour earlier. It was a little chillier than usual that morning. But Benjamin’s face at that moment was very warm because he was not happy with Selma Applebaum. She needed to mind her own business, he thought.

He was not, however, going to tell her this because he needed to leave.

He marched forward to the gate on the other side of the town that would lead him to somewhere else. He walked past the school, past Pritchett Pollock’s office, past Bernard Zwirn’s house, and past the train station. And as he passed the train station, he closed his eyes as he realized that the building looked no different than any of the other production studios. Was it actually a train station? he asked himself. Or, was it another dream manufactured by these people? He was puzzled and then someone grabbed his left shoulder.

“So,” Ryan Wazen said without pausing for a second. “Could you fly?”

“Could I fly?” Benjamin asked, angered that yet another student had found him on his attempt to leave. “No, I couldn’t fly,” he lied. “Flying is impossible.”

“Of course,” Ryan said. “Flying is impossible but that doesn’t answer my question.”

“It’s a silly question.”

“No, it’s not. Could you fly?”

“Of course I couldn’t fly,” Benjamin lied for the second time. “No one can fly.”

“People can fly but if you can’t, I guess that’s a shame. Miss Lindenmeyer was wrong about that kind of stuff before. Don’t take it too hard, kid.”

“What do you mean in the past?”

“About kids that she thinks can fly. They usually can’t. Some of them could, I was told. But, we never saw them again.”

“Where do they go?”

“Wouldn’t you like to know,” Ryan said as he started to walk backwards from Benjamin. “You don’t have to worry about it because you can’t fly. Don’t ask questions you don’t want to know the answer to. That’s what my dad always told me.”

Ryan ran off and Benjamin turned around to continue to walk to the exit. He did not want to know anything more about this place. There were too many secrets and too many people who confused him.

Guarding the gate were two men who looked identical to Noel Jaffin. They both had the same box shaped figure and short stature. Benjamin thought that if they did not let him pass, he might be able to quite easily topple them over.

“Stop!” the guards yelled in unison. “If you pass, it will only be by gas.”

“What?” Benjamin asked.

“If you pass--”

“I heard what you said,” Benjamin responded. “I didn’t quite expect you to say that. I’m leaving, Noel, so I would appreciate if you would open the gate.”

“Who is Noel?” asked one of the guards as he stamped his wooden pole into the ground.

“Are you Noel?” the other guard asked the previous one.

“I’m not Noel. I’m Joel. Are you Noel?” Joel asked the other guard.

“I’m not Noel. I’m Cole. Haven’t we met?” Cole asked Joel.

“I guess not.”

“We stand her every day and we’ve never introduced ourselves.”

“It’s nice to meet you,” Joel said to Cole.

“Same!” Cole said he shook Joel’s hand.

“But you shall not pass unless you are gas!” Joel and Cole yelled at Benjamin in unison.

“I don’t think you realize what you’re saying,” Benjamin said as he tried not to giggle.

“The only way you’re getting through us is if you’re gas,” Joel said sternly.

“Yes, I know but you’re saying--” Benjamin began.

“You shall only pass if you’re gas,” Cole repeated.

        “OK, I need to leave,” Benjamin said.

        “No!” they yelled back in unison. “No one leaves!”

        “I am no one. Can I leave?”

        Cole and Joel looked at each other with a puzzled expression. They looked as if they were pondering something their brains were not capable of understanding.

        “Well, this is interesting,” Cole said to Joel.

        “Interesting indeed,” Joel said to Cole.

        “Could this be the no one that is allowed to leave?”

        “It’s quite possible that if no one is allowed to leave and this child before us is no one, he could leave.”

        “That seems right to me as well but how do we know that he is no one?”

        “He just said he was no one.”

        “Ah, right. But would no one lie?”

        “Good point, Joel! No one tells the truth all the time.”

        “So then, no one is a liar.”

        “This child is no one the liar.”

        “No one, you shall not pass!” they yelled in unison.

        “Is there another gate?” Benjamin asked. He did not want to have to deal with Joel and Cole any longer. He was getting a headache.

        “Of course, there are four more,” Cole said as he stamped his wooden pole back into the ground.

        “There are four more!” Joel said with surprise.

        “I really think we need a better onboarding process,” Cole said. “I don’t know who guards those gates.”

        “Me neither!”

Benjamin walked along the walls at a quick speed to find another gate. He did not want to have to deal with Joel or Cole if he could find an easier way to leave.

“Good luck, no one,” Cole cried out after Benjamin.

Benjamin walked between the castle walls and the back of small houses and production studios. It was a narrow alley that felt neglected compared to the rest of the clean town. It was muddy and there were bits of garbage tossed throughout. It made sense, he thought, because no one walked along this path. As Benjamin walked further, he wondered if the only people who would traverse this disgusting, claustrophobic path were the guards who tended the gate.

He had been walking for a good period of time and did not yet see an exit. The curved walls of the castle made him think the he might walk a full circle to see Joel and Cole again.

His left foot stepped into wet mud that sucked his foot. He quickly moved his right foot to a rock and tried to pull his other foot forward. It was gross and disgusting and Benjamin knew that he would have to throw his shoes away after this was all done. It made a loud squishy noise like the sound he made when he tried to vacuum the water out of the bathtub when he was six.

It started to make him laugh.

And, he would have continued to laugh except that he heard another familiar voice.

“But, what if I don’t want to,” Benjamin heard Steven Wazen say. “I’m not as good as the others.”

“It doesn’t matter if you’re stronger or better than the others,” Benjamin heard Thalia Nachamie say. “You are my son and you will follow in my footsteps. No other person or child is going to get in your or my way. Do you understand?”

Benjamin crouched as low as he could to the mud as he realized the noise was coming from the house immediately to his left.

“I understand, father. I’ll follow in your footsteps.”

“I’ve already paved the path for you. Miss Lindenmeyer has been replaced. You won’t be seeing her again and there is no chance that she’ll get in our way again,” Thalia Nachamie said.

Benjamin’s heart sank as he wondered what had happened to Miss Lindenmeyer. He had just seen her yesterday.

“What about Selma?” Steven Wazen asked his father.

“You won’t have to worry about Selma,” Thalia Nachamie said. “With Miss Lindenmeyer out of the picture, I’ll be King. And then, you’ll be King. This is a glorious time for us.”

“It is, father,” Steven Wazen said.

“Now, run along,” Thalia Nachamie said. “I have to do some things to get ready for tomorrow.”

Benjamin kept his little body as close to the wet, sticky mud as possible so that he could avoid being seen. He was scared for himself. And also, he was scared for Miss Lindenmeyer. He wanted to know what happened to her and why Thalia Nachamie got rid of her. He did not know that Steven was Thalia Nachamie’s son. No one said anything about that before.

It was hours before Benjamin moved. He was as still as a clay statue.

        The sun setting on the other side of the castle cast a shadow over the path. He would be hidden, he thought, but only if he moved quickly. With his left foot hovering above the ground, he counted to three and then sprinted. The castle wall moved so quickly that he wondered if he could run this fast forever. He would have to because he did not know what was on the other side. He was prepared, he thought as he ran, to blast through whoever stood at the end.

        With the exit in sight, Benjamin ran faster and faster.

        He closed his eyes and ran straight through someone. The collision felt like when he accidentally ran into the basketball pole at home.

        “What in all that is good are you doing?” Noel Jaffin yelled at Benjamin.

        “Noel, is that you?”

        “Benjamin! What is wrong with you?”

        Noel had been knocked over like a beanbag chair thrown down a staircase.

        “Noel, is that really you?”

        “Yes, Benjamin. It is me, Noel. Who else would it be?” Noel said. “Now, would you mind telling me why you ran me over?”
        “Noel, Miss Lindenmeyer. Where is she?”

        Noel’s expression changed and he looked from side to side quickly. He lowered his tone and he voice a lot.

        “We can’t talk about that here, Benjamin,” Noel said. “She’s missing.”

        “Missing!” Benjamin yelled.

        “Quiet! Quiet!” Noel whispered. “Yes, you’re in a lot of danger. It’s good I ran into you. I wish you didn’t run into me. But, I need you to wait here. I parked my car on the other side of the market. I’ll be right here in five minutes. Do not move a muscle, OK?”

        Benjamin nodded as he looked at the hundreds of people moving throughout the marketplace. Noel disappeared into the audience and Benjamin decided that he could trust the guard. He had to find Pritchett Pollock to understand what had happened to Miss Lindenmeyer. He couldn’t leave just yet, he thought. He needed to make sure she was OK.

        As he waited, he scanned across the people in the marketplace and recognized a face. Benjamin retreated into the shadow so that he could not be seen. It was Russell Fox.

        Russell Fox was walking around very suspiciously. He was wearing a long dark jacket and had both his hands in his pocket as he moved from market shop to market shop. Benjamin watched him very carefully because he knew Russell Fox was trouble. As Russell Fox turned in place, Benjamin got a glimpse of something metal that Russell Fox was holding in his right hand. And then, Russell Fox walked to a stand covered in oranges and stood there for a few minutes. Something was very wrong, Benjamin thought. Russell Fox then stuck his right hand in the middle of the oranges and walked away quickly, in the opposite direction of Benjamin. And as he walked away, Benjamin noticed the metal piece was no longer in his pocket.

        As soon as Russell Fox faded into the crowded, Benjamin snuck quickly through the crowd to the gigantic stack of oranges. He put his hand into the oranges as the shopkeeper stared at him with an annoyed expression. Benjamin tried to be calm about it. He tried to find the place where Russell Fox placed his hand.

        Then, he felt something metal.

        He grabbed it and waited for the shopkeeper to be distracted by another customer. Benjamin removed it quickly and put it in his pocket.

        As he walked back to the shadow where Noel Jaffin was to find him, he took it out. He knew exactly what it was. He looked at the dream machine and realized he could help this castle after all. He found the missing piece.

Chapter 17: In Which There Is A Judgment

        “Noel!” Benjamin yelled as the overweight guard drove a vehicle only slightly larger than his body to Benjamin. His car looked like a square, metal box in which Noel occupied just about the entire space. Once he parked, he leveraged all of his weight forward to get out of the vehicle like an elephant trying to squeeze itself out of a refrigerator.

        “What is it, Benjamin?” a sweaty Noel answered as he brushed the dust from his pants.

        “Noel, I found something that could help me and help Ehtahl,” Benjamin said as he gripped the missing piece in his pocket.

        “Right. Right. I’ve heard this before. Let’s just get you to the police station so we can figure out what to do with you next.”

        “You don’t understand. This could answer all of our problems. The mystery of the missing piece of the dream machine is over,” Benjamin said as he opened his hand to reveal the missing object.

        Noel did not look convinced. He crossed his arms and tightened his lips, ultimately ending his bored performance with a heavy sigh. He picked the piece from Benjamin’s hand and inspected it from every angle.

        “This is scrap,” he said as he tossed it over his shoulder.

        Benjamin ran after it and caught it before it hit the ground. If the missing piece broke, then the dream machine certainly would not work.

        “Noel, this is the missing piece. We can put it in the dream machine and it’ll start working again.”

        “How are you so sure? This is scrap metal. This doesn’t mean anything.”

        “Can’t we at least try?”

        “Try what?” Steven Wazen said from behind Benjamin.

        Benjamin did not know how long Steven Wazen had been standing behind him or how much he had heard. At that moment, Benjamin wanted to focus only on getting this metal component into the dream machine. He was worried that Steven Wazen might distract from this goal.

        “Nothing, Steven,” Noel Jaffin said in response. “Just another person among hundreds of thousands thinking they are special enough to have found the missing piece of the dream machine.”

        “He thinks he’s found the missing piece to the dream machine?” Steven Wazen asked as he stood immediately next to Benjamin. He had a skeptical and accusational expression that made Benjamin’s stomach clench. “How long have you had it?”

        “How long have I have it?” Benjamin asked with a startle. “I’ve only just found it. I found it in the market. We have to see if it fits because this could answer all of our problems.”

        “Can I see it?” Steven Wazen asked.

        Benjamin paused. He did not want to give it to anyone else after having watched Noel Jaffin carelessly toss it over his shoulder.

        “Come on,” Steven Wazen continued. “Let me see it.”

        Benjamin stared into Steven Wazen’s eyes and then glanced at the ground. Before he could hide the piece, Noel Jaffin let out a loud groan and yanked it from Benjamin’s hands.

        “I don’t understand kids these days,” Noel Jaffin said to himself as he gave Steven Wazen the component. “Here. Here is the scrap metal.”

        Steven Wazen inspected it in exactly the same way Noel Jaffin had just examined it. But unlike Noel Jaffin, Steven Wazen’s expression became more and more intrigued and curious. It was as if he was understanding something that Benjamin could not see.

        “It’s scrap metal,” Steven Wazen said quickly.

        “I knew it,” Noel Jaffin said. “Now, Benjamin, let’s get a move on.”

        “Can I have it back?” Benjamin asked Steven Wazen who still held the metal piece.

        “I’ll dispose of it for you,” Steven Wazen said as he put it in his pocket and quickly ran away.

        “There,” Noel Jaffin said. “That was really nice of him to offer to get rid of it for you.”

        Benjamin was irate. He wanted to run after Steven Wazen but the boy had already become hidden by the crowd in the marketplace.

        “Noel, that was the missing piece!” Benjamin said in complete disbelief. “He took the missing piece for the dream machine!”

        “It’s scrap metal, Benjamin. You’re not the first person to claim to have found the missing piece. You’re actually the seventeenth person who claims to have found one today. Or, eighteenth. I’m not sure. The sooner we get you to the station, the sooner we’ll know what number you are,” Noel Jaffin said as he ushered Benjamin to the small car. “Now, we’re going to have both fit inside here. You get in first.”

        Benjamin looked at Noel Jaffin with disapproval. There was no room for anyone else in this car once Noel Jaffin was inside it.

        It was the most uncomfortable car ride that Benjamin had ever experience, his face squashed between the window and Noel Jaffin’s hot, squishy belly. His legs were on top of each other and he could not move his arms. When they arrived in the station’s parking lot, Benjamin felt like his body had been damaged in every place. It was excruciating and upon seeing Selma Applebaum at the station, embarrassing.

        “What are you doing here?” Benjamin asked Selma as he tried to straighten out his bones and muscles.

        “I was arrested,” Selma Applebaum said without flinching.

        “Really?” Benjamin asked.

        “No,” Selma Applebaum said as she walked past him. “I was searching for Miss Lindenmeyer.”

        “Noel told me she’s missing.”

        “She is,” Selma Applebaum replied. “Noel asked me to stop in the station to talk to some of the other guards.”

        “Do you know where she is?”

        “No,” Selma Applebaum said. “But, I have a good idea who is responsible for this.”

        “Who?”

        “I can’t tell you now. But for your own safety, you better stay out of sight. You’re making quite a few enemies.”

        “I’m making quite a few enemies!” Benjamin exclaimed. “I’ve been nice to everyone.”

        “Not everyone thinks that’s the case.”

        “Benjamin,” Noel Jaffin called from his office on the other end of the station. “Get in here.”

        “See you later, Benjamin,” Selma Applebaum said as she left the station.

        “Selma, wait! I forgot to tell you--” he started to say but it was too late. Selma Applebaum had already left and could not hear him. He should have mentioned the missing component earlier, he thought, because maybe she could get it from Ralph Eden.

        Benjamin walked along the blue carpet lined with yellow desks and cubicles until he reached Noel Jaffin’s office. The room was, sadly, only slightly larger than Noel Jaffin. Benjamin paused at the door, took a large sigh, and then squeezed his way between a small space between the desk and a wall. There was only a little bit more space than there was in the car. But unlike the car, Benjamin and Noel Jaffin sat face to face, only inches away from touching.

        It was uncomfortable.

        “Benjamin, we’ve got to find a way to hide you for a bit,” Noel Jaffin said.

        Benjamin wanted to end this conversation as quickly as possible so that he could leave the office.

        “Sure, OK. Let’s do it,” Benjamin said quickly.

        “Alright, so I’ll just arrest you and we’ll put you in a jail cell for the time being. No one is going to bother you there.”

        “Wait. Arrest me?”

        “Yep, I’ll arrest you for assault or something. I’ll tell people who you hit me. Ouch!” Noel Jaffin said with a hearty chuckle. Benjamin could feel the heat of the laugh on his face. It was disgusting.

        “Can’t you just put me in a jail cell?” Benjamin asked. He couldn’t believe he asked the question because he did not want to be in a jail cell at all. There must be a better option, he thought.

        “No, no, no,” Noel Jaffin said while shaking his head. With each turn of his neck, Noel Jaffin almost hit Benjamin with his nose. “We can’t put innocent people in the jail cells.”

        “But, I am innocent.”

        “Yes, but that’s why I said I would tell people who you assaulted me.”

        “But, I haven’t assaulted you.”

        “It’s true. OK, hit me.”

        “What?”

        “Hit me,” Noel Jaffin said as he squinted his eyes and lifted his shoulders in preparation of Benjamin hitting him.

        “I’m not going to hit you!”

        “Hit me!”

        “No!”

        “Do it!”

        “No!”

        “Punch me in the face!”

        Benjamin wanted to punch Noel Jaffin in the face. But, he knew he couldn’t do it. If he went to jail for a crime that he did in fact commit, he would be in even more trouble than he was now.

        “No, I won’t!”

        “Fine,” Noel Jaffin said as he opened his eyes and relaxed his body. “I’ll just tell people who you punched me in the face.”

        “But, I didn’t. Can’t you put me somewhere else than a jail cell?”

        “There is no other place in this castle that is as safe and secure as our jail cells. No one will bother you there. The only other place is the zoo but I don’t think you’ll like it there.”

        “There’s a zoo?” Benjamin asked with curiosity.

        “Yes, it’s over--” Noel Jaffin began to say until a woman twice Noel Jaffin’s size entered the doorway.

        Benjamin swallowed hard. There was no more space in this office. He would be crushed if she wanted to sit inside the office as well.

        “Noel, may I have a word with you?” the enormous square woman said.

        “Yes, boss, sure,” Noel Jaffin said to her. “Stay here, Benjamin.”

        Noel Jaffin squeezed his way out of the office, causing Benjamin to feel crushed between the desk and the wall. His body had not endured so much torture as it had from this large man in such small environments. Benjamin breathed heavily in an attempt to get his health back in order. The office walls had pictures and books that had been squashed like flies against the white paint. A plant looked like it was flattened against the window and Noel Jaffin’s chair looked like it had been through several wars. It was losing the battle against Noel Jaffin’s weight.

        “Benjamin,” Noel Jaffin said as he reentered the doorway. Benjamin hoped that Noel Jaffin and his boss were not about to both enter the office. “We have to go for a castle meeting.”

        “OK, I’ll be here,” Benjamin said.

        “No, you’re coming along.”

        They walked to the plaza and to Benjamin, it felt nearly identical to the setting when Thalia Nachamie addressed all of the town. The entire castle’s population was standing and sitting around while some workers were scrambling to erect screens and speakers. Noel Jaffin did not have the same expression of worry that Miss Lindenmeyer had the last time Benjamin was here. Instead, he kept looking at his watch while shuffling a candy bar in his other hand.

        “What is this for?” Benjamin asked.

        “I don’t know exactly,” Noel Jaffin replied. “But, it better not get in the way of lunch.”

        “When is lunch?”

        “When isn’t it lunch?” Noel Jaffin said with a hearty laugh. “Twenty minutes.”

        Benjamin looked around the audience for someone he knew but like last time, did not see anyone. There was no Miss Lindenmeyer. No Pritchett Pollock. No Selma Applebaum. And, no Steven Wazen or Ryan Eden.

        There was, however, someone he had recognized before. On the opposite side of the plaza, Benjamin saw Rodney Cohen.

        “Noel, that’s Rodney!” Benjamin said to Noel Jaffin. “I know him.”

        “Argh, Rodney Cohen,” Noel Jaffin said. “Stay away from that man, Benjamin. His incompetence is contagious.”

        “Incompetence?”

        “Rodney Cohen makes problems, despite his best efforts to not make problems.”

        Benjamin strained his neck to see where Rodney Cohen was walking. If he knew where Rodney was going next, he could meet him once this announcement ended. As Benjamin thought he watched Rodney enter a door to a large building, the audience stood and jumped with excitement. A roar of cheers waved across the people as Benjamin looked to the balcony to see who was going to speak to the crowds.

        It was Thalia Nachamie. Benjamin expected to see him and hoped that he was standing far away that the evil man would not be able to see him.

        But then, two more people stepped onto the balcony. Benjamin did not expect to see these two and his heart slowed with a little worry.

        It was Ryan Eden.

        And behind Ryan Eden, it was Steven Wazen.

        “What are they doing up there?” Benjamin muttered to himself.

        “Quiet,” Noel Jaffin said as he nudged Benjamin. “We’re going to find out if they’ve found Bernard Zwirn.”

        Thalia Nachamie hit his hand against the microphone three times, causing all of the speakers around the audience to pop in response. He leaned forward and with his long, crane-like nose hooking over the microphone began to speak.

        “We have not found our beloved King Bernard Zwirn,” Thalia Nachamie said to the cries of the audience below. “But, our efforts are not in vain. We are continuing to search for him. We search in the night. We search in the day. We are searching all the time. And so, it is with my deep regret that I must be made king. It is not by my choosing, of course. It is to make sure that dreams are available to all that go to sleep at night. You see, without a King, this castle does not have a leader. And without a leader, there are no dreams. Today, I present myself, King Thalia Nachamie, the leader of Castle Ehtahl.”

        As Thalia Nachamie stopped talking, the crowd remained silent for a few seconds until Russell Fox began to clap. When Russell Fox clapped, people around him started to clap. And then, people around those people started to clap. And this persisted until the entire audience was clapping for Thalia Nachamie, their new king.

        “My followers, I want to let you know that even though I am now King, that does not mean that we will stop looking for Bernard Zwirn. In fact, it is quite important that we not be stopped in our plan to continue searching for our friend. For you see, good people, there is one person among all of you who is hindering our progress. There is one person among all of you who does not want us to find Bernard Zwirn. There is one person who is trying to steal from us.”

        Gasps and whispers spread throughout the audience. Even Benjamin wondered what Thalia Nachamie was alluding to. If anyone was in the way of searching for Bernard Zwirn, Benjamin thought, it was Thalia Nachamie.

        “Only this morning, I was made aware of this.”

        Thalia Nachamie turned around and Steven Wazen handed his father the missing piece of the dream machine that Benjamin had only hours earlier.

        “That’s the piece,” Benjamin told Noel Jaffin.

        “The what?” Noel asked as he looked at his watch again.

        “That’s the missing piece of the dream machine that you said was scrap metal.”

        Noel Jaffin did not say anything. He looked forward, squinting his eyes to see if Benjamin was, in fact, correct.

        “There is someone in this audience who had the missing piece of the dream machine all along,” Thalia Nachamie’s voice echoed through the plaza. “This person did not want us to have it. He wanted to keep it for himself. He wanted to make sure the dream machine never worked.”

        “That was Russell Fox,” Benjamin whispered to Noel Jaffin. “That’s who I saw put it in the market stand.”

        “Shh, quiet down,” Noel Jaffin said to Benjamin. “I may have to make an arrest.”

        “Someone in our castle is preventing us from making dreams. Someone has been putting us through turmoil all along.”

The audience stirred.

“But my followers, I am proud to say that we have identified the person. And, we are going to exile him from our castle. He is no longer welcomed here and we will not have him among us any more.”

        Cheers and applause echoed throughout the plaza. Benjamin strained his neck to see where Russell Fox was, but he was not standing in the same location as he was before. Benjamin looked in every which direction to find where the thief went.

        “That person will be punished!”

        The crowd screamed loudly.

“He will be removed!”

The crowd raised their fists in the air.

“He is no longer welcome here!” Thalia Nachami raised his fist into the air as he finished each sentence.

The crowd cheered.

“He must leave immediately and go outside these castle walls! Benjamin Buckingham, that means you!”

Chapter 18: In Which There Is A Departure

        Benjamin was thrilled. He wanted to leave the castle all along and finally, he was being granted his request. He was not thrilled with the way in which he would be leaving. He had hoped that he everyone would be smiling and happy and that a few people would have tears in their eyes as he departed. No one had tears in their eyes. Instead, everyone was squinting their eyes at Benjamin with intense hatred.

        And yet, Benjamin had a hard time not smiling himself.

        He was leaving. He was finally leaving. This was the best moment so far.

        “Why are you smiling?” Selma Applebaum whispered to Benjamin as the large crowd in front of him began to create a path for him to walk to the gate.

        “I’m finally out of here. I get to leave the castle,” Benjamin said.

        “You need to stop smiling,” Selma said sternly between her teeth. “You are making people very angry.”

        “What do I care?” Benjamin said. “I’ll never see any of these people again.”

        “I don’t think you know what you’re getting yourself into,” Selma said quickly. “You don’t know what’s on the other side of those walls.”

        “I know what’s on this side of the wall and it isn’t my home. If it’s not here, it must be out there,” Benjamin said as he tried to rationalize his enthusiasm.

        He couldn’t stop grinning. He was smiling from ear to ear.

        And yet, he did not want to make anyone angry. He was just so happy. And everyone was certainly angry. There was no disputing that. The people in front of him were angrier than any people Benjamin had ever seen before. There were so many reasons to be happy right now that Benjamin did not care what anyone else thought of him.

        He did not even care what Thalia Nachamie thought of him.

        “Benjamin Buckingham,” Thalia Nachamie stood in front of the exit. “You are hereby banished from this castle and you are never to return.”

        He emphasized every other word with spit and a clenched fist.

        “Do you understand?” Thalia Nachamie stared deep inside Benjamin’s eyes.

        “Yep,” Benjamin said quickly.

        “You shall never return!”

        “Yep, I shall never return.”

        “You shall not be welcome back.”

        “Yep, I shall not be welcome back.”

        “You shall live forever with nightmares.”

        “What? Nightmares? Where?”

        “Leave! Now!”

        Thalia Nachamie turned to the guards standing behind him. Noel, Joel, and Cole all turned a steel wheel as quickly as their short bodies could turn it. The wheel was nearly double their size and as one of the guards pulled, another was lifted up into the air until he let go.

        He was going home.

        Noel, Joel, and Cole opened the door nearly halfway when Thalia Nachamie motioned for them to stop. The guards were dripping in sweat and breathing like dogs having chased tennis balls for hours. Thalia Nachamie had decided that there was enough room for Benjamin to exit.

        Then, all of the people in the plaza turned their heads and stared at Benjamin. He had never had such attention in his life as he had at that moment. He was the most popular person in the castle.

        He took one step forward and Selma Applebaum tugged at the back of his shirt.

        “You can still apologize,” she whispered quickly.

        “What?” Benjamin asked with confusion.

        “You can apologize. If you apologize, they may let you stay.”

        “Why would I want to stay?” Benjamin whispered back as he took another step forward.

        “Because,” Selma Applebaum said slowly. “You don’t know what’s on the other side of the walls.”

        “You’re right,” Benjamin said as he took another step forward. “But, I know what isn’t here. I have a better chance of getting home out there than I do here.”

        “You don’t know that,” Selma Applebaum said with a sense of warning.

        “I don’t but I’m willing to take my chance. If you haven’t noticed, I am not very popular right now,” he whispered as he waved to more people who were sneering at him as he passed.

        “Don’t say I didn’t warn you,” Selma Applebaum said as she disappeared into the crowd.

        Benjamin saw some of his classmates in the crowd along with several actors he had seen in the production studios.

        “So long,” he said casually to a group of women on his right.

        “Have a good day,” he said to some men on his left.

        “Let’s go,” Thalia Nachamie said as Benjamin approached the gates. “We don’t have much time.”

        “Alright, alright,” Benjamin said as he skipped forward to the door. “So long, Noel. So long, Joel and Cole.”

        “So long, no one,” Joel and Cole said.

        “Be gone with you!” Thalia Nachamie yelled as he pushed Benjamin through the door. “Don’t ever come back!”

        Benjamin was being pushed forcibly through the exit. He went through the gigantic iron doors with the largest smile on his face that he could remember.

        He left.

        He finally left.

        Behind him, the guards trampled on top of each other to close the door. Benjamin listened to the straining metal door as it whined in pain. When it was finally closed, it let out a short thud.

        And then, Benjamin heard applause and cheering.

        The plaza from which he left had erupted in happiness and excitement.

        This hurt Benjamin’s heart. He did not want to be hated. No one wanted to be hated. But Benjamin especially did not want to be hated.

        It was fine, he thought to himself, because he would never see those people again. He could finally go home.

        But as he looked at the area outside the castle, he did not know exactly where to begin. It was not as bright and lovely and beautiful as he had expected. Instead, it was a desert.

        There wasn’t a living plant as far as Benjamin could see. There was no water or even any animals. There was just dirt and cracks in the ground and the sound of the sun baking the earth.

        Maybe, Benjamin thought, he did not know what he was getting himself into.

        He couldn’t think about that now. The decision had been made. He was now on the other side of the castle. The door behind him was closed and Benjamin could hear the guards closing more doors and then raising a bridge and then closing another door and then pushing heavy objects behind the door.

        He was not welcome to return.

        He did not want to go back, even if they wanted him to return.

        “Incoming!” Benjamin heard Noel Jaffin’s voice yell from behind the walls.

        Benjamin turned and upon seeing something in the sky heading in his direction cowered in fear. He was now being attacked! They were throwing things at him.

        When it hit the ground, Benjamin saw it was a backpack. He ran over to it and opened it up to find a bottle of water and more arrows than Benjamin thought could fit in the backpack.

        “Incoming!’ Benjamin heard Noel Jaffin’s voice yell again.

        In the sky, another object headed straight for Benjamin who ducked away as quickly as he could. This object, he realized, was a bow and a guide to edible plants outside the castle. It was actually entitled A Guide To Plants Outside The Castle Not That You’ll Ever Need This Because Everyone Stays In The Castle.

        Noel must know something that Benjamin doesn’t, he thought. And for that, whatever these gifts were, Benjamin said thank you to the castle wall.

        “Quiet villain!” Noel yelled back.

        Benjamin chuckled.

        “Thanks, Noel.”

        And with that, he was on his own. He turned and walked into the desert as alone as a person could be. He took five steps and the feeling of loneliness began to replace the feeling of excitement and happiness.

        He had no idea what he was doing.

        It was him, the desert, and his thoughts.

Chapter 19: In Which There Is A Squirrel

        This time around, Benjamin did not want to see dinosaurs. If he saw one of those gigantic creatures here, it was undoubtedly going to be because the lizard wanted to eat him or stomp on him. The desert was no place for fun. It was ruthless.

        And, certainly, there was no desert near his home.

        As he walked further into the dry emptiness, the cold castle behind him faded into the distance until he reached a point in his walking where he could see nothing in the distance.

        Benjamin reached into the backpack for some water. As he drank some, he knew that he had to save more for later. There was no water fountain for as far as he could see.

        He put it back in the backpack and upon doing so, realized that there was a piece of paper at the bottom of the bag. He took it out and upon unfolding it, he saw that it was a crudely drawn map. In large letters in the lower right hand corner was the name Noel.

        The castle was in the center. To the north of the castle was a forest. Noel had drawn some terrible looking trees. To the south were the words Don’t go here! and to the east were the words You’ll die here! and to the west were the words Worse than the other two!.

        Benjamin decided that he would walk to the forest but he didn’t see any forest in site. Was he walking north? He didn’t know. He hoped so because Noel made it very clear that north was the only direction to go.

        As Benjamin pondered which way to go, he heard a faint noise from behind him. He squinted his eyes but could not see what was making the commotion. It sounded like an air conditioner in the distance getting louder and louder. Benjamin squinted more and noticed a trail of dust being sent into the air by something moving along the land at a fast speed.

        It was coming right at him.

        Benjamin picked up the backpack and ran as fast as he could away from whatever was chasing him.

        The humming noise was getting louder and the trail of dust was getting closer. Benjamin ran faster but he could not run fast enough. The sound was beginning to take the shape of a siren. Something was going to run him over soon enough. He crouched to the ground and braced himself for impact.

        “North! North! North!” yelled a squirrel as it ran past. “North! North! North! North!”

        Benjamin opened his left eyes and saw the squirrel sprint off as dust and dirt flew into the air. He had never seen a squirrel move as fast as that squirrel had moved. He also had never heard a squirrel speak.

        “Wait! Wait!” Benjamin yelled to it.

        “North! North! North! North!” the squirrel kept yelling in the distance.

        Benjamin ran in the same direction but could not maintain the same speed that the squirrel maintained. It was as if the squirrel had an engine. At least, Benjamin thought, he knew where north was. He walked forward and about two hours later, he saw a forest on the horizon and no speaking squirrel in site.

        The forest began to expand to the left and to the right of the horizon as Benjamin approached it. It seemed to be as wide as Benjamin could see. And on the edge of the desert, about a hundred feet from the start of the forest, was a wooden stand with a large sign at the top that read Information Desk. It was peculiar, Benjamin thought, because there was nothing else out here. He approached the stand and saw that there were maps, brochures, and even coupons for a variety of discounts.

        But on top of the counter was a silver bell with a note that said to ring for assistance. Benjamin certainly needed assistance. So, he rang the bell.

        The leaves of the forest swayed as if a wide wind had swept across the land. The trunks of the trees moved back and forth while the foliage on the ground moved into the air.

        Benjamin looked into the forest to see what would happen.

        “Why hello there!” Benjamin heard a voice but he could not see the speaker.

        “Hello?” Benjamin asked.

        “Hello there! How are you?” the voice said again. It was loud enough to be a person but Benjamin could not see who was speaking.

        “Hello? Where are you?” Benjamin asked as he strained his head to look around and around.

        “I’m right here! How are you?”

        “Right where?”

        “Here!”

        “Where is here?”

        “Here? This is the forest!”

        “No, where are you?”

        “Oh, I’m on the information desk. Welcome to the information desk! I don’t get many visitors but that does not mean I am not well trained in the art of customer service.”

        Benjamin looked at the desk and saw a green caterpillar the size of his thumb. It was standing on its end and speaking to him.

        “You’re a caterpillar!” Benjamin said in surprise.

        “You’re a human!” the caterpillar responded in mock surprise.

        “And you can talk?” Benjamin asked.

        “And you can talk?” the caterpillar responded again.

        “Well, I’ve never heard a caterpillar talk before.”

        “Trust me, son. You’re going to see some things you’ve never seen before out here.”

        “Out here?”

        “Yes, outside the castles.”

        “Castles? There’s more than one?”

        “Oh, my. You can’t be from here. You’ve got so many questions. Where are you from if you don’t mind my asking?”

        “New York,” Benjamin said quickly. The caterpillar’s green face turned white and the leaves stopped swaying and the tree trunks stopped shaking. Everything had come to a standstill. “Why does everyone react this way when I say I’m from New York.”

        “Sh! Sh!” the caterpillar yelled as it held its finger to its lips. “Don’t be so loud!”

        “But--”

        “Listen just because you’re from New York doesn’t mean you have to tell people from here you’re from New York.”

        “But--”

        “OK, so you’re from New York. What in the universe of dreams are you doing here?” the caterpillar had its hands on its hips and was tapping its right feet on the ground.

        “I am trying to leave. I’m trying to go back to New York.”

        “Sh! Sh!” the caterpillar hushed Benjamin. “OK, OK. That makes sense. How did you ever get here in the first place?”

        Benjamin began to open his mouth to explain.
        “You know what?” the caterpillar quickly responded. “It’s probably best if I don’t know about it. What is your name?”

        “My name is Benjamin.”

        “Benjamin, it’s a pleasure to meet you. My name is Myrna Delacourte. Now let me see here,” Myrna said as she rummaged through the brochures and informational papers properly organized in the information stand. “Forest. Forest. Forest. Going north. Things not to eat. Things to eat. Things best left untouched. Sorry, Benjamin. I don’t have any information guides for New York.”

        “I don’t need a guide for getting to New York. I need a guide to leave here.”

        “Well,” Myrna responded with shock. “This may not be the cleanest or the coolest or the hippest or the healthiest place but it is not the worst, either!”

        “No, I mean I have to go home and if I can get to anywhere with a plane, train, or bus, I can get back to New York.”

        “Sh! Sh! We have planes, trains, and buses,” Myrna said as she went through her papers again.

        “Will they take me to New York?”

        “No, they won’t take you to New York!”

        “Oh,” Benjamin paused. “So how can I get home.”

        “Well, you’re going to have to start by going through the forest. Is that a map you have?” Myrna pointed to Noel’s map in Benjamin’s hand. “Let me see it?”

        Myrna put on a pair of glasses and made disapproving facial expressions at the map.
