        Benjamin looked at himself and wondered how he had gotten himself into such a mess. Selma nearly pushed him to a glass window from where Benjamin could step outside onto the spherical glass.

        “I’ll hold onto the rope and as soon as you want to come back inside, just give it a good tug,” she said.

        The rope was attached to the top of the room by a pulley with one end connected to Benjamin and the other end connected to a wheel that looked like it belonged on an ocean ship. Selma used all of her weight to turn the wheel, giving Benjamin more rope with which he could step outside.

        “I really think--” he started to say.

        “Off you go!” Selma yelled with excited enthusiasm as she gave the wheel a full turn. Benjamin nearly fell outside the window with the sudden slack in the rope.

        The man in white stood without making a sound, adjusting his hat and cane every so often. His eyes focused on the small piece of dust that Benjamin was going to retrieve.

        Benjamin, for his part, couldn’t even see the dust from the window. It was so small he had no idea where it was. But as he leaned outside the window, he decided he would move in the general direction of the dust. Benjamin’s thoughts were as cloudy as the skyline in the distance. He couldn’t make any sense of what he was about to do. He also could not understand how Selma could have such a wide smile as she was currently wearing. With one more glance of disbelief, he turned and stepped onto the glass ceiling.

        It was worse than he expected. Outside of the glass skyscraper, it was windy, cold, scary, frightening, terrifying, excruciating, and traumatizing. Benjamin positioned his feet against the glass so he could walk down the side of the wall. As he started to walk down, he could see Selma and her big smile spinning the ship’s wheel as fast as she could. As she spun and spun, the man pointed his cane lower and lower, indicating that Benjamin needed to walk further.

        He never thought he’d be in this kind of situation and decided that he needed to find that piece of dust as fast as possible. This was worse than most of his nightmares.

        As he stepped lower and lower, he came within eyesight of where the man was pointing. Selma kept spinning and spinning. And as he tried to get closer to the glass to find the one spec of dirt that had soiled this otherwise perfect, pristine skyscraper he slipped.

        Selma stopped spinning.

        The man in white jolted forward.

        And Benjamin slammed into the side of the skyscraper.

        If it wasn’t painful, it was embarrassing. But with eyes now as close to the glass as they could be, he saw the spec of dust. He couldn’t believe it. It was smaller than he expected and absolutely impossible for the average person to see. He picked it up and showed it to Selma and the man in white who eagerly nodded their heads up and down. Benjamin put it in his pocket and Selma spun the wheel the opposite direction as quickly as she could.

Walking back into the glass sphere was a lot easier than walking out. Benjamin felt that way about most places, that it was a lot easier returning than it was going. But in this case, he was thousands of feet above the ground tied to a rope that was being controlled by his inexplicably happy classmate on the other side.

So when he got back inside the room, he felt nothing but accomplishment for having found the piece of dust.

“I’ve got it!” he yelled as he removed his harness.

        “I thought you were a goner,” Selma said with an expression that was much more worried than he had seen before.

        “I can’t believe it but I got it! Your castle is now clean of dirt.”

        Benjamin stepped forward and handed the spec of dust to the man in white. It looked like a tiny dot on his white gloves. The man removed his monocle and looked at it closely.

        “I cannot believe it,” he said. “I mean. Wow. Just wow. You really went out there and got this spec of dust?”

        “Yes, I did,” Benjamin said proudly.

        “I mean. That’s just nuts. Wow. I can’t believe you went out there. No one goes out there!”

        “No one?” Benjamin was confused at how shocked the man was.

        “No one! You’ve got to be insane to go out there! Everyone leaves. They all go back down the elevator and never come back.”

        “They leave?” Benjamin was even more confused as to why he did what he just did.

        “I mean. That was impressive! I didn’t think you’d be able to do it. Wow. You’re a really nuts kid. You were outside the window! You were thousands of feet in the air. That’s crazy, right? Crazy!”

        Benjamin crossed his arms and noticed Selma did the same. They were not excited by the man’s game that they had just played.

        “You mean I didn’t have to go outside to get the piece of dust?”

        “Well, I didn’t expect you to! I thought the two of you would leave!”

        “We didn’t know you were playing a game.”

        “Ah, yes,” he said. “Sorry about that.”

        “So can we see the travel agent now?”

        “Why of course! I mean, anyone that would go outside this room certainly needs a vacation. Anyone that comes up here just goes back down. They want to leave, especially if it means doing what you just did. You both need a vacation! You might be the first two to take a vacation since I’ve been here,” he said as he grabbed the doorknob behind him. “Here, go inside. The travel agent is inside. You can leave the boxes here.”

        Benjamin and Selma walked inside, exchanging annoyed glances with each other and the crazy man dressed in white.

        “Oops,” Selma whispered to Benjamin.

        “Yes,” Benjamin said. “Oops.”

        Seated at a small desk in this room made of black glass, Benjamin saw a woman who looked exactly like a peacock. Her hair was every color and extended as wide as the room. It was as brilliant and perfect as all of the glass castle. And as she raised her tiny head, Benjamin saw one of the prettiest women he had ever seen. She tilted her head to the side and slowly moved her lips.

        “Why hello you two and welcome to Dream Travels LLC,” she said as elegantly as one could say such words. “And, where would you like to go today?”

        “New York.”

Chapter 25: In Which There Is A Queen

        Castle Ehtsetra was silent. Benjamin knew that any people who had previously been stirring thousands of feet below had stopped. Nothing moved. Nothing made a sound. Except, that was, for the travel agent who tapped her pen on the nameplate on her desk. It read Lizette Gohara, Travel Agent of Dream Excellence. She tapped her named steadily. But, she ground her teeth with increasingly tense ferocity.

“He means he’d like to go to Castle Newer,” Selma said as she pushed Benjamin away.

        “That’s not what he said,” Lizette Gohara responded tersely. “He said he wanted to go to New York.”

        “I misspoke,” Benjamin said quickly. “I meant Castle Newer.”

        “No one misspeaks that eloquently,” Lizetta Gohara continued. “How do you know about this place, New York?”

        Lizette Gohara stood from her desk, the hair on her head touching three walls of the room. She leaned forward on her desk and brought her face within inches of Benjamin’s. Her eyes narrowed and Benjamin felt like she was trying to read his mind.

        “I don’t know,” Benjamin said. “It was a mistake.”

        “There are no mistakes,” Lizette Gohara said as she spaced out her words longer and longer. “There are only surprises. How do you know where New York is?”

        Benjamin did not know how to respond and so he looked to Selma for advice. But unfortunately, Lizette Gohara had her hand over Selma’s mouth. She could not help him now. Benjamin had to answer for himself.

        “Because, I want to go home.”

        Lizette Gohara stood back as quickly as she had moved forward. Benjamin did not want to lie. He knew lying was wrong. And, he was going to the travel agency so that he could find a way back home. If he lied, he could be further away from where he wanted to be. And so, Benjamin felt fine with answering the question as best as he thought he could answer it.

        “That’s where I’m from,” he added. “I’m from New York.”

        “Well,” Lizette Gohara said. “I’ve never met anyone from New York before. I mean, I’ve certainly heard of it. But, here you are standing before me, flesh and blood, a living New Yorker.”

        “He means Castle Newer,” Selma said as she moved Lizette Gohara’s hand away from her mouth. “He’s delusional and he doesn’t know where he needs to go.”

        “Oh, young girl. I think your friend knows exactly where he’d like to go. He’d like to leave this land. He’d like to go to New York.”

        “He says that but he doesn’t know where New York is.”

        “Well, regardless, I’m not going to be able to help you get to New York,” Lizette Gohara said as she moved around her desk to a large filing cabinet against a wall. “I can, however, offer you some fantastic prices on trips that have been extremely popular this year.” She turned her head to face both Selma and Benjamin. “Would you like to hear about them?”

        A chill ripped through Benjamin’s body as he feared what this woman was capable of doing.

        “Yes,” Selma and Benjamin said in unison.

        “Why that’s wonderful! Let’s start with the islands!”

        Lizette Gohara threw open a cabinet door and pulled out several posters featuring many islands. She danced around the room as a ballet dancer would move about a stage. She placed posters on every wall, posters of islands Benjamin had never seen before. He did not know such places existed.

        “Islands, you see, are beautiful places to be. You can escape. You can be alone. You can have your own personal, lovely prison-- I mean vacation! Vacation! What do you think? Shall we send the two of your to an island?” Lizette Gohara said as she once again leaned so close to Benjamin and Selma’s faces that Benjamin thought they would touch.

        “How would we get there?” Benjamin asked. “I don’t see any islands from here.”

        Lizette Gohara pretended to look through the window to see if she could identify any islands in the distance. Benjamin knew there were no islands because he could see everything when he was removing that small spec of dust.

        “No, you’re right. You cannot see any of the islands here. It’ll be a longer train ride and you’ll eventually have to take a boat. But, it’s quite safe and the boats haven’t sunk in many years. So what do you say, would you like to see the islands?”

        Benjamin knew he did not want to go to the islands. He wanted to go home and an island meant that he would be stuck somewhere else.

        “I don’t think I would do well on the islands.”
        “Don’t like the sun?”

        “I’m afraid of sharks.”

        “You don’t have to go in the water.”

        “I’ll probably go in the water.”

        “Don’t go in the water. There are sharks.”

        “Do you have anything on land?”
        Lizette Gohara tore down all the posters and danced back to the cabinet where she opened another shelf. This time, she began to place posters on the wall of beautiful mountain resorts with waterfalls that clung onto the sides of cliffs as they weaved through trees and grass.

        “If the islands aren’t to your liking, how about an escape to the mountains where there promises to be amazing wildlife, adventure, and certainly no sharks.”

        “That is much better, I suppose, because of there being no sharks,” Benjamin said.

        “So, then you’ll take it! I can book a trip for two to leave in an hour. Does that work? Would you like to spend your vacation in a place your friends will be jail, I mean jealous of. They’ll be jealous. I’m sure of it. So, two then?”

        “I think we want to go on a long train ride,” Selma said.

        “A long train ride?” Lizette Gohara asked with confusion.

        “Yes,” Selma said slowly. “Do you have any trips that go to many places in a short period of time?”

        “Well, I don’t know. All the trips I have ready to schedule go to one place. I mean, you’ll stay in one place. It’s not that they all go to the same place. That would be silly,” Lizette Gohara laughed loudly in a quite obnoxious way. “I don’t think I have any trips that would take you around from place to place. Why would you want such a thing?”

        Benjamin thought he knew what Selma was planning. If they travelled from place to place, eventually they would find an exit. He was beginning to question whether Lizette Gohara was telling the truth or not. He was beginning to think that she was not as real as he thought she might be. In fact, he began to wonder if she had an plan of her own.

        “We like to ride trains,” Benjamin said. “We’re not ones to stay still.”

        “Well, obviously not. I mean, you’ve presumably been to New York--”

        “Castle Newer,” Selma interjected.

        “I doubt it’s Castle Newer,” Lizette Gohara said slowly as her eyebrows started to narrow. “I doubt you have any interest in Castle Newer. No one wants to go to Castle Newer.”

Lizette Gohara was walking slowly to Selma, her arms at her sides like a preying mantis approaching a small insect.

“I think there’s something you two are trying to hide from me.”

She grabbed Selma by the shoulders and stared deep into her eyes. Benjamin did not know how to react. He stepped backward until he touched the wall. He wanted to help Selma but he didn’t know how.

“And you know what,” Lizette Gohara continued. “I don’t care.”

        “Why don’t you care?” Benjamin asked because he thought he could distract her.

        “Why don’t I care?” Lizette Gohara said as she grabbed Benjamin and pushed him into Selma’s shoulders. The two tried to free themselves but her strength was too much. “I don’t care because you two are going nowhere.”

        “Nowhere?”

        “Nowhere!”

        “But now that I think about it, the islands sound great,” Benjamin said quickly. “I can handle the sharks. I’ll just stay out of the water.”

        “You two will be going nowhere,” she said fiercely. “Well, that’s a lie, actually. Guards!”

        The door behind them burst open and dozens of men dressed in blue approached Benjamin and Selma. The guards grabbed their arms and legs to prevent them from moving. Benjamin felt himself being hoisted into the ground, unable to free himself of their grasps.

        “You’re both going to jail.”

        “Jail!” Benjamin yelled. “For what?”

        “For trespassing! You’re obviously not from here. And even worse, you might be from New York!”

        “For the last time, there’s nothing wrong with New York!”

        “Save it for the Queen. If you’re not from here, you’re a nightmare to deal with. And you, young lady,” she said as she turned to Selma. “I’m quite disappointed that someone of your upbringing would associate with someone like him. It’s quite shameful really. Don’t you know any other little boys your own age of your own kind? Take them away!”

        “Wait! We just want to leave the castle!”

        “Away! Away with them!”

        Benjamin and Selma were thrown into the elevator with the guards surrounding them. Not one of them made a sound as they descended to the ground. Benjamin was not sure where they were going but he knew that going to the travel agent was a bad idea. And unexpectedly, he saw in Selma’s expression that she must have also realized it was a bad idea. He thought he saw her start to cry but she turned her face away from him quickly.

        “We have to leave,” she said sternly.

        The guards didn’t move. They stared at the number of floors remaining. There were still over two-thousand left and they were passing three floor every second.

        “How?” Benjamin asked in an attempt to whisper. “We’re surrounded by guards.”

        “I don’t know,” Selma blurted out. “We’ll think of something but we cannot get in trouble here.”

        “Why? What’ll happen?”

        The guards all cleared their throats at once.

        “Let’s not talk about it,” Selma said as she sulked into the corner.

        For the first time since he saw her, Benjamin realized that Selma was capable of being defeated. She had always been so strong and forceful that he never imagined someone like her could also be vulnerable. It made him start to wonder if someone as scared and cowardly could be the opposite as well. And if Selma was feeling down at that moment, he knew that he had to be the one to bring her back. She had led him for so long. It was his turn.

        When the elevator reached the second floor, it stopped. Benjamin thought that certainly no one would try to get on this elevator. There was no room. And, no one was trying to get on. He, Selma, and the guards were all going to leave. The guards hurried them from the elevator and down a long hall to a dark purple glass room with a small sign that read Judgment Room. The guards shoved Benjamin and Selma into the empty room and then closed the door tightly. Benjamin heard three locks turn before he heard footsteps run away.

        “I know how we’re going to get out of here,” Benjamin said.

        He didn’t. But, he thought that if he convinced Selma that he had a plan, she would become less sad.

        “You don’t have plan,” she said.

        “What do you mean? I have a plan!”

        “No, you don’t. I can tell when you’re lying. Your eyebrows are always raised when you’re lying and your eyebrows are raised right now.”

        Benjamin paused for a second and shrugged his shoulders.

        “Maybe the plan was going to be amazing.”

        “You don’t have a plan.”

        Before he could respond, a television screen the size of one of the walls turned on and on it appeared a frail, skinny woman dressed in ornate white robes with a golden crown upon her head. She looked like she had just been woken from a nap and she moved her head and arms slowly. Benjamin thought she looked exactly like a sea turtle.

        “Are you the trespassers?” she asked.

        “No,” Benjamin answered. “We were here to book a vacation.”

        “But, we don’t book vacations to trespassers.”

        “We weren’t trespassing.”

        “Then, you would have been booked a vacation,” she said as she wiped her mouth with a fuzzy cloth. The video occasionally had static that caused the image to distort. “My name is Queen Sey Mour and I’m here to hand you your judgment.”

“But we haven’t done anything wrong,” Selma said sternly. “And, you haven’t listened to our story yet. You can’t judge us without knowing what our story is.”

“Selma, please,” Queen Sey Mour said. Benjamin looked at Selma, not realizing that the young girl might know the older Queen. “You should know better than to travel around with a nightmare of a boy.”

“He’s not a nightmare,” Selma protested.

“That’s not for discussion right now. We are here to discuss your punishment. And for that I decree that--”

“You can’t punish us without hearing our side of the story,” Selma protested.

        “Selma, I’ve got lots of day dreams to handle today. I cannot deal with your behavior right now. If you want me to tell your mother where you are, you should continue behaving badly. But if you want me to not mention anything to her, I suggest you keep your mouth shut.”

        “So it won’t be a bad punishment?” Benjamin asked.

        “For her, it won’t. For nightmares, it will.”

        “He’s not a nightmare,” Selma said as she stamped her foot on the ground.

        “I enjoyed hearing your story, Selma. Now, please quiet down.”

        Queen of Sey Mour adjusted her sunglasses and read from a bright white piece of paper handed to her from someone offscreen. Benjamin watched as this old lady squinted her eyes like she was trying to find the words on the paper.

        “In the complaint of trespassing on Castle Ehtsetra, Selma Applebaum receives a punishment of a day of community service,” the queen read.

        Benjamin didn’t think that the punishment was so harsh. Certainly, he wouldn’t mind doing some community service as well. And if it meant he could eventually leave the castle to find another path to leave, he was fine with this punishment. He didn’t know why he was so scared earlier.

        “And in the complaint of trespassing on Castle Ehtsetra and for being a nightmare, the nightmare will have his head chopped off.”

Chapter 26: In Which There Is A Door

        The television screen shut off immediately. Benjamin and Selma stood alone in the room, both not looking at each other. It could not be real, Benjamin thought to himself. He knew he was trapped in this room but there could not be any chopping of heads anywhere.

        “So,” Selma dragged the word out for a while. “That was a surprise.”

        “I’ll say,” Benjamin said. “You got a day of community service and I’m going to lose my head. That doesn’t seem fair.”

        “But you don’t want me to lose my head?”

        “No, I want a day of community service as well.”

        “Right. That would’ve been better.”

        “So what do we do now?” Benjamin asked as he realized this may be real.

        “The way I see it we have two options. You can lose your head or we’re going to have to escape.”

        “Or, I could convince them that I’m not a nightmare. How can I do that?”

        “That’s impossible. Once you’re called a nightmare, you’re stuck with it. The only way to convince anyone is to get King Bernard Zwirn to clear your name.”

        “So, escape?”

        “Do you want to lose your head?”

        “No. Let’s escape.”

        Dozens and dozens of guards dressed in blue stormed the room and took Selma and Benjamin away. There was no use struggling because they were outnumbered. Benjamin wondered how they were going to escape if they were constantly surrounded by so many people.

        They were rushed through a long wide glass room with doors at the end that reached to the ceiling. Benjamin could already see what was ahead through the glass. There was some sort of glass platform with a glass guillotine positioned on top. As he was pushed outside the skyscraper into the open air, he could see that there was indeed a machine ready to remove his head. The reality of the situation sunk in. Not only would he not be able to get back home, he would be losing his head in the process.

        “Selma, we have to do something!” Benjamin yelled as he was being dragged up glass stairs to the top of the glass platform. “Selma!”

        “I’m thinking, I’m thinking!” Selma yelled as she was taken to a viewing area at the base of the platform. She was chained to a chair and despite her struggles, she could not free herself. “Run away!”

        “Run? I can’t get myself free of their grips.”

        “Just run! I’ll be fine.”

        Benjamin squirmed back and forth as the only guard on the platform pushed him closer and closer to the guillotine.

        “It’s not working, Selma!”

        “Run! Or, jump! Any way you can to get out of here.”

        “This isn’t good!”

        Benjamin jumped and squirmed and attempted to run but in every attempt, he was being overpowered. The guard was too strong and Benjamin was too weak. He tried moving every part of his body but nothing could free himself.

        “Try harder!” Selma yelled as the guards tightened her chains to the chair.

        And then, Benjamin jumped and inadvertently hit his head straight into the guard’s head. Benjamin did not want to do this. It hurt. In his attempts to jump and move and free himself, it was an unavoidable collision. And despite the collision, the guard was physically uninjured. In fact, he was fine. But in the process of hitting the guard in the head, Benjamin knocked the man’s sunglasses off his head. That was when something peculiar happened. The guard froze, his eyes wide open, staring forward. He was still alive. He was breathing. It was just that he looked like he was in a trance. So at that moment, Benjamin was free, at least from that one guard.

        “The sunglasses!” Benjamin yelled to Selma. “Knock their sunglasses off their faces!”

        Selma only had one hand free as the guards continued to tie her to the chair. But with that one hand, she swiped at one of the guard’s faces and knocked his sunglasses to the ground. Immediately upon having the sunglasses removed, that guard too froze. And so, Selma swiped at the other guard who realized what had happened to his friend. He ducked away and continued to try to overpower Selma. But then, Benjamin ran down the stairs from the platform and hit his sunglasses onto the ground. The guard was stuck in a trance and Benjamin was able to release Selma from the chair as dozens of other guards descended upon them.

        One by one, Selma and Benjamin fought back against the men in blue suits. They ducked when the guards would try to grab them and then swung at their heads to remove their sunglasses. It was a fast, manic, panicked, energetic affair. Selma and Benjamin had knocked over forty sunglasses, leaving forty men staring into the distance. They didn’t flinch. They didn’t move. They just stayed in the position they were in when their sunglasses were removed.

        And after Selma and Benjamin surrounded the last guard, jumping at his head to unhinge his sunglasses, they sat in the middle of these people, exhausted and confused.

        “Good job,” Selma said as they sat with their backs to one another, worried that more guards would be on their way. “How did you know to remove the sunglasses?”

        “I didn’t,” Benjamin said as he scanned the horizon for more blue suits. “I accidentally knocked them off. I didn’t even want to. What happened to them?”

        Selma walked up to one of the guards and waved her hand in front of his eyes. He still didn’t move. He was as still as a statue.

        “They’re daydreaming,” Selma said.

        “Daydreaming?”

        “Yes. The sunglasses must prevent them from dreaming.”

        “So if they put the sunglasses back on, they’ll come back to attack us?”

        “I think so.”

        Benjamin jumped to his feet and gathered all of the sunglasses that had been strewn across the glass floor. When he had them all, he quickly broke each one of them into two pieces. This, he thought, would make them unusable to the guards. They could finally escape.

        “Let’s go!” he yelled to Selma as he grabbed her hand.

        They ran through a glass hallway, away from the guards.

        “We have to find the train that everyone takes when they start their holiday. The one that Lizette Gohara talked about. We’ll get on that train and leave the castle,” Selma said as they ran away, one pulling the other.

        As they turned a corner, a video screen appeared on the glass wall in front of them. It flickered briefly and then Benjamin saw the unmistakable image of Queen Sey Mour.

        “How dare you!” Queen Sey Mour yelled. “You stop running this instant!”

        Benjamin didn’t think twice. He grabbed Selma’s hand and pulled her along as they ran faster and faster. They moved through a glass maze in the castle’s plaza, searching for a train. As they turned a corner, the screen with Queen Sey Mour appeared again.

        “Do you think you’re going to leave?” she screamed. “You aren’t going to leave, nightmare.”

        They continued running, turning whenever they thought one path might be better than another. Despite the walls and everything around them being made of glass, it was still difficult to find a train in the distance. It was especially difficult when Queen Sey Mour continued to appear.

        “Nightmare, you will not destroy my castle,” Queen Sey Mour threatened.

Benjamin wished that he could explain to the woman that he was not a nightmare. But, this was not the time. He was not about to lose his head. He knew he needed to leave as quickly as possible. Another video screen appeared as Selma thought she saw the train preparing to depart.

“Selma! I’m informing your mother of your whereabouts!” Queen Sey Mour screamed. “We have fought the nightmares for a long time and they have finally been weakened! I will not have a nightmare in my castle destroyed dreams for innocent people.”

        It made Benjamin angry that Queen Sey Mour continued to refer to him as a nightmare. But, he kept his focus and continued to run faster, pulling Selma along even when she started to slow down.

        “There!” Selma yelled as a puff of smoke burst into the air above a train made of blue and red glass. “Over there!”

        They ran as the train started to lunge forward. One last screen appeared on the castle wall as Benjamin climbed the stairs on the side of the train.

        “Nightmare, don’t you ever return!” she exclaimed. “If you come back, you’ll lose more than your head.”

        The train moved forward and Benjamin pulled Selma up the staircase with all of his strength. As the train departed the castle, the two children sat next to each other, physically exhausted and mentally beaten down. Surely, Benjamin thought, Queen Sey Mour would one day learn that he was not a nightmare. And in order for that day to occur, Benjamin needed to leave this place. He needed to go back to New York. Because here, he realized, he could not explain himself to people who were not willing to listen to him.

        “Where does this go?” Benjamin asked Selma about the train.

        “I have no idea,” Selma said quickly. “We just needed to leave.”

        Benjamin went through his backpack and removed the map that had been given to him by Myrna Delacourte. It was worn now. But, the exit and several other key places were still clearly visible. Benjamin scanned the skyline to see in what direction they might be headed. Selma watched Benjamin struggle with reading the map. It was frustrating to Benjamin because he could not easily figure out where he was. He pulled on his hair and rotated the map back and forth, still unable to guess where the train was going. He threw the map into his backpack and threw his head upon his hands. It seemed like he would never get back home.

        Selma reached across Benjamin and took his backpack. She opened his map and looked at it briefly, sharing the same confused face that Benjamin had. Benjamin didn’t look up. He continued to sulk as he watched the ground move like a blur of color.

        “We’re here,” Selma said. “I’m pretty sure of it.”

        Benjamin turned his head to look in her direction.

        “Where?” he asked.

        “Here,” she said as she pointed at the map. “It’s not marked. Castle Ehtsetra isn’t marked. But, I’m pretty sure we’re here.”

        Benjamin moved next to her so that he could look at the map as well. He didn’t know if she was right but had a feeling that he should trust her. She knew a lot more than he did about this land.

        “So, we’re close to the exit,” he said as he pointed at the map.

        “Yes, it’s not too far away,” she said. “If we ride the train for a little bit longer, we’ll be able to get off and walk the rest of the way.”

        Benjamin felt a renewed sense of encouragement. Even if Selma was wrong, he was happy knowing that they had a plan. They would wait for the train to stop at the next station, and then they’d walk to the exit. If the exit wasn’t there, they would walk back to the train.

        When the train came to the station, Benjamin and Selma departed quickly, worried that there might have been other guards on the train. But as soon as they stepped from the train, it departed again, leaving them alone in a remote area. Birds flew from tree to tree while alligators roamed the stagnant water. It was an unlikely location for a train station because it did not seem like there was a castle nearby.

        Selma retrieved Benjamin’s map and located where the exit might be.

        “We have to hurry,” she said. “Because we don’t want to be here at night time.”

        “What happens at night time?” Benjamin asked.

        “We’re too close to Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle. If he wanted to unleash nightmares, we would be the first to get them. We don’t want to be here for that.”

        They walked along a thin dirt path that seemed to be the only evidence that people had been here before. As the sun continued to set, they picked up their pace and searched for the exit in the distance. Benjamin didn’t know what an exit would look like because he could imagine that this land simply ended with a wall. It had to be something else.

        As alligators snapped near their legs, Benjamin and Selma climbed over tree trunks and squeezed their way through thorny bushes to continue along. The path was becoming more muddy and with each step their shoes stuck to the ground. All of this, however, Benjamin was willing to endure because he was finally headed back to New York.

        In the distance, they saw it. It was a red barn in the middle of the swamp with large white lettering that read EXIT. A humungous yellow arrow pointed to the door. It was quite remarkable and felt oddly out of place. But Benjamin did not care what it looked like. So long as it was the exit, he was fine with it.

        As they approached the door, Benjamin looked at Selma and held out his hand.

        “Thank you very much,” he said as he waited for her to shake his hand. “Are you going to be able to get back alone?”

        He was confused why Selma didn’t shake his hand. She looked at him like he was behaving in some foreign manner. Maybe, he thought, she just didn’t like shaking hands. But Selma crossed her arms and began to narrow her eyebrows at Benjamin. He didn’t know why she was getting upset and so, he decided it was well enough that he should be on his way.

        “I really appreciate your help,” he said. “Take care.”

        As he turned to open the barn door, something was amiss. He didn’t know why but something felt wrong. He couldn’t put his finger on it. He had had an adventure. Perhaps, it was not the adventure that he had hoped for. But, it was an adventure and he had grown a little bit. He still didn’t feel as courageous as he would have liked to be. He did feel, however, that he had grown a tad more independent.

        He didn’t know what it was that didn’t feel right. But, he did know the door was locked.

        He pulled and pulled and listened to Selma laughing behind him.

        It was as locked as a vault.

        “You don’t have a key?” Selma asked with disbelief. “Didn’t whoever gave you the map to the exit also give you a key?”

        Benjamin felt defeated. He had come all this way. He had found the exit. And, he never thought the exit might require a key.

        “No,” he said. “I thought it would be open.”

        Selma laughed at his pitiful situation.

        “Don’t you think if the exit was open we’d have people always coming and going?” she asked with a giggle. “I can’t believe you don’t have a key!”

        “Where can I get a key?” he asked.

He was getting a little angry. He had prepared himself to leave and had not anticipated that his only place to depart might be locked. It was excruciatingly painful.

        “I only know one person that has a key,” Selma said calmly. “I don’t know how else you get a key. I thought you knew.”

        “Well, I thought that maybe it might be unlocked,” he said.

        Benjamin marched back the way they had come.

        “Where are you going?” Selma asked.

        “I’m going to get a key. I’m going to Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle.”

Chapter 27: In Which There Is Nightmare Castle

        That night, Benjamin and Selma walked further than Benjamin had ever walked in a day. He was determined to get to Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle and Selma was determined to make sure he did not get hurt along the way. She could barely keep pace with Benjamin he was moving as fast as his body could take him.

        “Slow down!” Selma yelled from behind. “There’s no rush.”

        “I want to go home,” Benjamin said.

        “I know you want to go home but whether you go home tonight or tomorrow or the next day or the day after that isn’t going to make a difference.”

        Selma was exhausted. She had been through so much with Benjamin and she did not have the same goal that he had. In fact, so long as Benjamin did not hurt himself, she achieved her goal.

        “I’m tired of being here and I want to go home. And if that means going into Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle to get a key, I’m going to get it.”

        Benjamin didn’t even notice how confident and courageous he had suddenly become. He was about to enter a castle that produced nightmares with the intentions of retrieving a key. It was not, he thought, going to be easy. But, he saw no other way to get home.

        “You’re going to get killed if you don’t stop and think for a moment.”

        “There’s nothing to think about anymore. I’m going to go into the castle. I’m going to find King Bernard Zwirn. I’m going to get the key. And then, I’m walking back to the exit in the swamp. And then, I’ll say goodbye to you again.”

        Selma didn’t want to stop Benjamin’s enthusiasm for getting the key. She knew that it was his only way home. King Bernard Zwirn was the only person who knew where Benjamin had come from. He was the only person that could actually send Benjamin home. But to get to King Bernard Zwirn in Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle was as dangerous as trying to spoonfeed a monster.

        “Is that it?” Benjamin pointed to a volcano in the distance that spewed lava thousands of feet into the air.

        Selma took one look and gave Benjamin a thumbs up.

        “Yep,” she said. “That’s Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle. I’ve never been there. I’ve only seen drawings. And it looks so much worse in person than it does in anything I’ve ever seen. You know, Benjamin. I wonder if there’s another way we can get you back home. Maybe we can go back to Castle Ehtahl and get the others. We’ll bring them all back and then we can all go in together.”

        Selma turned to face Benjamin and upon doing so, she noticed that he had already left and was walking down a hill to the castle that sat in the volcano a mile away. She let out a loud sigh and then ran to catch up with Benjamin. Benjamin was still so focused on finding an exit he did not consider the alternatives that might happen. His only alternative that he worried about was not getting home.

        “I’m going to go inside,” Benjamin said. “So you can wait outside if you want.”

        “If I want?” Selma asked with confusion.

        “Sure,” he said. “This is my problem. You don’t have to go inside if you don’t want to. It’s going to be dangerous and all.”

        “Benjamin, it’s going to be beyond dangerous. This is one of the worst places imaginable.”

        “So it’s not the worst place imaginable?”

        “Well, no. But any castle that produces nightmares is an awful place.”

        “There’s more than one?”

        “Oh yes,” Selma said. “There’s a dozen. They all surround a fortress in the middle some distance away.”

        “What’s in the fortress?”

        “Let’s not talk about it.”

        “OK, so do you have any recommendations for how I can get inside?”

        “Well, the first thing is that you should probably try not to get killed.”

        “OK, I’ll try not to get killed.”

        “And that’s about it. These nightmares are awful. It took our castles decades to keep all the nightmares away. They’ve been here for so long and have only recently started to attack us again. Fighting nightmares is one of the most difficult things I know of.”

        “So, no advice?”

        “I don’t have any,” she said as she threw her hands in the air. “If we knew how to destroy the nightmares, we would have done it already.”

        “So I’ll just try to stay alive.”

        “Yup,” she said. “Just try to stay alive.”

        They walked up the volcano, dodging lava and ash as it fell from the sky all around them. It started to get louder and noisier the closer they got to the walls, a sound that was similar to a boiling pot of water. The walls were darker and taller than any of the walls Benjamin had yet seen. They were dirty and smelly and covered with disgusting liquids that rolled down their sides. And unexpectedly, there was no door. There was no drawbridge or doorbell or small opening in which Benjamin could enter. It looked like the kind of place that did not let anything inside leave.

        Benjamin could hear the sounds of screaming and yelling as he approached the rocky exterior of a wall.

        “Get back!” Selma yelled as she pulled him behind a piece of cooled lava. “They’re going to see you.”

        “Who?” Benjamin asked as he ducked near Selma.

        At that moment, three screeching dragons the size of buses flew overhead. Benjamin could see fire in their eyes and their talons looked like they could break anything with ease. They flew around in a pattern like they were searching for something inside the castle. The screams grew louder as the dragons hissed and snarled at something on the other side.

        “We have to climb the wall,” Selma said to Benjamin. “But only once the dragons disappear.”

        “We?” Benjamin asked her.

        “You think I’m going to let you go in there and die? Do you know how much work it’ll be for me to explain to everyone what happened to you?”

        “Which wall?”

        “That one,” Selma said as she pointed to a wall that had more darkness upon it than the others.

        As more dragons soared around the castle, Benjamin and Selma sprinted to the wall. A glass wall would have been difficult to climb. But this wall was rather easier because it had been damaged so many times by falling lava. And Benjamin was beginning to think that the walls weren’t built so that they could keep people out. They had been built to keep the nightmares inside.

        They climbed the wall, rocks slipping underneath them as they went higher. Benjamin noticed that he was further up than Selma and so, he stopped and held his position. He didn’t want to be in a place where he couldn’t help her if she needed it. When Selma got to his spot, they climbed side by side until they reached the top.

        And at the top, Benjamin saw the worst sight he had ever seen. On the other side of the wall was the largest army Benjamin had ever seen. Aloysius Trenhaile was preparing for war. He was going to attack Castle Ehtahl.

        Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle was littered with broken houses made of rock that lined lava rivers. There were rusty military vehicles that looked like they had been inspired by porcupines, spikes coming out of every side. There were weapons that seemed large enough to destroy any castle Benjamin had seen. And throughout, there were trolls who grunted and growled at each other. There were more skeletons than Benjamin could count on the far east end of the castle. And when one of them moved, Benjamin’s stomach turned. There were ghosts scattered throughout and awful creatures that Benjamin could not name everywhere. They looked like the horrifying creatures that only a nightmare could produce. It was worse than Benjamin imagined.

        “Now what?” he said to Selma.

        “Stay alive,” she said calmly. “The key is going to be with King Bernard Zwirn. And, he’s probably held captive in that tower.”

        In the center of the castle was a tower that even lava could not destroy. It had a staircase that wrapped around its exterior dozens of times before it reached the top. The dark, dirty exterior made it almost invisible against the night sky. If it wasn’t for the large fire at the top, Benjamin was sure he would have missed it.

        “We just have to get to the top somehow,” Benjamin said to Selma.

        He scanned the castle for an easy path to the tower but it was difficult to find given the darkness. The stairs were the most obvious choice, he thought. But, he would probably be seen. If there was a way he could disguise himself, he could walk through unseen.

        As he was going to whisper his plan to Selma, the three dragons suddenly appeared on the other side of the castle walls. They stared at Benjamin and Selma who were only ten feet away. Benjamin could feel the searing hot air the dragons were exhaling. They were doomed, he thought.

        One of the dragons grabbed Selma and flew into the darkness. Benjamin tried to reach for her but it was too late. The other two dragons grabbed Benjamin and flew him across the castle and above the lava river. He was certain that he was going to die at that moment. The dragons would tear him to pieces. It was a dreadful situation and Benjamin did not know how to free himself.

        He wished that he could fall. If he was so hot or so cold that he would hurt the dragons, they would drop him. Or, if he was made of spikes or if he was slippery, they would drop him. Or, if he was extremely heavy or big or tiny or unseen, they would drop him. And at that moment, all he wanted was to be dropped, safely and not torn to pieces.

        He closed his eyes and imagined what it would be like to be all those things that the dragons couldn’t hold. And suddenly and unexpectedly, he opened his eyes and found himself in a freefall. There was not much distance between him and the ground but with lava everywhere, he was still concerned. Luckily, he fell directly into the back of a cart filled with coal.

        “Selma!” he yelled into the empty darkness.

        The cart jolted forward and Benjamin hid among the coal. The army was much larger than Benjamin had guessed. He looked ahead and noticed that he was only a short distance away from the tower. But he also noticed that the cart was headed directly for the staircase that ran along the tower. As it approached, Benjamin saw that the disgusting troll that was pulling the cart was going to attempt to pull the cart up the staircase.

        The troll pulled the cart up one step and Benjamin was jostled back and forth. He did not like being thrown about in such a violent way. The troll pulled the cart up another step and Benjamin hit his head against the iron wall of the cart. And then another step and Benjamin hit his back against the coal. There were hundreds of stairs and if the troll was going to continue to pull the cart this way, Benjamin thought he would be unconscious before he arrived.

        He imagined what it would be like if there were no steps going up but instead it was a smooth ride all the way to top. It would be a gentle ride and the troll could go a little faster. And when he got to the top, Benjamin could still have his consciousness. When he stopped imagining what such a ride would be like, he opened his eyes and realized that he was at the top of the tower. The sight baffled him. Although the tower looked high from the ground, it felt much taller here. And, he could see the full violence and size of the volcano. It was dreadful and around it, thousands of beasts prepared for battle.

        Benjamin waited for the troll to leave and then he snuck into the tower’s square room where a large fire burned at the top. As soon as he entered, he heard a familiar voice that he had not heard from for a really long time.

        “Benjamin?” King Bernard Zwirn asked.

The king was seated in an iron cage stuck in the air. Although it hadn’t been a long time since Benjamin had last seen him, he looked remarkably older and weaker. Benjamin knew the king was in trouble. There was no one else in the room. There was just a gigantic fire and a loud, vibrating machine in the middle.

“Benjamin! What are you doing here?”

“It’s a long story but I’m trying to leave,” Benjamin whispered. “And I need a key to leave.”

“I’m sorry I couldn’t get you out earlier, Benjamin. I didn’t expect things to go this direction. And you can’t stay here. I don’t know how you got in but you’re in a lot of trouble. If my brother finds you, you’re going to be in a lot of trouble.”

“Your brother?”

“Yes, my brother.”

“Your brother is Aloysius Trenhaile?”

The fire roared and lightning struck the tower. The demons, ghosts, and horrid creatures all screamed in unison at the base of the castle.

“Benjamin, you cannot say that name!”

“Where is he?”

“He’s coming back. He’s making nightmares. Benjamin, you should probably leave. I don’t know that you’ll be able to help me. You just have to tell someone that I’m still alive.”

“I’ll tell Selma,” Benjamin said.

“Selma’s with you? Yes, I got kicked out of Castle Ehtahl by Thalia Nachamie.”

“I thought Thalia Nachamie might have taken control. It’s not good times for dreaming, Benjamin. Dreams may soon come to an end. So, you should leave. If my brother finds you, he’s going to try to hurt you.”

        There was another roar in the distance.

        “King Zwirn, how can we destroy the nightmares?”

        “We’ve never been able to figure it out, Benjamin. If we can stop this machine here, we’ll be able to temporarily stop their production. But so long as there are dreams, there are bound to be people who want to create nightmares.”

        “So if I turn off this machine, I’ll have stopped the nightmares.”

        “Yes, but we don’t know how to turn it off. My brother is the only person who knows.”

        “What can I do?”

        “I don’t think anything. You don’t have much time. You’re in real danger. The key is on the other side of the room and you need to get it quickly before my brother returns.”

        Benjamin looked and spotted the small silver key on the other side of the room. He ran to the wall and climbed an iron ladder that led to the ceiling. With one hand after another, Benjamin imagined scaling the ladder faster than he felt he was capable of moving. When he arrived at the top, he grabbed the key and could hear King Bernard Zwirn applauding on the other side. Benjamin turned and saw the largest smile he had ever seen the king wear. But Benjamin did not realize what he had done. He had simply climbed the ladder. And now, he could finally leave.

        “Bravo, Benjamin!” King Bernard Zwirn yelled. “Now, leave! Go find someone who can help save me!”

        Without thinking, Benjamin ran down the ladder as quickly as he had climbed up it. He hit the ground and held the key out for King Bernard Zwirn to see.

        “I don’t know how you got in here, Benjamin,” King Bernard Zwirn said. “But if there’s anyone who knows how to escape, it’s probably you. Trust your own instincts and tell everyone that I’m still alive.”

        “So long, King Zwirn,” Benjamin yelled in response. “It was great to meet you.”

        “Bye, Benjamin. I hope you can continue dreaming.”

        Benjamin turned to leave and immediately upon trying to exit, Aloysius Trenhaile appeared.

Chapter 28: In Which There Is A Nightmarer

        He was much taller than Benjamin expected. His body was thin like a crane. He stood like a young tree with branches arms that stretched outward like crooked branches. His fingers extended outwards like long, narrow daggers. His elbows, knees, and shoulders were sharp, not smooth like a normal person’s. His feet were narrow and long while his ears were wide and short. His nose arched forward like a parrot’s nose and his eyes sunk into his face like coals on a beach. And as he walked toward Benjamin, he moved like a sly fox stalking his prey.

        “So, this is the one?” Aloysius Trenhaile asked King Bernard Zwirn amid lightning and thunder. “You told me I’d never come upon him. That he’d come upon me. And with what luck, here he is. What is your name, child?”

        Benjamin hadn't moved. He didn’t know how to interact with this man that had been so feared by so many. This man was responsible for destroying dreams in the castles and he had an army ready to destroy dreams forever. He was the reason dreams were disappearing in New York.

        “Leave the boy alone!” King Bernard Zwirn yelled from the cage. “He causes you no harm. Let him be.”

        Aloysius Trenhaile walked around Benjamin several times, his legs taking long strides. His hands were behind his back. Benjamin felt like the man was going to grab him if he tried to flee.

        “Bernard, that can’t happen,” Aloysius Trenhaile said calmly. “Any child that comes to my castle surely is not worthy of letting go free. Why is he here, Bernard?”

        “He was just leaving, Aloysius! Let him be.”

        “But why leave now? Don’t you want to see the release of my greatest creation yet? I was just about to create a nightmare’s nightmare. Stick around, boy.”

        Chains burst from the ground and wall. They wrapped themselves around Benjamin’s arms and legs so quickly that Benjamin didn’t have any time to react. The rusty chains pulled Benjamin into the air next to King Bernard Zwirn.

        “You can stay there,” Aloysius Trenhaile said with an annoyed, calm voice. “You’ll be witness to something that will change human history. This will revolutionize the way people live. This will change the way people think. For too long, there has been a divide between the people who can dream and those who cannot. But, nightmares do not discriminate. Nightmares affect everyone. And tonight, this machine will make sure that no one dreams. The dreamers will stop dreaming and be just like the people who are unable to dream.”

        “I don’t understand,” Benjamin said meekly.

        “What don’t you understand. Nightmares are fair. Dreams are unfair. Not everyone can dream, boy.”

        “Why don’t you make dreams for the people who cannot dream?”

        Aloysius Trenhaile let out a long, loud laugh that caused the fire at the top of the room to roar. Benjamin tried to avert his eyes as lava fell throughout the room from the volcano outside.

        “You assume that everyone wants to dream!” Aloysius Trenhaile screamed.

        “Everyone wants a dream,” Benjamin replied without thinking that responding might make the situation much worse.

        “No!” Aloysius Trenhaile exclaimed. “Everyone does not want a dream! Lots of people want to live life without a dream! The dreamers always think that everyone should have a dream. But, they’re wrong! And for that, boy, the dreamers will be punished! The dreamers will be nightmarers!”

        “Nightmarers?”

        “Yes! They will no longer have dreams but nightmares!”

        “But, that’s not even a word.”

        King Bernard Zwirn put his finger to his lips and shook his head back and forth quickly.

        “No, Benjamin. Don’t say that,” King Bernard Zwirn whispered to Benjamin.

        “Nightmarers is now a word. I invented it. It means a dreamer who only has nightmares!”

        Benjamin didn’t understand what had led Aloysius Trenhaile to come to this conclusion. If there were no dreamers, the world would be a sadder place, he thought. It would be filled with people who just did what they were told, people who did not think beyond what they saw, people who did not care about creativity, people who did not try to stretch their minds, people who were insecure, people who were afraid of being different, people who were exactly the same as everyone else. It seemed to be an awful place. And, it was certainly a place Benjamin did not want to live. He wanted dreams.

        “Bring in the catalyst!” Aloysius Trenhaile yelled as he inspected the complicated nightmare machine in the center of the room.

It was made of many electrical parts Benjamin could not identify. It looked so much more complicated than the dream machine in Cafe Ehtahl. From four doors on all sides of the room, demons entered with various pieces of equipment. They began to plug cords into the nightmare machine and pull levers that sent sparks flying into the air. The nightmare machine was slowly coming to life.

“Oh, one more thing, Bernard,” Aloysius Trenhaile said amid the chaos of the awful creatures running around. “We have the girl, too.”

“Selma!” Benjamin yelled.

“Aloysius, you let her go! She’s here to do no harm!” King Bernard Zwirn yelled back.

“I don’t know why she’s here. I assume she’s here to save you. But, we both know you can’t be saved,” Aloysius replied.

Trolls entered and began putting the finishing touches on the nightmare machine, which started to make lots of noise and generate more sparks. Every so often, a spark would explode so much that it looked like a firework. To Benjamin, the nightmare machine looked like it was going to explode. Even the demons and trolls and other disgusting beasts on the floor began to look at it with fear. Some slowly backed away and ran down the exterior staircase while others admired the lights and noises with amazement. Benjamin and King Bernard Zwirn continued to avert their eyes. It was too bright to look directly at and too loud to hear.

“Benjamin, you have to get out of here,” King Bernard Zwirn said.

Benjamin looked at the chains that held him in the air. He jostled his body back and forth but could not free himself.

“How?” Benjamin asked. “I’m stuck.”

“How did you get to this castle? How did you get up this tower? How did you climb that broken ladder to get that key? That ladder only goes halfway up the wall but you somehow managed to climb a ladder all the way to the top.”

Benjamin looked across the room and noticed that the ladder did indeed stop halfway up the wall. But, that wasn’t what he remembered. He remembered climbing a ladder all the way to the top. In fact, he was sure a ladder went all the way to the top because he wouldn’t have been able to climb it otherwise. And yet as he looked across the room, the ladder definitely stopped well short. Maybe, he thought, he imagined it. Maybe that was why King Bernard Zwirn was clapping as loudly as he was. Maybe it was all in Benjamin’s mind.

“You can free yourself, Benjamin. You’re the only one who can. You just have to imagine yourself being freed,” King Bernard Zwirn whispered. “I believe you can do it.”

Benjamin didn’t understand what the king meant. He didn’t try to create a ladder that extended all the way to the top of the ceiling. He didn’t try to move the troll and the coal cart from the bottom of the tower to the top. He didn’t try to do anything. They just sort of happened. How could I try to imagine something so creative, he thought.

His mind started to wonder as he watched pieces of lava fly into the room through the open roof above. He wondered how it was possible that he hadn’t been hit by lava yet. He was glad he hadn’t been hit by lava because that surely would have hurt. But with all of the pieces falling into the room, it was surprising that nothing hit him, King Bernard Zwirn, or the nightmare machine that Aloysius Trenhaile continued to work on. If only a piece of lava would fall through the ceiling and hit the iron chains, Benjamin would be free. He imagined how it would be, a small piece of lava moving so fast that it would melt the chains instantly and let him free.

And the next thing he realized, he was on the ground.

Aloysius Trenhaile turned to face Benjamin, his face as angry and upset as a face could make. He started to march toward Benjamin but Benjamin closed his eyes and imagined that lava was hailing down on the nightmare machine. Aloysius Trenhaile screamed and roared loudly. Benjamin opened his eyes to find that the machine had been hit by lava several times. Trolls and demons ran back into the room. They desperately tried to control the melting structure and fire that had started on the machine.

“You are going to die!” Aloysius Trenhaile screamed at Benjamin.

Benjamin moved backwards and looked up to King Bernard Zwirn.

“You did it! Leave!” the king yelled. “Go! Hurry! Find Selma!”

Benjamin turned and ran down the exterior of the tower, listening to the king shout instructions to him as he moved.

 “That will stop them for now. Go find Selma and tell the others that I’m alive! They must come at once to free me. It will take all the dream castles to destroy this castle but we must do so before Aloysius has an opportunity to create this nightmare’s nightmare.”

He didn’t know where Selma might be. All around him, the awful creatures of Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle began to stir with confusion as to what was happening at the top of the tower. It was chaos and amid it all, Benjamin yelled for Selma wherever he could. The last thing he remembered was that she was taken away by a dragon. So if he found a dragon, he could find Selma.

In the sky, there was a dragon in the distance and Benjamin watched where it was headed. As trolls and skeletons climbed the tower, Benjamin proceeded to descend and follow where the dragon went. As it neared the castle, it changed directions quickly to fly toward the tower. And as it flew up the tower, Benjamin saw the other two dragons leave a destroyed house near the lava river.

He ran as quickly as he could and crossed a terribly hot bridge over the lava. Without thinking, he busted down the door. But there was no monster, only Selma and her foot chained to the ground. Without thinking, Benjamin imagined the roof being pulled off the house and a small piece of lava melting the chain. When he opened his eyes, he saw that the roof was gone, the iron chain had been cut, and Selma had a shocked expression on her face.

“We have to hurry!” Benjamin yelled to her.

She still didn’t move so Benjamin grabbed her arm and led her through the destroyed castle and onto the bridge over the lava river. They ran among the chaos of trolls and ghosts trying to make their way up to the tower. At the top, Benjamin could see that the fire was raging more and more. He worried about King Bernard Zwirn but he knew he had his instructions. He had to get help.

“What happened?” Selma yelled as they ran further.

“Aloysius Trenhaile created a nightmare machine that can create a nightmare’s nightmare.”

“A what?”

“A nightmare’s nightmare. It’s a nightmare that will stop everyone from dreaming. There would be no more dreamers. Only nightmarers.”

“That’s not a word.”

“I tried to tell him but he wouldn’t listen.”

“So we have to stop it!” Selma yelled.

“I did!” Benjamin replied. “I don’t know exactly how but lava melted parts of it. They can’t use it. It’s broken.”

“Did you find King Zwirn?”

“Yes, I did. He’s up there in the tower. I got the key and then Aloysius entered and started the nightmare machine. I was chained to the wall and I imagined lava destroying the machine and setting me free. And then, I realized I was free. Aloysius is really angry right now. We have to leave before he finds me or else he’ll kill me.”

“Wait! Wait. I’m confused. Why didn’t you set King Zwirn free too?”

Benjamin paused for a moment while they were running to think. He could have set King Zwirn free but that wasn’t what King Zwirn told him to do. He told Benjamin to leave and get help. And, that’s what Benjamin was going to do.

“He told me to leave and get help. He said that I should let everyone know that he is still alive. Everyone needs to come back and battle this castle,” Benjamin said to Selma.

She didn’t look pleased with his response but continued to sprint for the wall.

“So he wants us to get help?”

“Yes, he said get the other castles to free him. I guess he thought that Aloysius could only be defeated by the castles.”

At that moment, the fire at the top of the castle exploded into a large fireball that forced both Benjamin and Selma to turn away. He saw demons and ghosts and skeletons falling off the staircase that surrounded the tower. If they did not move more quickly for the exit, Aloysius may find them.

Benjamin and Selma reached the wall and climbed it as fast as they could. At the top, Benjamin reached into his pocket and tightened a fist around the key. It was still there. King Bernard Zwirn was still at the top of the tower. But now, Benjamin could make sure that everyone knew he was still alive. Selma knew and when Selma went back to Castle Ehtahl, she could tell everyone. They would all come back and set the king free. He would be safe.

And for that night, there would still be dreamers because Benjamin had damaged the nightmare machine. Aloysius Trenhaile could not execute his plan without fixing it first. When the castles free King Bernard Zwirn, the king should be able to lead everyone in defeating Aloysius Trenhaile for good.

This was good, Benjamin thought. He could finally go home to New York.

He nodded as he looked as the disaster before him and then climbed down the other side of the wall. When he got to the bottom, he assisted Selma in safely touching ground. But unexpectedly, Selma didn’t share the same happy emotion that he had.

And, he didn’t know why.

Chapter 29: In Which There Is A Realization

        Benjamin was ecstatic. He had done it. He had the key. He had done something that he never imagined he was capable of doing. And now, he could leave. He could exit this awful land that had been nothing but difficult and painful. He wanted to go home because although home didn’t have any friends or dreams, he was not under attack.

        He didn’t realize how fast he was walking away from the castle. As excited as he was, he felt as if he was flying. He moved along the land so quickly that he was far ahead of Selma who was only steps outside of the castle. Benjamin turned and started walking backwards so that he could see her.

        “We did it!” he yelled to her. “I’m going home!”

        He turned around and continued to move faster and faster. After everything he had gone through, events had turned in his favor.

        “What is wrong with you!” Selma screamed.

        She had her arms stretched as wide as they could extend and her head was pushed forward as far as it could go. Benjamin had not yet seen her this angry. She looked as if he had done something terrible.

        “Nothing,” Benjamin said warmly. “Nothing’s wrong with me. I’m really happy.”

        “Are you nuts!”

        “No, look I have the key.”

        “Oh my--,” Selma started to say but stopped and paced back and forth. Benjamin watched her pace and grunt loudly with frustration and annoyance.

        “Why are you so angry?”

        “Are you serious!”

        He didn’t know what to ask next. He needed to figure out what was wrong with Selma but he wasn’t sure how to get her to tell him.

        “So,” he began. “I’m a little confused why you’re so upset.”

        “You’re confused! Great! You’re confused!”

        “Yes, so, you could, you know, tell me why you’re so upset? That might be, well, nice.”

        Selma stopped pacing in front of Benjamin. Benjamin was sure she was going to hit him at that moment.

        “You are being so selfish. You don’t understand why I’m upset because you’re being so selfish!”

        “I don’t understand--”

        “I know!”

        “Well, I don’t understand because I’m here to find the key so that I can go home. That is selfish, yes. But, isn’t that what I’m here to do?”

        “It is, Benjamin. It is. You’re right.”

        “So,” Benjamin said quietly. “I’m going to continue walking.”

        “What about King Zwirn?” Selma called out to Benjamin as he walked away.

        “What about him?” Benjamin answered without pausing his pace.

        “You could save him,” she stated as a matter of fact.

        “I could save him?” Benjamin said as he stopped. “Selma, did you see that monster? There is absolutely no way I can save him. Someone bigger than me, maybe. Not me. I’d be killed instantly.”

        “Then what happens to him?” Selma asked as Benjamin again continued to walk.

        “I don’t know,” he said because he honestly didn’t know.

He did not want King Zwirn to be hurt, to be imprisoned, or to be alone. But, he did not know what he could do to save him. That monster, Aloysius Trenhaile, was bigger, meaner, and tougher than anything Benjamin could ever dream of being. There was no way that Benjamin could save King Zwirn. If he tried, he risked causing more harm to the king. And certainly, Benjamin thought, Selma would not want that.

“King Bernard Zwirn didn’t ask me to save him,” Benjamin said.

“Why did he need to ask?” Selma responded.

        If they were going to walk back to Castle Ehtahl, he had to think of a plan for saving King Zwirn that would make Selma happy. Benjamin worried that she would run back into the castle and try to save him. If Benjamin could not save the king, Selma could not save the king either.

        “I have a plan,” Benjamin said as he quickened his pace.

        “What is this plan?” Selma said with an upset tone.

        “We’re going to go back to the castle and we’re going to tell everyone that we found King Zwirn. Then, we’ll bring back everyone so that we can all fight Aloysius Trenhaile together.”

        He was satisfied with this plan because it made sense to him. He alone could not beat Aloysius Trenhaile but perhaps he and an army could defeat the monster and its army. Even a monster as gargantuan as Aloysius Trenhaile would have difficulty fighting thousands of people. This was, Benjamin decided, a good plan. And, he thought to himself, it meant that he could still go home while knowing that he did his best to help King Zwirn.

        “That won’t work,” Selma said. She still had not moved and the gap between Benjamin and Selma grew larger and larger.

        “Why not? How do you know?”

        “It’s not going to work because no one in the castle is going to leave. They are too scared of that of which we do not talk about.”

        “Who?”

        “Aloysius Trenhaile.”

        “Oh, well, I suppose it might not work. That’s a possibility. But, it’s a better possibility than me going back into that castle and dying because I tried to destroy a monster five thousand times my strength.”

        Selma didn’t respond. She leaned her weight on her right hip and stared into the sky. Benjamin took one glance and thought he saw her muttering something. He couldn’t understand what she was saying. And, he couldn’t understand why it was so important that he save King Zwirn. Certainly, she did not know Benjamin nearly as well as Benjamin thought he knew himself.

        Benjamin continued to walk and felt as if he was making really good time. At this rate, he could get back to the castle in just two days. It would be a difficult two days, he thought to himself, because it would probably be exhausting. But with the key, he thought, I’ve got all the motivation I need.

        At the same moment Benjamin thought about how the key was motivating him to run back to the castle, Selma sprinted the distance between the two of them and then tackled Benjamin from behind. Benjamin flew about ten feet into the air and then fell into the ground, the key flying into the air. He was more surprised than hurt. In fact, Selma had tackled him in such a way that he was completely uninjured. He was simply shocked.

        “What are you doing?” he asked in surprise.

        Selma stood and pinned him to the ground. She held his arms down on his side and stared straight into his eyes.

        “You are going to save the king,” she said sternly.

        “Don’t you think you should? You’re obviously stronger than I am,” Benjamin said as he tried to wriggle free. It could not be done. Selma was definitely stronger and tougher than he was.

        “No, you are going to do it. I didn’t come this far so that we can go back without the king. You are going to save him.”

        “Why me? Why not you?”

        “Because I can’t.”

        “Why can’t you?”

        “Because,” Selma started as she closed her eyes. “I’ll watch your back.”

        He knew that she was not telling him everything that was running through her head. And, he also knew that he could not expect to make any further progress toward getting back to Castle Ehtahl. Selma was not going to allow it.

        “Fine,” Benjamin gulped. “I’ll go die trying to save King Zwirn if that’s what you want.”

        “That’s what I want,” Selma said as she released the boy. “But, you know, without the part of you dying. Please don’t die in the castle. Don’t die, in general. But, you know, please don’t die while you’re trying to save the king.”

        “I don’t know how I’m going to survive,” Benjamin said.

        “Just do your best,” Selma said.

        “Selma, that’s not inspiring. I don’t know what that means. I’m really scared.”

        “You should be scared. Aloysius Trenhaile is a gigantic monster.”

        “Right! That’s why I don’t want to go see him.”

        “I know,” Selma said with a more understanding tone. “I wouldn’t want to either. But trust me, Benjamin. If you save the king, you’ll be saving yourself.”

        Benjamin and Selma walked back to Aloysius Trenhaile’s castle without saying a word to each other. Benjamin’s pace was much slower and much less enthusiastic than when he thought he was leaving. For Selma, he decided, he would save King Zwirn. If this was what she wanted and this was what would allow him to go home, this was what he would do.

        He stood in front of the castle door that they had only recently exited and took a deep breath.

        “If you need me, I’ll be right here,” Selma said as she straightened her clothes and readjusted her backpack.

        “Thanks,” Benjamin replied.

        “Good luck. And, don’t die.”

        “OK,” Benjamin said as he lowered his head and walked through the door. He would not have bet on him being the winner of this outcome. As far as Benjamin was concerned, he was walking to the end of his life.

Chapter 30: In Which There Is A Battle

        Benjamin climbed over the wall and then down the other side, without the same enthusiasm he had when he first entered the castle. He sighed when he saw that the army had erupted into all out frenzy. Skeletons were losing limbs. Trolls were stumbling over minotaurs. Ghosts were scaring each other. Dragons were flying into one another. And, lava was falling everywhere. Benjamin took a deep breathe and then let all the air out of his body through his vibrating lips. He was not excited, at all.

        He walked through the mayhem and screams and yelling to the start of the staircase. Selma waited outside the castle and as Benjamin scaled the stairs, he saw her. She was watching his every move. And when Benjamin paused to take a break, he saw her waving to him. He waved back as a headless horseman ran by and fell off the staircase into the coal pile below. Benjamin continued his journey upwards as if nothing surprised him anymore.

        When he got to the top, he could see that the nightmare machine had melted thoroughly enough to render it unusable. But, parts of it were still functioning and it looked like it was going to explode. Aloysius Trenhaile was giving orders to all of the beasts around him to save the machine.

        “Don’t turn it off!” he screamed. “Keep it running and save every part!”

        “Aloysius!” Benjamin heard King Bernard Zwirn yell. “You have to stop this immediately. This is no way to behave, brother.”

        “Quiet!” Aloysius yelled. “If this doesn’t work tonight, it’ll work tomorrow. And, you’ll witness it then!”

        At that moment, Benjamin pushed open the large door to the room which created a slow squealing noise that grabbed everyone’s attention. In fact, as soon as Benjamin stood inside, he saw that every creature was looking at him. Aloysius Trenhaile dropped a box of tools on the ground upon seeing the young child.

        “Really? You again? You came back? Did you drop something that you came back for?” Aloysius Trenhaile asked. “You have to be so stupid in order to come back here. I let you free. I didn’t chase after you. And now, what? What do you want?”

        Benjamin paused and twisted his foot into the ground. He let out a long sigh and thought really hard about why he had returned.

        “Oh you must be kidding me,” Aloysius Trenhaile said with a chuckle. “You’re here because you want to stop me.”

        Benjamin continued to twist his foot in the ground and then he began stretching his arms. He wasn’t sure what was going to happen next. Benjamin had never fought anyone in his life. He never wanted to fight anyone. It was not in his character. Through his entire life to date, he had always received the insults and punches. He never delivered them. And so, he didn’t quite know what to do.

        “Aloysius Trenhaile!” Benjamin yelled. “Stop the nightmares now!”

        Aloysius Trenhaile laughed. There was a long silence And then, all of the beasts around him laughed. And then, all of the beasts and nightmares throughout the castle laughed. But there were two people other than Benjamin who were not laughing. King Bernard Zwirn looked scared for Benjamin. And upon looking outside, Selma was still waving.

        “Child, leave now before you get hurt,” Aloysius Trenhaile said. “I don’t think you know what you’re getting yourself into.”

        “You’re right,” Benjamin said. “I don’t know what I’m getting myself into. But, I know that I want you to stop what you’re doing.”

        “And what if I don’t?”

        “Then I’m going to have to stop you.”

        The roars of laughter spread throughout the castle over and over. Benjamin did not look like a threat. He knew this. He knew this his entire life. But all of that perception was going to change. If Aloysius Trenhaile was not going to stop, Benjamin wanted to stop him.

        “Alright everyone,” Aloysius Trenhaile said to all the beasts. “Let’s get back to saving this nightmare machine. Cool the rest of the melting sections and then--”

        Aloysius Trenhaile continued to give instructions to his followers as Benjamin continued to stand there. Benjamin turned to King Bernard Zwirn and saw that he did not look as scared as he did moments before. Instead, the king clench his fist and held it in front of him to give Benjamin his sign of support. And so, Benjamin decided that it was time for him to take things into his own hands. Because if he was going to get hurt, he was willing to get hurt knowing that he could save dreamers like himself everywhere.

        He closed his eyes, took a deep breath, and upon opening his eyes watched a gigantic lava ball smash into the nightmare machine destroying everything that Aloysius Trenhaile was trying to preserve. Unlike before, the beasts and creatures did not respond with panic or confusion. Everyone looked at Benjamin who was imagining another lava ball falling into all of these demons.

        With one quick motion, Aloysius Trenhaile pushed everyone away to the walls as a lava ball crashed into the room resulting in a fantastic explosion. Aloysius Trenhaile made a motion with his hands and froze the explosion as it occurred. Benjamin’s jaw dropped as he watched Aloysius take the explosion and throw it thousands of feet in the air. They were fighting, Benjamin thought.

Benjamin imagined destroying the walls on all sides of the room so that they stood on only a floor on top of the tower. Aloysius responded by creating a large crack in the ground that splintered through Benjamin’s feet. Benjamin jumped to the side and watched a chunk of the tower fall to the ground. He picked up some of the boulders and threw them one after another at Aloysius. Aloysius collected them in midair and then threw them back at Benjamin who ducked to the ground to avoid them. This was not going to be as easy as Benjamin thought. Aloysius could imagine things as well as Benjamin could.
