        And then, Aloysius did something that Benjamin did not expect. He transformed into a gigantic bull. Benjamin started to build a wall in front of him as quickly as he could. Aloysius breathed fire out of his snout and then proceeded to run forward. Benjamin built and built and built until the wall was twenty feet high and twenty feet thick. And still, Aloysius charged through it like it was a stack of cards. Benjamin fell to the ground and slid to the edge of the floor. He held on tightly so as not to fall off the tower.

        He imagined a lightning bolt shattering the sky and hitting Aloysius square in the back. The bull squealed in pain and Aloysius transformed back into a human body. The evil man gathered a fire and set the entire floor ablaze. Benjamin responded by freezing everything around him and then freezing the entire top half of the tower. Aloysius roared in response and then transformed into a cyclops a dozen times larger than Benjamin. He grabbed a section of the building and slammed it over Benjamin. But Benjamin imagined himself in a solid sphere and the tower broke all around him. Aloysius charged and then created a sound wave with his hands that blew Benjamin off the tower.

        Benjamin was in freefall and could feel that he was losing control. He spun every which direction and did not know how much further he had until he hit the ground. But then he imagined that like that day in the academy, he could fly. And so Benjamin returned to the top of the tower flying and imagined a tornado headed directly for Aloysius. Aloysius responded with a hail storm that absorbed the tornado and tried to suck Benjamin inside it.

        Aloysius transformed into a dragon and began chasing Benjamin in the air while sending fireballs in his direction. Benjamin dodged each one and flew throughout the castle, trying to get away from the beast. He circled the tower over and over but Aloysius kept on his tail the entire way. Aloysius snapped at Benjamin with his teeth whenever he neared but Benjamin continued to avoid the monster. He imagined that Aloysius was stuck in an iron cage and when that cage appeared around the flying dragon, Aloysius fell to the ground with a thud loud enough to create another lava river running through the castle.

        Benjamin looked down and thought that he did it. He had defeated Aloysius Trenhaile. The monster had fallen to its own demise. Benjamin quickly flew to the top of the tower to find King Bernard Zwirn. He was a little shaken but he was fine. Benjamin opened the cage and let him free.

        “Thank you, Benjamin,” he said.

        “Are you OK?” Benjamin asked.

        “Well,” the king said slowly. “I don’t suppose anyone could say they felt OK after having survived what you and my brother just created. But, I’m fine. We have to leave, Benjamin.”

        They turned to go and then Benjamin saw a sight that was familiar to him from long ago. When he was with his friends, the dinosaurs, trying to stop Professor Undutois from destroying the planet, there was a terrifying monster. It was a monster so feared that the dinosaurs ran from it. A monster that ruined his dreams and turned them into nightmares. And at that moment, Benjamin saw that same monster jump up the side of the tower and land at the very top.

        The tower couldn’t take the weight of this enormous beast. It swayed from side to side as another chunk of the tower fell to the ground. A crack rippled through the ground to the top floor. The monster looked at Benjamin and let out a roar so loud it could be heard throughout the entire land Benjamin had travelled. Benjamin couldn’t hear. The noise was so deafening. And the resulting ringing in his ears made him dizzy. He looked around and saw that King Bernard Zwirn was holding his ears and laying on the ground. He was alive but like Benjamin in a lot of danger. The monster roared again and then snapped at Benjamin.

        It wants to cut off my head, Benjamin thought.

        As he thought about the last person who wanted to cut off his head, he thought he knew how to destroy this monster. But to do so, he would have to dream of something so massive that the beast couldn’t stand a chance. And so, he transformed into a humongous white dragon.

        Benjamin knew what he was going to do next. He flew into the air and Aloysius gave chase. They flew around the castle several times as Aloysius continued to try to grab and thrash at the white dragon.

        Having been on a basket flown by a bird, he knew that one way to get the bird to fall to the ground was to hit it on the side.

        “Throw something at him!” Benjamin yelled to King Bernard Zwirn as he flew by the top of the tower.

        Benjamin led the monster around the top of the tower several times until he saw King Bernard Zwirn had a ball of fire ready to throw at it. When the king released it, the fire struck the beast in the side. And that alone was not enough to stop it. But, it reacted with confusion and pain. It shook the fire off its body but while it was doing so, Benjamin flew as fast as he could at the monster’s eyes.

        He needed to prevent the beast from being able to see.

        And then, he remembered the coal.

        He took as much coal as he could and thrust it at the monster’s eyes. The beast screamed in pain and in the middle of the sky, it transformed back into Aloysius Trenhaile. Benjamin thought about letting Aloysius fall to the ground but seeing that he was unconscious, he grabbed him before he fell.

This was it.

At the top of the tower, King Bernard Zwirn restrained his brother who at that point was weakened and could no longer fight back.

        The tower started to crumble. Benjamin took the king and Aloysius and flew them to where Selma stood outside the castle. As he flew over the wall, the tower completely collapsed and buried all of the monsters and nightmares that were living below. There was nothing left but walls that surrounded a gigantic mound of dust and lava.

        “Hey, you’re alive,” Selma said rather cooly.

        “Yes, I survived,” Benjamin said as he lay on the grass, exhausted by it all.

        “Not to say I didn’t think you could do it, but I’m a little impressed.”

        “A little?”

        “Well, you’re alive. I actually am quite impressed with that.”

        “Thanks, I guess.”

        “But did you really have to bring him back with you?” Selma asked as she pointed to the still unconscious Aloysius Trenhaile.

        “We’re taking him back with us,” King Bernard Zwirn said. “He won’t be producing nightmares any longer.”

        Benjamin reached inside his pocket and felt for a key. It was still there. Despite all of the flying and falling and fire and ice and lightning and earthquakes, he still managed to have the key. He could finally leave. And, he could finally leave knowing that Selma was happier with how he was leaving.

        “How did you and your brother grow so far apart?” Benjamin asked. “You make dreams and he makes nightmares.”

        “He didn’t always make nightmares,” King Bernard Zwirn said as they prepared themselves for the journey back to Castle Ehtahl. “No one wants to be evil. Something happens that makes good people do evil things. My brother originally made dreams. He made some of the most beautiful, inspiring dreams you could ever imagine for people. But one day, everything changed for him. He wanted something he couldn’t have. And when he realized he couldn’t have it, he started getting angry.”

        “What did he want?” Selma asked.

        “He wanted to always live in a dream. It’s one thing to have dreams and be a dreamer. But, we can’t live in our dreams. We have to accept that reality is separate from them. He couldn’t understand it and he believed that there were people who lived in dreams. And since he was unable to live this way, he decided that no one else should either. That’s when he joined the castles that produce nightmares.”

        “What are you going to do with him now?” Benjamin asked. “His castle’s destroyed. He can’t produce nightmares there anymore.”

        “He can’t but he could go somewhere else, if he wants. If I know my brother, he’s as stubborn as I am. And so, I’d like to keep him in Castle Ehtahl for a while. I think if there’s anyone who can convince him to change his ways, it’ll be me. I can’t send him back out into this land. The land will either kill him or he’ll hurt others.”

        Benjamin respected King Bernard Zwirn for not giving up on his brother. He thought it was commendable that he was going to try to change him to be good. At home, he didn’t think most people behaved the same way.

        “So now there’s no more nightmares,” Benjamin said.

        “Well,” Selma started. “There’s no more nightmares from Aloysius Trenhaile.”

        “It’s impossible to get rid of all the nightmares, Benjamin,” King Bernard Zwirn said as the sun started to rise in the distance. “So long as there are dreamers, there are going to be people who want to destroy dreams. The victory today is that there will be more dreams than nightmares. And for your New York, that means there will be dreams again.”

        Benjamin watched the sun rise and felt that he was fine with this situation. He could dream again.

        “Let’s go home,” King Bernard Zwirn said. “I’m exhausted.”

Chapter 31: In Which There Is A Guard

        

        When they returned to Castle Ehtahl’s walls, Benjamin felt relief knowing that he had finally made it back. Selma and he were exhausted. Aloysius Trenhaile was still unconscious. But, King Bernard Zwirn seemed as energetic as possible.

        “Before we go inside,” Benjamin said. “You should probably know that Thalia Nachamie is in charge and he isn’t really fond of me.”

        “Don’t worry, Benjamin,” the king said. “I will clear up everything in the castle.”

        “Oh, that’s great,” Benjamin said as the king was about to pound on the wall. “Also, I was wondering if you could clear everything up at Castle Ehtsetra.”

        The king froze and looked at Selma.

        “What happened at Castle Ehtsetra?”

        “Nothing really but the queen there doesn’t appear to like us either,” Selma said. “She wanted to cut Benjamin’s head off.”

        The king let out a loud sigh.

        “OK, I’ll clear that up as well,” he said.

        Before he could pound on the door for the second time, Benjamin interrupted him again.

        “Oh also,” Benjamin said. “You should probably talk to Myrna Delacourte.”

        The king looked at Selma and Benjamin.

        “Where have you two been over the past week?” he asked with disbelief.

        “We’ve been to a lot of places. I’ve met a lot of people,” Benjamin said.

        “I’ll clear it all up. You don’t have to worry about a thing.”

Bernard Zwirn pounded on the castle wall as loudly as he could.

        “Who is it?” Noel Jaffin asked on the other end.

        “Noel, this is King Zwirn. Let me in.”

        “Ah, I’ve been hearing that all week. Try something else, Dave.”

        “What? Noel, this is King Zwirn. Let me in this instant.”

        “Oh, right. And, I’m five feet tall and cleanly shaven.”

        Benjamin stepped forward and pounded on the door.

        “Noel, let us in!” Benjamin yelled as loudly as he could.

        There was a pause on the other end. Benjamin could hear feet shuffling around and then a ladder being rested against the door.

        “Benjamin? Is that you?” Noel Jaffin whispered quickly.

        “Oh, so you recognize Benjamin’s voice but you don’t recognize mine,” Bernard Zwirn said as he rolled his eyes.

        “Sorry about that, King Zwirn,” Noel Jaffin said as the doors to the castle began to open. “We’ve been getting so many visitors who claim to be you. Some of them sounded nearly identical to you.”

        “None of them did,” Cole said.

        “Well, not exactly but they were certainly very close to how King Zwirn speaks,” Noel Jaffin defended himself.

        “None of them were close,” Joel said with a long sigh.

        “I didn’t say exactly but I’m saying that they could have been mistaken for King Zwirn.”

        “Noel, you need to get your ears checked,” King Zwirn said as he reentered his castle.

Benjamin followed behind and was happy to be in a place that was more hospitable than some of the other places he had been. Selma walked at his side. He knew that she wanted to smile but that she was holding herself back.

        Noel left Cole and Joel to close the door and stumbled his way to Bernard Zwirn’s side. He was breathless as he tried to speak to the king.

        “Where have you been?” Noel blurted.

        “I was kidnapped, Noel,” Bernard Zwirn said without looking at the sweaty guard. “But, now I’m back. And, I need to see Thalia Nachamie immediately.”

        Noel stopped working and looked to the ground.

        “Why of course,” Noel said. “I’ll go find him. But, what are we going to do with Benjamin?”

        Bernard Zwirn stopped walking and turned his head slightly to the side.

        “What do you mean what are we going to do with Benjamin?”

        Benjamin saw that Noel was trying to keep the conversation private between the king and himself. Noel moved closer to Bernard Zwirn and stood on his toes so as to speak closer to the king’s ear. Bernard Zwirn didn’t move so Noel tried to speak as quietly as possible, while watching Benjamin in the corner of his eye.

        “He’s a convicted villain,” Noel whispered.

        “A convicted villain?” Bernard Zwirn blurted.

        “Sh! He’s right there,” Noel whispered back in a panic.

        “What has he been convicted of?”

        “Stealing.”

        “What has he stolen?”

        “He stole the missing piece of the dream machine.”

        “So, the dream machine now works?”

        “Well, it could. It doesn’t, though. After Benjamin left, Thalia Nachamie told us that since it had not been used in such a long period of time, it was impossible to figure out where the missing piece actually went.”

        “And Thalia Nachamie is the one who convicted Benjamin of stealing?”

        “Yes, of course.”

        “But, he didn’t steal it.”

        “Well,” Noel said slowly as he looked away shyly from Benjamin. “If you say so.”

        “Noel, did anyone see Benjamin steal anything?”

        “No.”

        “And don’t you think it is odd that Thalia Nachamie didn’t fix the machine? He kicked Benjamin from the castle and then did nothing with the missing piece.”

        “Well, that’s not exactly true.”

        “What isn’t true?”

        “You see,” Noel started to speak more slowly.

        “I kicked Benjamin out of the castle,” Pritchett Pollock said from behind Bernard Zwirn. “We had to find you. And so, I sent Benjamin to find you by having him be kicked out of the castle.”

        “You sent a child to find me?”

        “He’s not just any child. He’s got a larger imagination than any person I’ve ever met. His creativity is beyond my understanding.”

        “If you wanted me to find King Bernard Zwirn,” Benjamin said. “Why didn’t you just let me go outside like I wanted all along?”

        “Because you would have wanted to come back,” Miss Lindenmeyer said. “And, we would have had to let you come back. We couldn’t think of another way to find King Bernard Zwirn but for some reason, we all agreed that if anyone could find him, you could find him.”

        Benjamin was flabbergasted. He could not believe that this had been arranged. The sun beat steadily upon his face as his heart beat twice as fast.

        “But, I could have been killed out there. I had no idea where I was going and I had no idea what I was doing. What if I had gotten myself killed?”

        “You wouldn’t have,” Selma said.

        “Why not?”

”As long as you were able to destroy your fears, you were going to be fine,” Miss Lindenmeyer said.

        “And he did find me,” Bernard Zwirn said.

        “And he was the only one who could possibly find you,” Pritchett Pollock said.

        “It was in your favor, Benjamin,” Miss Lindenmeyer said. “Because, we couldn’t send you home without King Zwirn’s assistance. He’s the only one that can let you leave. You would have been stuck here forever unless you found him. There isn’t a door outside the castle that takes you back to New York. There isn’t a door here, either. The door opened when you defeated your nightmare.”

        Benjamin realized at that moment that everything that he had gone through had been a result of his desire to leave. He helped others as he tried to help himself. And in the process, he saw that he was cared for and loved by friends he had known for only a short time.

        “So, I can now go home?” Benjamin asked.

        “Yep,” Bernard Zwirn said as he knelt down to the young boy. “You’ve done an amazing thing, Benjamin. No one else would have been able to do what you’ve done. You’ve given us the chance to dream again.”

        “But,” Benjamin started to say as he glanced at Selma. “I don’t really want to leave anymore.”

        “You don’t want to leave?” Selma yelled.

        “Well--”

        “You don’t want to leave! You realize everything we did was to give you a chance to leave! And now, you don’t want to leave?” Selma screamed.

        Bernard Zwirn physically restrained the young girl from tackling Benjamin.

        “It’s just that,” Benjamin said shyly. “I like it here. I want to see my parents. But, I like it here. I like you all.”

        “Oh, great,” Selma said sarcastically. “He likes us now.”

        “I do! I do like you. You are my friends.”

        “Benjamin,” King Zwirn said. “You need to go back and take care of your parents. And, you need to take care of your brother. If we are going to continue to make dreams, we need people to dream.”

        Benjamin looked at the ground and wondered how he could go back to New York now. He had been through so much that had made him happier and braver than he was before. But when he thought of his parents, he knew that the decision was not a difficult one. He had to go back.

        “I’m going to find Russell Fox,” Bernard Zwirn said. “When you are ready to leave, let me know Benjamin.”

        “We’re going as well,” Miss Lindenmeyer said, referring to Pritchett Pollock. “We will see you soon. You can come back whenever you want.”

        “Bye, Benjamin,” Pritchett Pollock said. “Please try to keep your dreams a little less creative. You’re stretching my budget.”

        Benjamin watched them leave and wondered when he would see them again. He wondered when he would see the production studios. And then, he wondered if he would ever see Snark again. Rodney! He never met Rodney Cohen and still did not know anything about him.

         “OK,” Benjamin said reluctantly. “I’ll go back.”

        “Just like that?” Selma said quietly. “You’re not going to even fight to stay?”

        He wasn’t sure if he saw water well in her eyes or if she was squinting her face in anger, but in either case Selma looked hurt.

        “But, you just told me--”

        “I know what I told you,” she said. “I guess I expected that you’d spend a little over five minutes thinking about staying. But, you’re ready to go.”

        “Well, my parents--”

        “Yes,” Selma said. “You should go.”

        “But Selma--”

        “Go!”

        “Selma!”

        “Go!”

        Benjamin grabbed her and hugged her as hard as he could. He was hugging her so hard that he worried he had squeezed all of the air from her little body. He released her a little bit but when he felt Selma hug him back, he squeezed her again.

        “I’ll miss you,” she said quietly.

        “I’ll miss you, too,” he said.

        “And if you tell anyone I said that I’ll kill you!” she yelled as she ran away.

Chapter 32: In Which There Is A Dinosaur

        Mrs. Buckingham drove over a hundred miles an hour through the neighborhood, careful not to run into any pigeons and squirrels walking across the street. Her eyes were focused on the road like a racecar driver searching for a finish line. The news reporter on the radio was going on and on about the same story.

        “In a report issued last night, people everywhere are dreaming again,” the reporter said. “The dreams are back and people are more confident than ever. For more on this story, we’re turning to field reporter Rebecca--”

        “I don’t understand why every morning has to be like this,” she said to Benjamin who sat silently in the passenger seat. Benjamin bounced the back of his head against his seat.

        “I didn’t hear my alarm,” Benjamin said quickly.

        “You say that every morning,” Mrs. Buckingham said as she swerved around a group of squirrels fighting over a nut. “And every morning I have to race through the neighborhood giving all the little critters along the way heart attacks.”

        “I can be late.”

        “You cannot be late.”

        “Sure, Billy comes in late almost every day.”

        “You aren’t Billy. You missed too much class already what with your having disappeared for so long.”

        Benjamin heard a pigeon scream as it narrowly missed being struck by their little car.

        “I’ll make it up. No big deal.”

        “No big deal? Benjamin, we still have to talk about where you were. This is a big deal.”

        Mrs. Buckingham slammed on the brakes and stopped at a red light. Benjamin flew forward and nearly hit his head on the dashboard.

        “It’s not like we learn anything at school anyways,” Benjamin said matter of factly.

        Mrs. Buckingham stared at him with accusing eyes for about a minute. Benjamin didn’t know why she didn’t agree. He learned more in the past month than he had in all of his days in Mr. Marchetta’s classroom.

        “Benjamin, I love you but sometimes you say the most ridiculous things. When you get home tonight, you have to tell me where you were for the past month,” his mother said as she accelerated the car faster and faster through New York.

        Benjamin wondered how much easier it would have been to get to Aloysius Trenhaile’s Castle if he had a car. He assumed, of course, that he knew how to drive. But based on how his mother was currently driving, he decided it could not be that difficult. He then wondered how much sooner he would have gotten home had he had roads to follow like the roads throughout his neighborhood. And then, he wondered how much further he could have travelled each day if there were lights scattered throughout to illuminate his path. There were things everywhere along this race to school that made Benjamin wonder whether he could have endured less in his voyage.

        And at that moment when a squirrel jumped over the car to avoid Mrs. Buckingham’s dash to the finish line, he knew that it would all be different. If he had things that could have made his journey easier, he would not have evolved from the boy who was scared of everything into the boy who was scared of a lot less.

        “Bye, mom,” Benjamin said as he exited the car in front of the school as she waved goodbye and blew him a kiss.

        The school looked the same. Nothing had changed. It had a boring exterior. The grass was barely alive. Kids trampled over each other to get through the door before the bell rang. It was exactly as it was. There was nothing different.

        And, Benjamin loved that.

        Because for the first time in his life, he knew that he was different.

        And that meant that possibly, just possibly, he was not below average.

        He sat in Mr. Marchetta’s classroom as the teacher lectured over and over again about forests.

        “Forests have lots of animals in them. There are deer, birds, raccoons, all sorts of animals. The only animal you don’t find in a forest is people. We don’t live in forests. We live in cities. Forests don’t have toilets or grocery stores or movie theaters. You think it’s funny but if you ever decide to spend some time in a forest, you’ll learn it’s not an enjoyable place. You’re going to want to leave. Forests are the worst. They are scary and ruthless and dangerous. There’s nothing fun about a forest. But if you find yourself in a forest, make sure to mark trees with a rock as you walk. That way, you’ll know how to exit. You just search for the trees that you marked. And then, you’ll be on your way out unless...”

        Benjamin stared out the window and watched a large billowing cloud takes its time moving along the blue canvas of the sky toward the golden sun resting above the buildings across the street. He saw Mr. Marchetta’s fancy car parked outside the school. It was blue and looked like it would move much faster than his mother’s car. He didn’t like it. Part of the reason he didn’t like it was because it was owned by Mr. Marchetta. But, the other part that he didn’t like was that it looked out of place. He wanted to see a tree or a bush or a river or a volcano instead.

        And then suddenly, Benjamin saw Snark appear from seemingly out of nowhere. Benjamin’s heart raced and his eyes widened as he stretched his neck to see what Snark was going to do.

        The ground vibrated with each step Snark took, pounding the pavement and rattling the windows. Snark paused and turned his gigantic head. Benjamin knew Snark was looking directly at him. Snark’s mouth opened slightly to reveal his teeth and Benjamin saw him pant lightly like a dog when it’s happy.

Benjamin grinned as well.

Snark lifted his left leg high into the air and then slammed it down into Mr. Marchetta’s car. It made the same sound as when Benjamin stepped on an empty soda can. And since Benjamin liked that sound so much, it was impossible for him to not stop laughing.

        Snark left as quickly as he arrived but not without waving to Benjamin beforehand.

        “Benjamin!” Mr. Marchetta yelled.

        Benjamin covered his mouth and then turned to his teacher.

        “I asked you a question! Why weren’t you paying attention?” Mr. Marchetta asked with a stern, angry look.

        “Because he still doesn’t know where he is,” Howard Horne snickered from the back. “Benjamin’s lost in the forest.”

        The class, Howard Horne’s audience, giggled in response. Mr. Marchetta started to laugh as well. Benjamin looked around and saw that he was the joke of everyone around him.

        But unlike weeks ago when Benjamin was bullied and felt like there was nothing outside of that classroom for him, he knew that there was a big world ready to welcome him.

He didn’t need the bullies.

He had his friends.

And so, he smiled.
